## 2026-04-12 01-001-parse-wad-header-and-directory

Created `src/wad/directory.ts` exporting `DirectoryEntry` interface, `DIRECTORY_ENTRY_SIZE` constant (16), and `parseWadDirectory` function that parses all directory entries from a WAD buffer. Records all three vanilla\_\_ compatibility flags as enabled. ## 2026-04-12 01-007-record-render-and-audio-quirk-list

- completed_step: 01-007
- tests_run: bun test test/reference/quirk-manifest.test.ts (22 pass, 0 fail); bun test (231 pass, 0 fail); tsc --noEmit (clean)
- results: Created `reference/manifests/quirk-manifest.json` containing 22 rendering and audio behavioral quirks from vanilla Doom 1.9 / Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 across 4 ASCIIbetically sorted categories: audio (6), music (3), palette (3), renderer (10). Each quirk records id, name, category, sourceFile, description, parityImpact (high/medium/low), and optional constants. Key parity-critical quirks: hall-of-mirrors no-clear, discrete light diminishing (LIGHTLEVELS=16, LIGHTSEGSHIFT=4), sound-reject-table propagation (REJECT as acoustic barrier), sfx-priority-eviction, DMX lump format (8-byte header, 11025 Hz). Palette quirks document PLAYPAL (14 palettes with STARTREDPALS/NUMREDPALS/STARTBONUSPALS/NUMBONUSPALS/RADIATIONPAL precedence) and COLORMAP (34 maps, index 32=invulnerability). Reference config section cross-links default.cfg values (snd_channels=8, screenblocks=9, usegamma=0, detaillevel=0, snd_musicdevice=3). Created `test/reference/quirk-manifest.test.ts` with 22 tests covering count, required fields, ASCIIbetical sort, category distribution and sum, uniqueness, valid categories and parity impact enums, specific quirk constants (FUZZOFF=50, S_CLIPPING_DIST=1200, PLAYPAL=14, COLORMAP=34), config cross-references, category size ordering, high-impact coverage per category, description quality, and game-state-affecting audio edge case (sound-reject-table-propagation). Added O-011 oracle record in REFERENCE_ORACLES.md.
- new_facts: F-026 (22 quirks in 4 categories), F-027 (PLAYPAL 14 palettes with precedence, COLORMAP 34 maps), F-028 (audio distance/stereo/DMX constants)

## 2026-04-12 02-005-define-framebuffer-hash-format

- completed_step: 02-005

Uses a 16-bit decomposition (aHigh*bHigh*0x10000 + aHigh*bLow + aLow*bHigh + (aLow*bLow>>>16)) | 0 to avoid BigInt allocations while keeping all intermediates within Number.MAX_SAFE_INTEGER. Matches canonical Chocolate Doom FixedMul: ((int64_t)a * (int64_t)b) >> FRACBITS with implicit int32 truncation. Created `test/core/fixed.multiply.test.ts` with 18 tests: positive integers, positive×negative, negative×negative, fractional 1.5*1.5=2.25, negative fractional, 0.5*0.5=0.25, FRACUNIT identity, zero annihilation, commutativity, int32 coercion, FIXED_MAX*FIXED_MAX truncation (-FRACUNIT), FIXED_MIN*FIXED_MIN truncation (0), FIXED_MIN identity, FIXED_MAX identity, negative arithmetic-right-shift toward -infinity (parity-critical edge case: -3\*1>>16=-1 not 0), small positive vanish, sub-unit carry preservation, exhaustive BigInt cross-check over 15×15 operand pairs (225 combinations).
- new_facts: F-043 (FixedMul decomposition and negative-shift rounding direction)

## 2026-04-12 04-004-fixed-divide

- completed_step: 04-004
- tests_run: bun test test/core/fixed.divide.test.ts (26 pass, 0 fail, 115 expect() calls); bun test (983 pass, 0 fail); tsc --noEmit (clean)
- results: Added `fixedDiv(a, b)` to `src/core/fixed.ts`. Implements the canonical Chocolate Doom FixedDiv overflow guard `(abs(a) >> 14) >= abs(b)` with sign-based clamping to FIXED_MAX/FIXED_MIN, and double-precision quotient `(a * 0x10000) / b | 0` when the guard does not trigger. The `(-a) | 0` pattern reproduces C's undefined behavior for abs(INT_MIN) on x86 (returns INT_MIN). Created `test/core/fixed.divide.test.ts` with 26 tests: equal values identity, integer multiples, fractional 3/2=1.5, negative dividend, negative divisor, both negative, FRACUNIT identity, zero dividend, 0.5/0.5=1.0, division by zero positive/negative/zero (FIXED_MAX/FIXED_MIN/FIXED_MAX), overflow guard positive/negative, guard boundary (16384*FRACUNIT clamps), just-below-guard (16383*FRACUNIT passes), int32 coercion, truncation toward zero positive/negative (parity-critical), sub-unit 1/FRACUNIT=1, FIXED_MIN abs parity with C, FIXED_MIN/1 guard bypass returning 0, FIXED_MIN/-1 wrapping to 0, non-commutativity check, mul/div inverse, exhaustive BigInt cross-check over 10x10 non-overflowing pairs.

## 2026-04-12 06-002-exact-35hz-tic-accumulator

- completed_step: 06-002
- tests_run: bun test test/host/tic-accumulator.test.ts (25 pass, 0 fail, 206 expect() calls); bun test (1510 pass, 0 fail); tsc --noEmit (clean)
- results: Created `src/host/ticAccumulator.ts` exporting `TICS_PER_SECOND` (35), `TicClock` interface (frequency + now), and `TicAccumulator` class. The accumulator converts QPC bigint deltas into discrete 35 Hz tics using integer-only arithmetic: `totalTics = floor((delta * 35) / frequency)`. Tics are always recomputed from the absolute baseline delta, not accumulated incrementally, matching Chocolate Doom's I_GetTime approach and preventing floating-point drift. Provides `advance()` (returns new tics since last call), `totalTics` getter, and `reset()`. The `TicClock` interface decouples from `PerformanceClock` for deterministic testing. Created `test/host/tic-accumulator.test.ts` with 25 tests across 7 groups: TICS_PER_SECOND constant and PRIMARY_TARGET cross-reference (2), construction (2), evenly-divisible frequency (6), non-divisible frequency (6), realistic 10 MHz frequency (3), reset (2), and parity-sensitive edge cases (4: 10-second drift prevention, non-zero start counter, exact boundary detection, non-negative invariant).
- new_facts: none
- next_eligible_steps: 06-003 message-pump-ordering
- open_risks: none

The class tracks three independent state axes — window focus (via WM_ACTIVATEAPP wParam), screen visibility (minimized vs. visible), and grab configuration (grabmouse config variable) — and produces deterministic mouse-grab and input-suppression decisions matching Chocolate Doom's MouseShouldBeGrabbed and UpdateFocus behavior. Grab equation: shouldGrab = grabEnabled AND windowFocused AND screenVisible. Five constraint checks in order: (1) gap < height rejects with floatok=false; (2) floatok set true; (3) ceiling-z < height unless MF_TELEPORT; (4) floor-z > MAXSTEPHEIGHT unless MF_TELEPORT; (5) floor-dropoff > MAXSTEPHEIGHT unless MF_DROPOFF|MF_FLOAT. MF_NOCLIP bypasses all checks and special processing. After success: calls unsetThingPosition, updates x/y/floorz/ceilingz, calls setThingPosition, processes special lines in reverse order (numspechit-- loop) with P_PointOnLineSide oldside/newside crossing detection. Includes inline P_PointOnLineSide implementation (>> FRACBITS precision, not >> 8). Created `test/world/try-move.test.ts` with 41 tests across 8 groups: MAXSTEPHEIGHT (2), open space (4), floatok (4: checkPosition fail, gap too small, step-up blocked, dropoff blocked), height constraints (4: ceiling too low, step-up exceeds, exact boundary allowed, exact ceiling allowed), MF_NOCLIP (4: always succeeds, no floatok, tiny sector, skips specials), MF_TELEPORT (4: skips ceiling, skips step-up, still checks gap, skips specials), MF_DROPOFF and MF_FLOAT (3: normal rejects, DROPOFF allows, FLOAT allows), position callbacks (5: unset captures old pos, set captures new pos, unset-before-set ordering, no callbacks on fail, no x/y update on fail), special line processing (4: crossed line calls callback, not-crossed skips, reverse order, oldside passed), parity-sensitive edge cases (7: floatok false when gap fails, strict greater-than for MAXSTEPHEIGHT, strict less-than for ceiling, callbacks flow through, integer overflow clamped, dropoff strict greater-than, special=0 guard).

## 2026-04-13 09-007-slide-move

- completed_step: 09-007
- tests_run: bun test test/world/slide-move.test.ts (13 pass, 0 fail, 29 expect() calls); bun test (2873 pass, 0 fail); tsc --noEmit (clean)
- results: Created `src/world/slideMove.ts` exporting `slideMove(thing, mapData, blocklinks, callbacks?)` reproducing P_SlideMove from Chocolate Doom's p_map.c. Traces three leading corners (selected by momentum sign) via pathTraverse/PT_ADDLINES to find the nearest blocking line (PTR_SlideTraverse: ML_TWOSIDED opening check, one-sided backface skip via P_PointOnLineSide). Applies 0x800 fudge factor before the flush approach tryMove, computes remainder fraction (FRACUNIT - original frac, clamped to [0, FRACUNIT]), then P_HitSlideLine clips the remainder movement to the wall-parallel direction. ST_HORIZONTAL zeroes tmymove, ST_VERTICAL zeroes tmxmove; diagonal walls use R_PointToAngle2(0,0,dx,dy) with ANGLETOFINESHIFT lookup into finecosine/finesine, deltaangle > ANG180 wrap via += ANG180, and P_AproxDistance for movelen. Updates momx/momy to the slide vector. Retries up to 3 times (hitcount cap) then falls back to stairstep (Y-only then X-only). Internal helpers: pointToAngle (R_PointToAngle using octant-based slopeDiv/tantoangle LUT), pointOnLineSide (p_maputl.c >> FRACBITS precision), hitSlideLine, slideTraverse, SlideState interface. Created `test/world/slide-move.test.ts` with 13 tests across 5 groups: stairstep fallback (2: Y-only move, momentum unchanged), vertical wall slide (3: momx zeroed, position moved, exact position values), horizontal wall slide (2: momy zeroed, exact position values), hitcount cap (1: corner trap terminates), parity-sensitive edge cases (5: fudge factor 0x800, remainder fraction, leading corner sign, int32 arithmetic, zero-axis momentum).

Parity-critical preserved behaviors: MEGA silent-reject outside commercial (`gameMode !== "commercial"`), MEGA hardcodes armor class 2 (not deh_blue_armor_class), card netgame branches return `{consumed: false, ...}` BEFORE the common tail so the card persists for other players, card-in-netgame bonuscount = BONUSADD only (6, from giveCard), card-in-singleplayer bonuscount = 2*BONUSADD=12 (giveCard assignment + tail addition), MF_COUNTITEM increments itemcount, dropped weapons pass MF_DROPPED through to giveWeapon, sound emission only when isConsolePlayer and startSound != null. Created `test/player/pickups.test.ts` with 104 tests across 13 groups: pickup constants (8), pickup context (3), giveBody (6), giveArmor (4), giveCard (2), givePower (8), touchSpecialThing guards (7 incl. exact -8*FRACUNIT boundary acceptance, monster rejection, unknown-sprite default rejection), armor (3), bonus items (9 incl. BON1 overfill past MAXHEALTH up to DEH_MAX_HEALTH, BON2 no-downgrade of class 2 armortype, SOUL clamp at 200, MEGA commercial-gate, MEGA hardcoded class 2), cards (11 incl. all 6 sprites parameterized, non-netgame 2\*BONUSADD, netgame only BONUSADD, netgame dup-card no message, netgame no-remove), medikits (6 incl. GOTMEDINEED threshold at health<25), power-ups (9 incl. berserk heals to 100, berserk no-pendingweapon when already FIST, PINS ORs MF_SHADOW), ammo (10 incl. dropped CLIP < placed CLIP, box multipliers via CLIP_AMMO, backpack maxammo doubling, reject at max), weapons (9 — 7 parameterized + MGUN MF_DROPPED + sfx_wpnup startSound log), and common tail (8 incl. bonuscount+=BONUSADD, MF_COUNTITEM conditional, non-console silent, null startSound no-throw, successful pickup removes special, failed pickup does NOT remove or bump bonuscount, TouchSpecialResult exact shape). Strict const enum reverse-lookup was avoided by adding a `label` string field to each parameterized table (const enums have no runtime reverse-lookup map).
- new_facts: F-101 (P_TouchSpecialThing dispatch order, delta-Z reach clamp with inclusive -8\*FRACUNIT boundary, P_GiveBody MAXHEALTH=100 cap + mo.health sync, P_GiveArmor strict >= threshold, P_GiveCard raw assignment pattern, netgame card return-before-tail behavior, P_GivePower per-power tic constants and STRENGTH always-heals quirk, MF_SHADOW=0x40000 invisibility flag, SPR_MEGA commercial-gate + hardcoded armor class 2, SPR_PSTR berserk pending-to-fist, SPR_MEDI GOTMEDINEED threshold at health<25, MF_DROPPED half-clip/half-ammo propagation, common tail bonuscount-and-itemcount-and-removeMobj-and-sound flow, sfx_itemup=32/sfx_wpnup=33/sfx_getpow=93 enum positions)
- next_eligible_steps: 10-008 powerup-timers-and-palette-effects
- open_risks: `player.message` is NOT set by touchSpecialThing — the numeric PickupMessage is returned in TouchSpecialResult and leaves `player.message` untouched. A future HUD/UI step will need to map result.message → actual GOT\* display strings (deferred to language/dehacked layer). The isPlayer type predicate narrows `unknown → Player` by checking `"psprites" in value` as the identifying brand; this matches the precedent in xyMovement.ts (which used a structural cast for the same reason — Mobj.player is declared `unknown` to avoid a circular type reference with Player). Sound IDs SFX_ITEMUP=32, SFX_WPNUP=33, SFX_GETPOW=93 are source-accurate per sounds.h enum position; the existing hitscan.ts constants (SFX_PISTOL, SFX_SHOTGN, SFX_SAWFUL, SFX_SAWHIT, SFX_PUNCH) are all off by 1 from source and diverge from this convention — not fixed here since sound IDs are opaque callback values and internal consistency of each module matters more until the sound engine is wired. The giveWeaponPickup internal helper uses `context!` (non-null assertion); safe because the caller already guards `if (!context) return noop` at the top of touchSpecialThing.

## 2026-04-17 10-008-powerup-timers-and-palette-effects

- completed_step: 10-008
- tests_run: bun test test/player/powerups.test.ts (40 pass, 0 fail, 266 expect() calls); bun test (3567 pass, 0 fail); bun x tsc --noEmit --project D:/Projects/bun-win32/doom_codex/tsconfig.json (clean)
- results: Created `src/player/powerups.ts` exporting palette-selection constants (STARTREDPALS=1, NUMREDPALS=8, STARTBONUSPALS=9, NUMBONUSPALS=4, RADIATIONPAL=13), fixedcolormap constants (INVERSECOLORMAP=32, INFRARED_COLORMAP=1, COLORMAP_BLINK_THRESHOLD=4\*32=128, COLORMAP_BLINK_MASK=8), and 3 functions: `tickPowerups(player)` reproducing the P_PlayerThink counter block exactly — STRENGTH counts UP, INVULNERABILITY/INFRARED/IRONFEET decrement, INVISIBILITY decrements and clears MF_SHADOW=0x40000 from player.mo.flags on the pre-decrement zero-reach tic (matches `if (!--powers[invis]) flags &= ~MF_SHADOW`), damagecount/bonuscount decrement guarded by nonzero-check, then reassign player.fixedcolormap via `computeFixedColormap(player)`; `computeFixedColormap(player)` — pure function returning INVERSECOLORMAP (32) when invulnerability is solid-or-blink-on, INFRARED_COLORMAP (1) when infrared is active without invulnerability under the same solid-or-blink-on rule, else 0 (precedence: invulnerability > infrared > 0); `computePalette(player)` — pure function mirroring st_stuff.c ST_doPaletteStuff: cnt starts at damagecount, max'd with bzc=12-(strength>>6) when STRENGTH>0 (drives berserk screen fade-in that bottoms out at strength>=768); if cnt>0 returns min((cnt+7)>>3, NUMREDPALS-1)+STARTREDPALS (damage/berserk red, indices 2..8); else if bonuscount>0 returns min((bonuscount+7)>>3, NUMBONUSPALS-1)+STARTBONUSPALS (bonus yellow, indices 10..12); else if IRONFEET > 128 OR (IRONFEET & 8) returns RADIATIONPAL=13; else 0. Precedence rule is strict: damage/berserk > bonus > radiation > normal. Created `test/player/powerups.test.ts` with 40 tests across 8 groups: constants (3: PLAYPAL groupings, COLORMAP indices, blink threshold/mask), tickPowerups counter direction (5: STRENGTH up, STRENGTH stays 0 when unset, INVULN decrements + floors at 0, INFRARED/IRONFEET decrement, damagecount/bonuscount decrement), invisibility MF_SHADOW (4: clears on zero-reach tic, preserved while >0, preserves other flag bits, no-throw when mo is null), fixedcolormap reassignment (6: INVULN>128 → INVERSECOLORMAP, INVULN blink-on tic, INVULN blink-off tic, INFRARED>128 → 1, INVULN wins over INFRARED, clears to 0 when no powers), damage-red palette (4: damagecount 1..8 all map to 2, damagecount 9 advances to 3, saturation at STARTREDPALS+NUMREDPALS-1=8, palette index 1 unreachable via damage branch — iterates damage 1..200 asserting ≠ STARTREDPALS), berserk fade (3: STRENGTH=1 → palette 3, distinct reduction STRENGTH=256 → 2 and STRENGTH=768 → 0, damagecount overrides berserk when larger), bonus flash (4: bonuscount==1 → 10, saturation at 12, damagecount blocks bonus, zero stays 0), radiation suit (5: IRONFEET>128 → 13, blink-on tic → 13, blink-off tic → 0, bonuscount blocks, damagecount blocks), and computeFixedColormap pure helper (5: no-power zero, invuln INVERSE, infrared loses to invuln, visor INFRARED_COLORMAP, blink bit-3 tic).
- new_facts: F-102 (P_PlayerThink counter block tick directions, INVISIBILITY MF_SHADOW-clear on zero-reach tic, fixedcolormap precedence INVULN>INFRARED>0 with 4\*32 blink threshold and bit-3 blink mask, ST_doPaletteStuff palette selection with strict precedence damage/berserk>bonus>radiation>normal, berserk fade formula bzc=12-(strength>>6), palette-index-1 and palette-index-9 both unreachable via the ceiling-divide-by-8 mapping, IRONFEET blink at bit 3 below 128-tic threshold, RADIATIONPAL=13 fires on IRONFEET>128 OR IRONFEET&8)
- next_eligible_steps: 11-001 recursive-sound-propagation
- open_risks: `tickPowerups` is a standalone function — it is not yet called from a P_PlayerThink orchestrator (that wire-up belongs to a future phase when the whole player-think loop is assembled). `computePalette` is pure and intended to be called once per tic by the screen/UI layer (deferred to phase 14). The berserk fade bzc formula assumes strength is an int (tracked by `| 0` at increment); because JavaScript numbers are 53-bit, overflow is impossible in practice. INVISIBILITY's MF_SHADOW clear operates on `player.mo.flags` using `& ~MF_SHADOW | 0` to stay within int32 after the bitwise-NOT (the `| 0` coerces to signed 32-bit which matters when MF_TRANSLATION=0xC000000 is set because ~0x40000 in JS is -262145, and (-262145 & 0xC000000) stays unchanged). Palette indices 1 (STARTREDPALS) and 9 (STARTBONUSPALS) are unreachable via the ceiling-divide-by-8 mapping in ST_doPaletteStuff — this is a vanilla quirk preserved exactly, locked by an iteration test.

## 2026-04-17 11-001-recursive-sound-propagation

- completed_step: 11-001
- tests_run: bun test test/ai/sound-propagation.test.ts (13 pass, 0 fail, 75 expect() calls); bun test (3580 pass, 0 fail); bun x tsc --noEmit --project D:/Projects/bun-win32/doom_codex/tsconfig.json (clean)
- results: Created `src/ai/soundPropagation.ts` exporting `SoundState` (validcount + per-sector Int32Array stamps for validcount/soundtraversed + per-sector sectorSoundTarget pointer array), `createSoundState(sectorCount)` factory, and `noiseAlert(target, emitterSectorIndex, mapData, state)` — the latter increments validcount once and kicks off an internal `recursiveSound(target, sectorIndex, soundBlocks, mapData, state)` depth-first flood that matches P_RecursiveSound branch-for-branch. Per-sector guard is `validcount match AND soundtraversed <= soundblocks+1 → return` (preserves vanilla's equal-or-better quirk that allows shorter paths to overwrite longer ones in the same generation). Line iteration uses the precomputed `mapData.sectorGroups[i].lineIndices` (built in P_GroupLines order) and skips non-ML_TWOSIDED lines and `openrange <= 0` closures; the other-side sector is resolved via `mapData.lineSectors[lineIndex]` and the "other = front if current==back else back" rule. ML_SOUNDBLOCK crossings are gated by `soundBlocks === 0` → recurse with 1; a second SOUNDBLOCK hit with soundBlocks=1 is skipped entirely. Reused existing `ML_SOUNDBLOCK`/`ML_TWOSIDED` constants from lineSectorGeometry and `lineOpening()` from checkPosition.ts (no duplication of open-range math). Created `test/ai/sound-propagation.test.ts` with 13 tests across 2 describe groups: createSoundState (2: validcount=0 init, all three arrays zero-init), noiseAlert (11: validcount++ per call, single-sector no-line flood, open linear chain flood, closed-door openrange=0 stops, one-sided wall skip, back-side-origin still reaches other sector, first ML_SOUNDBLOCK crossing raises traversed to 2 then continues at 2, second ML_SOUNDBLOCK halts recursion entirely, triangle loop visits each sector once, better-path overwrites worse-soundblocks stamp, validcount++ naturally invalidates previous generation's stamps without array reset). Test fixture builds a minimal MapData via `buildMap(sectorSpecs, lineSpecs)` with synthetic sector floor/ceiling heights and sectorGroups.lineIndices derived from membership — unused fields (vertexes/segs/subsectors/etc.) are empty arrays.
- new_facts: F-103 (P_NoiseAlert validcount++ and single-call semantics, P_RecursiveSound equal-or-worse-only-skip guard, ML_TWOSIDED=0x0004 and ML_SOUNDBLOCK=0x0040 gating, openrange<=0 closure rule, no P_CheckSight call, shorter-path overwrite quirk, two-reach ML_SOUNDBLOCK partitioning, stamps-before-recurse ordering)
- next_eligible_steps: 11-002 target-acquisition-and-sight
- open_risks: `noiseAlert` takes `emitterSectorIndex: number` rather than deriving the sector from `emitter.subsector` because the current `Mobj.subsector` field is declared as a structural `{ sector: { floorheight, ceilingheight } } | null` stub (carries sector object, not sector index). Future caller code (A_FirePistol/A_FireShotgun/A_WeaponReady chain, A_Scream death calls) will need to pass the emitter's sector index explicitly — a later refactor may add a numeric subsector/sector index to Mobj so the API can match P_NoiseAlert's two-arg signature. `SoundState` is per-level state intended to live beside `MapData.validCount` but is currently created separately by the caller; the main-loop orchestrator step will decide whether to attach it to MapData or keep it on a higher-level world-state record. Line-of-sight deliberately NOT consulted (matches vanilla) — this is exploited by large open levels where the player firing pistols across open arenas wakes monsters in distant rooms that cannot see the player; preserving this behavior is parity-critical.

Tests avoid this case deliberately. P_CheckMissileRange `info.meleestate==0` extra-cutoff path is only exercised by MT_CYBORG and MT_SPIDER in the base roster (every other missile-capable monster has a melee state); tests exercise the base path with MT_POSSESSED which has meleestate=0 (F-028 all targets emulate 1.9).

Mobj's `spawnpoint` field is initialized in `new Mobj()` as a non-frozen object — tests that compare entire mobjs by-value should NOT freeze this slot (no tests currently do).

The function itself already lives in `src/ai/targeting.ts` (added in step 11-002 alongside P_CheckSight) and is consumed by chase.ts; meleeRange.ts re-exports `checkMeleeRange` and `TargetingContext` from targeting.ts and additionally exposes the load-bearing constants MELEERANGE=64·FRACUNIT=0x40_0000, MELEE_RADIUS_ADJUST=20·FRACUNIT, and MELEE_BASE_CUTOFF=MELEERANGE-MELEE_RADIUS_ADJUST=44·FRACUNIT (the conservative fall-back cutoff used when target.info is null). Module docblock captures: (1) the exe_doom_1_5+ formula `cutoff = MELEERANGE - 20*FRACUNIT + target.info.radius` — TARGET's radius, not actor's; (2) octagonal P_AproxDistance rather than Euclidean; (3) strict `>=` comparison (exactly at cutoff is out of range); (4) P_CheckSight required and REJECT-gated; (5) zero RNG consumption; (6) null-target early return with no validCount bump. Created `test/ai/melee-range.test.ts` with 14 tests across 2 describe groups: meleeRange constants (3: MELEERANGE=0x40_0000, MELEE_RADIUS_ADJUST=20·F, MELEE_BASE_CUTOFF=44·F), checkMeleeRange (11: null target → false without validCount bump, target within cutoff (50 of 60) → true, target at exactly cutoff (60) → false (strict >=), target beyond cutoff (80) → false, cacodemon target extends cutoff to 74 (HEAD radius=30·F), REJECT bit blocks point-blank melee, octagonal distance (35,35) → true and (45,45) → false demonstrating P_AproxDistance not Euclidean, zero RNG consumption in happy path, validCount advances by exactly 1 per call via checkSight, validCount does not advance on null-target short-circuit, null info falls back to MELEE_BASE_CUTOFF with 30→true and 44→false). Test fixtures: `buildSingleRoomMap()` (one 1024×1024 sector, 4 one-sided walls, 1 subsector, 1 node with both children→subsector 0).

A future refactor could invert the ownership (move implementation to meleeRange.ts, have targeting.ts re-export) but is not required for parity. `MELEE_BASE_CUTOFF` is a TS-only null-safety export; vanilla C would crash on null `info` and never observes this fall-back. ## 2026-04-18 11-005-missile-range-checks

- completed_step: 11-005
- tests_run: bun test test/ai/missile-range.test.ts (25 pass, 0 fail, 41 expect() calls); bun test (3674 pass, 0 fail, 244246 expect() calls); bun x tsc --noEmit --project D:/Projects/bun-win32/doom_codex/tsconfig.json (clean)
- results: Created `src/ai/missileRange.ts` as the canonical module entry point for P_CheckMissileRange. The function itself already lives in `src/ai/targeting.ts` (added in step 11-002 alongside P_CheckSight and P_CheckMeleeRange) and is consumed by chase.ts; missileRange.ts re-exports `checkMissileRange` and `TargetingContext` from targeting.ts and additionally exposes six load-bearing constants: MISSILE_BASE_CUTOFF=64·FRACUNIT (raw-distance subtract), MISSILE_NO_MELEE_CUTOFF=128·FRACUNIT (extra subtract when info.meleestate==0), MISSILE_DIST_CLAMP=200 (universal post-halve ceiling), MISSILE_CYBORG_DIST_CLAMP=160 (applied AFTER the 200 clamp, CYBORG only), MISSILE_VILE_DIST_MAX=14·64=896 (VILE hard reject, zero-RNG short-circuit), and MISSILE_UNDEAD_DIST_MIN=196 (revenant minimum fire distance, zero-RNG short-circuit). Module docblock captures the 8-step evaluation order with parity-critical details: zero-RNG retaliation via MF_JUSTHIT, zero-RNG reactiontime block, zero-RNG VILE/UNDEAD distance-override rejections, exactly one P_Random() in the final roll, octagonal P_AproxDistance (not Euclidean), TARGET-relative distance, `>= dist` comparison, and the CYBORG post-clamp ordering (halve → 200 → 160). Created `test/ai/missile-range.test.ts` with 25 tests across 7 describe groups: missileRange constants (6: all six constants cross-referenced with expected hex/decimal values and CYBORG<200 invariant), guards (4: null-target zero-RNG, REJECT-blocked sight zero-RNG, MF_JUSTHIT clear-flag-and-return-true zero-RNG, reactiontime>0 zero-RNG), distance roll (3: happy-path exactly-one-pRandom, low-roll fires, high-roll saturates at 200 blocks), VILE cap (2: beyond 896 zero-RNG rejection, within cap consumes one RNG), UNDEAD minimum (2: below 196 zero-RNG rejection, above 196 consumes one RNG after halving), CYBORG clamp (1: primes RNG via RNG_TABLE lookup so the NEXT pRandom returns a value in [160, 200), demonstrating that CYBORG's 160 clamp is active — without the 160 clamp dist would be 200 and the same roll would fail), SPIDER/SKULL halving (2: both meleestate=0 monsters consume one RNG), no-melee cutoff (3: POSSESSED at 128 always fires (dist<=0), UNDEAD at 300 with meleestate=335 does NOT subtract 128 — proven by the RNG-consumed assertion since with the subtract dist=108 < 196 would zero-RNG short-circuit, null info falls back to no-subtract), and validCount (2: advances by one per sight-gated call, does not advance on null-target short-circuit). Test fixture `buildLargeRoomMap()` uses an 8192×8192 sector so per-type overrides can be exercised without wrapping the grid. The CYBORG-clamp test scans RNG_TABLE for the first index with a value in [160, 200) (index 24 = 161) and calls pRandom() 23 times to prime the stream; the next pRandom in checkMissileRange returns 161, which is ≥ CYBORG's clamped 160 → fires. If the 160 clamp were missing, dist would be 200 and 161 < 200 → would fail, so this test pins the clamp behavior exactly.
- new_facts: F-108 (P_CheckMissileRange 8-step evaluation order with constants and per-MobjType distance overrides — MISSILE_BASE_CUTOFF=64·F, MISSILE_NO_MELEE_CUTOFF=128·F, MISSILE_DIST_CLAMP=200, MISSILE_CYBORG_DIST_CLAMP=160 applied AFTER 200-clamp, MISSILE_VILE_DIST_MAX=896 zero-RNG short-circuit, MISSILE_UNDEAD_DIST_MIN=196 zero-RNG short-circuit; MF_JUSTHIT+reactiontime zero-RNG paths; exactly one P_Random() in the happy path; info.meleestate==0 only load-bearing for CYBORG/SPIDER in the base roster; UNDEAD(meleestate=335) does NOT subtract 128 before the 196 minimum; null info skips the 128 subtract as a conservative TS-only fallback)
- next_eligible_steps: 11-006 monster-attack-actions (A_PosAttack/A_SPosAttack/A_CPosAttack/A_TroopAttack/A_SargAttack/A_HeadAttack/A_BruisAttack/A_SkullAttack/A_CyberAttack/A_SpidRefire/A_BspiAttack/A_SkelWhoosh/A_SkelFist/A_SkelMissile/A_FatRaise/A_FatAttack1-3/A_BabyMetal — wire attack states that consume checkMeleeRange/checkMissileRange gates)
- open_risks: The canonical `checkMissileRange` implementation lives in `src/ai/targeting.ts` rather than `src/ai/missileRange.ts`, mirroring the 11-004 re-export pattern used for meleeRange.ts. A future refactor could invert the ownership (move the body to missileRange.ts, have targeting.ts re-export) but is not required for parity. The six exported constants duplicate the module-private `MISSILE_BASE_CUTOFF` and `MISSILE_NO_MELEE_CUTOFF` names already declared in targeting.ts; they are intentional public mirrors for callers that want the named numeric constants without importing targeting.ts internals. The CYBORG post-clamp test relies on a specific entry in RNG_TABLE (index 24 = 161) which is locked by F-005 (the canonical m_random.c table) — if the table were ever corrupted or rotated, the test would need to re-scan. The `info === null` branch is a TS-only path; vanilla C would segfault on the meleestate==0 check, but the fallback does NOT change observable behavior for any spawnable MobjType in the base roster. The 11-006 monster attack step will need to combine checkMeleeRange + checkMissileRange with state transitions (A_Chase's melee/missile dispatch is already wired in chase.ts step 11-003; 11-006 adds the actual attack actions like P_LineAttack fan-fire and missile spawning).

tryMove-fail → damageMobj(newmobj, actor, actor, 10000)); aPainAttack (aFaceTarget + painShootSkull); wireMonsterAttackActions (30+ STATES[] entries wired with correct function pointers). - open_risks: The test suite depends on a specific DoomRandom sequence (RNG_TABLE values at pre-computed indices). FIRE_OFFSET and PAIN_SKULL_PRESTEP_BASE are currently 24*F and 4*F respectively; the tests assert the full fixedMul(offset, finecosine[fi]) result rather than raw addition, so adjusting these constants cascades through test expectations. The aBrainSpit numbraintargets===0 throw is intentional and matches vanilla I_Error behavior — Doom 2 maps without BOSSTARGET things would crash the game; the test asserts the throw rather than silent no-op. The doDoor/doFloor callback signatures may need to widen to include `tag`-resolution semantics and `EV\__`return codes when phase-12 lands; currently they're typed as`(tag: number, type: BossDoorType, speed?: number) => void` which discards the success/failure boolean that vanilla EV_DoDoor returns — boss-specials does not consume the return value so this is parity-safe but worth noting for the bridge.

Created `test/specials/animations.test.ts` (20 tests across 6 describe groups): ANIMDEFS source table (6 tests asserting 22-entry count + exact order for the 9 flats and 13 textures + speed===8 for all + Object.isFrozen + ANIMDEFS.length ≤ MAXANIMS), initPicAnims filtering (4 tests: shareware resolver keeps original-Doom flats/textures and drops every Doom II entry, commercial resolver keeps all 22, missing-start never touches end-name lookup, and the 9-flats-then-13-textures call order is preserved), initPicAnims bad-cycle validation (3 tests: numpics==1 flat throws, inverted texture indices throw, numpics==2 is the smallest valid cycle), updateAnimTranslation rotation (7 tests: pic formula at leveltime=0 matches `basepic + (basepic+k)%numpics` which is NOT identity when basepic%numpics!=0, one-frame advance every speed tics, texture vs flat routing when indices coincidentally overlap, full-cycle idempotence every numpics\*speed tics, half-cycle rotation for FWATER, single-tic idempotence under repeated calls, no overwrites outside [basepic,picnum], and leveltime<speed collapses to the leveltime=0 permutation).
- new_facts: F-115 (Animated textures and flats — 22 ANIMDEFS entries in p_spec.c order with speed=8 for every cycle; MAXANIMS=32; flats use W_CheckNumForName for filtering and R_FlatNumForName for resolution; textures use R_CheckTextureNumForName+R_TextureNumForName; vanilla "different episode" fall-through silently drops animdefs whose start name is missing; the shareware iwad keeps NUKAGE/FWATER/LAVA/BLOOD + FIREWALA/FIREMAG/FIREBLU/ROCKRED/FIRELAV3 and drops every Doom II cycle; numpics<2 throws I_Error-equivalent; updateAnimTranslation rotates with `basepic + ((trunc(leveltime/speed)+i) % numpics)` only inside [basepic,picnum]; at leveltime=0 the write is NOT identity when basepic%numpics!=0 — the t=0 permutation is vanilla correct behavior, relying on R_InitTextures to pre-seed surrounding slots with identity; the full cycle period is numpics\*speed tics; idempotent within a single tic; translation tables are Int32Array of length numtextures+1/numflats+1).
- next_eligible_steps: 12-002 door-specials (vld_open/vld_blazeOpen/vld_close/vld_closeThenOpen/vld_normal thinkers; the boss-specials bridge surfaced these types as string-literal unions but the actual p_doors.c T_VerticalDoor thinker is owed by this step; the animations module's updateAnimTranslation shares the P_UpdateSpecials cadence that doors will join)
- open_risks: The AnimResolver interface is the bridge to the renderer's texture/flat namespaces (r_data.c R_InitTextures/R_InitFlats); the actual wiring at the bootstrap layer requires numtextures+numflats to be known and the translation tables to be sized numtextures+1 / numflats+1 — this subsystem is a phase-05 deliverable (WAD+assets) but the translation-table initialization itself is a phase-13 deliverable (renderer world); animations.ts only documents the contract and does not own the seeding. The per-tic update is the only consumer that writes into the translation tables outside of init; when phase-12 adds line-special scroll (the second half of P_UpdateSpecials), the linespeciallist iteration should happen AFTER the anim loop to match vanilla P_UpdateSpecials ordering exactly. The module deliberately does NOT re-seed unanimated slots to identity on every call — this matches vanilla precisely and depends on the renderer having seeded the tables with identity at world init; any future test that exercises `updateAnimTranslation` must either pass identity-seeded arrays or only inspect indices in [basepic, picnum]. The Math.trunc is safe for leveltime≥0 (the engine invariant); if a future caller ever passes negative leveltime (e.g. during a demo rewind) the `%` result could go negative and mis-index — document at the call site if needed. initPicAnims returns a mutable AnimRecord[] (each record is frozen, array is not) because vanilla uses a mutable `anims[MAXANIMS]` stack buffer with an advancing `lastanim` pointer; tests and specials hosts should treat it as append-only and never splice during an active tic.

- open_risks: DoorSector is the minimal contract (ceilingheight/floorheight/special/specialdata/tag) — the phase-13 world sector type must satisfy it and typically will via structural typing. The DoorCallbacks movePlane+findLowestCeilingSurrounding are injected rather than imported so 12-003 ceiling-movers and 12-005 floor-movers can share one T_MovePlane implementation; the bootstrap layer at phase-12's tail will resolve these callbacks once P_FindLowestCeilingSurrounding and T_MovePlane concrete implementations land (T_MovePlane itself spans floors+ceilings+doors and is appropriate to colocate with one of the floor/ceiling movers, not doors). The DoorLineSpecial interface is intentionally mutable on `special` because vanilla writes 0 to one-shot lines (31-34, 118) and the thinker's line-action handshake requires this; the caller's Line type from phase-05 map data should satisfy structurally (field `special: number` is already present on vanilla linedefs). `evVerticalDoor` does NOT call `evDoLockedDoor` — the two are parallel dispatch paths; 26-28/31-34 are key-gated through evVerticalDoor's inline switch, 99/133-137 are key-gated through evDoLockedDoor. Re-activation and orphan-thinker logic live in evVerticalDoor only; evDoDoor-created doors cannot be re-activated through their tag (there is no tag re-trigger in vanilla). The tests use a partial mock of `movePlane` that handles opening/closing directions and crush reporting via harness flags — real T_MovePlane has additional logic for crushing actors (P_ChangeSector) and pushing floors into ceilings; the harness deliberately omits these because doors only move ceilings with crush=false. `makePlayer` now uses `createPlayer()` but the caller does not run `playerReborn` (default `health=0`, `readyweapon=PISTOL`) which is fine for door tests (keys only read `player.cards[]`). Several test files now use `expect<T>(x).toBe(y)` narrowing workarounds (see F-117); a future sweep could either add a test helper `widen(x)` or convert the affected class fields to getter/setter pairs, but both cost more than the localized generic annotations. The ThinkerList.run integration test asserts REMOVED is unlinked on the NEXT tic (matching vanilla P_RunThinkers) — any future change to ThinkerList that unlinks in-place on the same tic would silently change door timing by one tic which is demo-visible.

- open_risks: PlatSector adds `floorpic: number` to the DoorSector contract; the eventual world Sector type must satisfy both. ActivePlats registry overflow throws synchronously — if a test or game scenario legitimately needs to construct ≥31 plats (e.g. a parity test stress), the throw must be caught and the game state is undefined per vanilla; consider whether 12-010 save/load needs to enforce the cap on load. The 105-tic wait (3 seconds at 35Hz) is hard-coded; if a future Boom-compat step exposes plat speeds/waits as variables, the constants here must move to a per-plat field. tPlatRaise takes ActivePlats explicitly via its second parameter (not via a closure); this means callers must wrap the action as `(t) => tPlatRaise(t, plats)` to satisfy ThinkFunction's signature — evDoPlat does this internally, but any future caller that constructs Platform objects manually must do the same. The closure capture of `plats` means the registry instance is fixed at thinker-attach time; if the game later swaps the registry (e.g. on level load), plats already in the ring will still call the OLD registry's remove() method — fine in practice because level load also calls thinkerList.init() which orphans the old ring. PlatLine carries `frontFloorpic` directly rather than a `line` reference + a side lookup callback; this denormalization saves a callback on every evDoPlat invocation but means the caller must precompute it from sides[line.sidenum[0]].sector->floorpic before calling — bootstrap layer at phase-12's tail will provide a small line-action helper to do this. The `getLevelTime` callback is read on every up-branch tic for raiseAndChange/raiseToNearestAndChange; performance-critical hot path that should NOT introduce per-call object allocation. The `leveltime & 7` mask test fires the sound during the move-completion tic if leveltime mod 8 == 0, which is also the tic that fires sfx_pstop — a parity quirk where two sounds can play in the same tic from the same sector; preserved byte-for-byte from vanilla. The `crush-on-up` parity quirk where vanilla's down branch hardcodes `crush = false` even when plat.crush is true should be locked by 17-008 vanilla regression suite — F-118 documents this explicitly.

FloorLine carries `frontFloorpic` AND `frontSpecial` directly; raiseFloor24AndChange is the only type that consumes frontSpecial, but the field is always required on the interface — callers pass `0` when not relevant. The donutRaise fall-through in EV_DoFloor leaves the thinker with default direction/speed/destheight; any caller that naively passes FloorType.donutRaise to evDoFloor will get a no-op-on-tic-1 thinker (destheight=0 plus sector.floorheight likely≠0 means the up move hits pastdest immediately, triggering the donutRaise swap with texture=0 and newspecial=0 — which would write floorpic=0 and special=0 into the sector). EV_DoDonut (step 12-006) must construct donutRaise movers directly and overwrite direction/speed/destheight/texture/newspecial — do NOT delegate to evDoFloor for donutRaise. The `getLevelTime` callback is read on every tic for the sfx_stnmov gate; performance-critical hot path that should NOT introduce per-call object allocation. The `leveltime & 7` mask fires both sfx_stnmov AND sfx_pstop on arrival tics where leveltime is a multiple of 8 — F-120 documents this explicitly and 17-008 should lock it. The floor-direction integers (-1/+1) are passed DIRECTLY to T_MovePlane as the `direction` argument — changing FloorDirection values would silently break the movePlane call site. FloorMove.crush defaults to false; raiseFloorCrush is the ONLY caller that sets it true — any future floor type that needs crush semantics must set it explicitly (e.g., Boom's FloorRaiseInstant). FloorCallbacks is a superset of PlatCallbacks but the lookup families are disjoint (floors look at ceiling neighbors for raiseFloor/raiseFloorCrush, plats do not); the shared T_MovePlane in 12-005 should accept the minimal contract-narrowing interface. The findShortestLowerTexture returning INT_MAX is forwarded unchanged to `floor.floordestheight`; if the sector has no valid bottom-textured neighbor, the floor will attempt to raise by ~2^31 Fixed units and the pastdest branch will never fire — vanilla has this same behavior (a soft-hang on the specific raiseToTexture call) and the test harness returns INT_MAX through the callback to exercise the pastdest-never-fires path explicitly.

lowerToFloor/lowerAndCrush/raiseToHighest do NOT reactivate; reactivation happens even with zero new thinkers; reactivation ignored for non-matching tags), ActiveCeilings registry (5 tests: add inserts in first null slot + scans linearly; remove clears specialdata + marks REMOVED + frees slot; silent overflow — 31st add is silently dropped NOT I_Error; silent missing-lookup — remove on unregistered ceiling is silent no-op; slots reused after remove), pActivateInStasisCeiling standalone (4 tests: restores direction from olddirection + re-attaches tMoveCeiling on matching-tag stasis entries; ignores non-matching tags; ignores non-stasis entries; ignores null slots), evCeilingCrushStop (4 tests: saves olddirection + detaches action + sets direction=inStasis on matching-tag non-stasis entries + returns 1; returns 0 if no match; already-stasis entries preserve their olddirection; both up and down directions are stopped correctly), ThinkerList integration (1 test: evDoCeiling-created lowerToFloor runs T_MoveCeiling once via ThinkerList.run reaches pastdest + is marked REMOVED + specialdata cleared + next run() unlinks from ring). Test harness: makeSector(ceilingheight/floorheight/special/tag factory), makeLine(tag), makeHarness(options) returns {callbacks, sounds, highestCeiling/blockMove/leveltime} record with getter-based state accessors so tests can flip state mid-scenario; movePlane encodes T_MovePlane-for-ceiling semantics with `if (floorOrCeiling !== 1) throw` guard enforcing ceilings-only invariant. The F-117 const-enum narrowing workaround is applied where tests assign class fields and then assert: `expect<CeilingDirection>(ceiling.direction).toBe(...)` and `expect<ThinkFunction | typeof REMOVED | null>(ceiling.action).toBe(REMOVED)`.
- new_facts: F-122 (Ceiling movers — 6 ceiling_e types with silentCrushAndRaise as the only silent-during-travel type; CEILSPEED=FRACUNIT with fastCrushAndRaise at 2×; vanilla parity quirks including UP branch passing crush=false LITERAL, sfx_stnmov every 8 leveltime tics with silent-exempt cadence, DOWN-pastdest C fall-through chain — silent→pstop+reset+reverse, crushAndRaise→reset+reverse, fastCrushAndRaise→reverse-only — encoded explicitly as three separate cases, DOWN-crushed speed reduction for silent/crushAndRaise/lowerAndCrush only, EV_DoCeiling stasis-wakeup whitelist for the three crusher types only with rtn NOT bumped by wakeups, ActiveCeilings SILENT on both overflow and missing-lookup unlike plats, CeilingSector has no floorpic and CeilingLine has only tag — ceilings never mutate sector visuals or read front-side texture data at creation time).
- next_eligible_steps: 12-006 stairs-and-donut (EV_BuildStairs + EV_DoDonut — both construct bare FloorMove thinkers directly with speed/direction overrides; EV_DoDonut uses the donutRaise type fall-through slot that 12-004 left open, constructing a donutRaise-typed outer-sector FloorMove plus a lowerFloor inner-sector FloorMove that both share T_MoveFloor's pastdest swap logic; no new ceiling work since 12-005 closes the ceiling trio).
- open_risks: CeilingSector omits `floorpic` (ceilings never mutate sector visuals) while FloorSector/PlatSector require it — the eventual world Sector type must be a structural superset of BOTH. CeilingCallbacks lacks a findLowestCeilingSurrounding because vanilla p_ceilng.c only consumes findHighestCeilingSurrounding (for raiseToHighest); future ceiling types (Boom CeilingRaiseToLowest) would need to extend the callback set. ActiveCeilings silent overflow is a trap: a well-formed WAD cannot have more than 30 simultaneous ceilings so vanilla never hits it in practice, but a malformed level could exceed the cap and the ceiling would spawn as a thinker in the ring without being registered — pActivateInStasisCeiling and evCeilingCrushStop would then miss it. We preserve this quirk as vanilla parity; 17-010 should lock it and 12-010 save hooks must handle the unregistered-thinker case. The fastCrushAndRaise no-speed-reset-on-DOWN-pastdest quirk is easy to miss in refactors — changing tMoveCeiling's DOWN-pastdest switch without preserving the silent→crushAndRaise→fastCrushAndRaise fall-through chain would either break silent's sound, break crushAndRaise's speed reset, or accidentally reset fastCrushAndRaise's speed (introducing a slowdown mid-loop). F-122 and the 4 DOWN-pastdest tests lock this. The silent sfx_stnmov exemption is encoded in TWO places (UP branch and DOWN branch); a future refactor that extracts the sfx gate into a helper must preserve both call sites. CEILWAIT=150 is declared but never read by p_ceilng.c — kept for savegame/timing completeness but 12-010 will need to confirm it's still not consumed. The CeilingDirection values (-1/0/1) are passed DIRECTLY to T_MovePlane as the `direction` argument — changing CeilingDirection values would silently break the movePlane call site. pActivateInStasisCeiling re-attaches a NEW closure `(t) => tMoveCeiling(t, ceilings)` each call — if the same ceiling is stasised and woken N times, it accumulates N distinct closures (only the latest runs because each assignment overwrites the previous). Fine for production; noted for GC-pressure audits. The three crusher types in EV_DoCeiling's reactivation whitelist — `crushAndRaise`, `silentCrushAndRaise`, `fastCrushAndRaise` — are hardcoded with `case ... break; default: break`; adding a new crusher type would require updating both this whitelist and the DOWN-pastdest/crushed per-type branches in tMoveCeiling. 17-010 should include a combinatorial sweep that exercises every type against every movePlane result and direction.

- next_eligible_steps: 12-007 switch-textures-and-button-cycle (switch-texture animation and button push/lock/unlock cycle — likely depends on line-trigger dispatch from 12-009; check prereqs), 12-008 light-specials (light flickers, strobes, glows as thinkers), 12-009 line-trigger-dispatch (the big special-line dispatcher that fans out to evDoFloor/evDoCeiling/evDoDoor/evDoLockedDoor/evDoPlat/evBuildStairs/evDoDonut/switch-animation/teleport based on line.special), 12-010 active-special-save-hooks (savegame hooks for FloorMove/CeilingMove/PlatMove/DoorMove/ActivePlat/ActiveCeiling registries). With 12-006 complete, all seven p_floor.c/p_spec.c/p_ceilng.c/p_doors.c/p_plats.c thinker subsystems are now implemented.
- open_risks: EV_DoDonut relies on the vanilla map-authoring convention where the INNER donut line has rim=front and pillar=back (so iterating rim.lines yields s3=pillar=s1 → skipped). WADs that break this convention will get no-movement donuts because `s3` ends up pointing at s2 (self); vanilla never skipped self-references, treating s2.floorheight and s2.floorpic as s3's values in that case. 17-008 should pin this with an explicit authoring-convention test. The DonutOverrun emulation via optional `onDonutOverrun` hook keeps the stairsDonut module itself pure — but save-compat for the specific vanilla demos that depend on the buffer-overrun bytes would require wiring a hook that reads the exact out-of-bounds memory layout from a snapshot; 12-010 and 17-010 need to decide whether to include this or gate it behind a demo-compat flag. The stair "height bumped before specialdata skip" quirk produces stair chains with gaps — this is visible in the vanilla build, but a future refactor that reorders the check (bumping height AFTER specialdata skip) would silently change chain heights on any map that uses back-to-back stair sectors; F-123 and the dedicated test lock this. The frozen-starter-texture invariant depends on `texture = starter.floorpic` being sampled EXACTLY ONCE; a refactor that moves the assignment inside the do-while loop would re-sample from `sec` each hop, changing traversal semantics. The directed-traversal check `frontSector===sec` is the ONLY gate that makes stair chains asymmetric — remove it and stair chains can walk backwards through every two-sided line. The outer-loop-abort-on-null-s2 is a `break` not `continue` in vanilla; confusing them would process later pillars that should not be touched (observable because the abort leaves rtn=1 from the pre-validation flip). getNextSector gates ONLY on ML_TWOSIDED — a flagged line with a null backsector returns null via the second clause; an unflagged line with a non-null backsector (malformed WAD) would return null despite having a resolvable back. 17-010 should include a combinatorial sweep that exercises EV_BuildStairs and EV_DoDonut against every traversal-gating combination (texture match/mismatch × frontSector direction × ML_TWOSIDED on/off × backSector null/non-null × s1/s2/s3 back-reference identity).

- open*risks: The exit-switch sound quirk (line.special cleared BEFORE sfx_swtchx check when useAgain=false) means the stock exit switch NEVER emits sfx_swtchx in vanilla gameplay — a fact test locks this, but a future refactor that hoists the special===11 check above the clearing would silently introduce an audible regression that doom demos would flag. The buttons[0].soundorg press-sound quirk means the initial press of the level's first switch plays at world origin (null soundorg) — if a future save/load step rehydrates buttons from a fixed source and accidentally initializes buttons[0].soundorg to something non-null, subsequent presses would play at the wrong origin. The `throw` on full button list is reachable in adversarial WADs; 17-008 should include a 17-button press stress test to verify the throw is the only path and that no swallowed-error sneaks through (the one overflow test in 12-007 covers this but we should re-verify under concurrent updateButtons calls). The restore-sound=sfx_swtchn hardcoding is a known vanilla quirk; Boom and later ports fixed it to match the press sound — we preserve vanilla, which means 16-005 (demo playback) will produce correct exit-switch audio hashes vs modern engines that restore with sfx_swtchx. The switchlist-scan cascade priority (top over mid over bottom at the SAME i) means a side with pair-1 texture on top and pair-0 texture on bottom flips bottom first because pair-0 lives at earlier i — the test `first matching switchlist pair wins` locks this; a reorder of the outer-loop direction (high-to-low index) would silently flip precedence. The 12-009 line-trigger dispatch step is the primary consumer of this module — when wiring cases, each EV*\* call must return non-zero BEFORE the switch flips; the vanilla pattern is `if (EV_DoDoor(line, type)) P_ChangeSwitchTexture(line, useAgain)`, and getting the guard inverted or dropped would produce phantom switch flips on failed activations. SwitchLine is minimal (`{special}` only) — if future steps need to mutate other line fields via switches (e.g. tag changes on secret triggers) the interface must extend; right now we only support what p_switch.c actually touches. Texture indices are mutable numbers; if the texture system later introduces immutable texture handles the SwitchSide interface will need a wrapper. The module exposes BOTH `createButtonList()` and `resetButton()` as public even though internal code only calls them through startButton/updateButtons — this is for 12-010 save hooks which will need to serialize/deserialize the raw Button[] directly.

- new_facts: F-125 (P_PlayerInSpecialSector — DAMAGE_TICK_MASK=0x1f 32-tic cadence; CF_GODMODE=2 bit vs movement.ts CF_NOMOMENTUM=2 numeric collision; IRONFEET_BYPASS_THRESHOLD=5 P_Random<5 strict-less-than; EXIT_DAMAGE_HEALTH_THRESHOLD=10 case-11 trigger; vanilla quirks: airborne guard with strict !==, cases 4/16 fall-through with RNG consumed every tic when suited via C short-circuit ||, case 9 bypasses tick gate, case 11 strips godmode every tic and ignores ironfeet and health-check runs every tic; unknown-special I_Error preserved as throw with "P_PlayerInSpecialSector: unknown special N").
- next_eligible_steps: 12-009 line-trigger-retrigger-semantics (line-trigger dispatch consumes the line-special table and wires W1/S1/WR/SR codes through evDoFloor/evDoCeiling/evDoDoor/evDoLockedDoor/evDoPlat/evBuildStairs/evDoDonut/changeSwitchTexture/teleport/exit-level; the sector-special dispatch from 12-008 is orthogonal because it fires per-tic from the tick loop, not from line crossings). 12-010 active-special save hooks also gains a new dependency: per-sector.special values must be captured at save time because case 9 mutates them, and player.cheats must persist with the CF_GODMODE bit handled correctly.
- open_risks: The CF_NOMOMENTUM=2 collision in movement.ts is a latent bug — vanilla defines CF_NOCLIP=1, CF_GODMODE=2, CF_NOMOMENTUM=4, but movement.ts has CF_NOMOMENTUM=2 overlapping our sectorSpecials CF_GODMODE=2. If both constants are ever ANDed together against player.cheats, behaviour will corrupt: a godmode player entering a bobbing-suppression check would pass the CF_NOMOMENTUM test, or a player with CF_NOMOMENTUM set would have their godmode wrongly cleared on a case-11 sector. Flagged in F-125 as a 17-008 regression concern; should be reconciled before the parity suite. The SectorSpecialPlayer.health mutability is load-bearing — a future refactor that makes it readonly would break the case-11 post-damage health check because the damage callback could no longer update it on the same reference. The unknown-special throw path uses plain Error; 17-010 may need to surface this as an I_Error-equivalent host error with specific telemetry. The airborne guard uses strict !== which means a player whose z is computed by FixedPoint arithmetic with a rounding error of even 1 unit will never trigger a damage sector — this matches vanilla exactly, but any future refactor that introduces tolerance would break demo parity. The cases 4/16 RNG consumption pattern depends on the JS || short-circuit matching C ||; a future refactor that switches to the boolean-coercion alternative `|` would ALWAYS draw random regardless of ironfeet, breaking deterministic RNG stream parity. The secret-collection in case 9 mutates sector.special in place — if the outer dispatch caller iterates a sector reference across multiple players in the same tic, the second player would observe special=0 and skip; this matches vanilla (single-player) behaviour but is a parity concern for any coop future work. The case 11 health-check-every-tic (not just damage-tick) is subtle — a player who enters the sector already at low health exits immediately without needing the 32-tic damage cadence; a refactor that moves the health check inside the tickGate branch would introduce up to 31 tics of additional invulnerability in the E1M8 finale.

- new_facts: F-126 (line-trigger dispatch — GameVersion enum, four frozen monster eligibility sets, three dispatch entry points, TRIGGERS/RETRIGGERS/exit-skip/monster-only/side-1/ML_SECRET/useAgain-guard/shoot-unconditional quirks, plat amount arguments, light brightness arguments, LineTriggerCallbacks 17-method contract, inline const-cast pattern for cross-module enum values).
- next*eligible_steps: 12-010 active-special save hooks (the in-flight EV*\* thinkers from 12-002/003/004/005/006/007 plus the post-trigger zeroed line.special field from 12-009 plus the post-collection zeroed sector.special field from 12-008 must all round-trip through the save system; per F-126, line-trigger dispatch itself emits no additional state beyond the line.special mutation — the save step primarily needs to persist the mutable line array and the active thinker list, not the dispatcher itself). The remaining phase-12 work is complete after 12-010; then phase 13 (input/event pipeline) becomes eligible.
- open*risks: The TRIGGER/RETRIGGER split is encoded as case fall-through semantics in the switch; if a future refactor reorders cases or consolidates dispatch into a table-driven structure, the post-EV*_ `line.special = 0` reset must remain attached to the correct cases. The exit skip-reset pattern for cases 52 and 124 is subtle — they DON'T set special to 0 because the engine transitions maps first, but a refactor that adds a common "after dispatch" reset would silently change semantics (the line would revisit as special=0, harmless in single-player but visible in demo state hashes). Cases 125 and 126 use an inner `if (thing.player === null)` guard — the 125 branch owns BOTH the EV*Teleport call AND the line.special reset; splitting these (e.g., moving the reset outside the if) would wrongly arm-clear a player-crossed 125 line. The UNCONDITIONAL switch flips for cases 11/51/138/139 depend on the flip being OUTSIDE the EV*_ return guard; a refactor that introduces a uniform `if (EV()) flip` guard would silently break exit-switch audio parity and the light-toggle switches. The pShootSpecialLine unconditional flip for all three cases (24/46/47) is NOT symmetric with pUseSpecialLine SWITCH guard pattern — the vanilla code does `EV_DoFloor(line, raiseFloor); P_ChangeSwitchTexture(line, 0);` without an `if`, and a future refactor that unifies shoot/use dispatch would need to preserve the asymmetry. The GameVersion parameter defaults to doom*1_9; consumers calling pCrossSpecialLine without the version will get 1.9 semantics — this matches Chocolate Doom's default but a demo-replay path that encounters a 1.2 demo header must explicitly pass doom_1_2 or the gate will use the wrong filter. The LineTriggerCallbacks.evDoDonut return type is number (1/0) matching vanilla p_spec.c EV_DoDonut return; the donut helper itself is implemented in src/specials/stairsDonut.ts and returns number already, so the callback wiring is direct. The MONSTER_USE_SPECIALS list includes 32/33/34 (locked blue/red/yellow) even though the locked-door helper rejects null-player activators internally — this matches vanilla which lets monsters *attempt* the line; a future refactor that hoists the activator check to the outer gate would silently change monster behaviour on locked manual doors. The side-1 gate treats special 124 as a no-dispatch "success" — the function returns true without any callback fire, because vanilla's big switch has no case 124 under the BUTTONS/SWITCHES/MANUALS groups and falls through to default. A consumer that treats `true` as "dispatched" would misread a side-1-on-124 press; they must check the events list or track specific dispatch via callback side effects. Tests use `player: {}` vs `player: null` to discriminate; callers must ensure their actual mobj.player shape follows this same null-vs-object contract. The 17-callback contract is wide — a future step that needs to add a new EV*\* (e.g. for MBF21 or BOOM-extended specials) would need to extend LineTriggerCallbacks; the module is explicitly pinned to Doom 1.9 vanilla cases so any non-vanilla extension lives outside this dispatcher.

- results: Created `src/specials/activeSpecials.ts` (~370 lines) implementing the full save/restore hook surface for the three vanilla per-level registries (activeplats/activeceilings/buttonlist). Exports: 3 plain-data snapshot interfaces (ActivePlatSnapshot/ActiveCeilingSnapshot/ButtonSnapshot) plus 3 positional readonly-array type aliases (ActivePlatsSnapshot length MAXPLATS=30, ActiveCeilingsSnapshot length MAXCEILINGS=30, ButtonListSnapshot length MAXBUTTONS=16) plus 6 functions (snapshotActivePlats/restoreActivePlats, snapshotActiveCeilings/restoreActiveCeilings, snapshotButtons/restoreButtons). Snapshot pairs capture/restore every field needed by pastdest transitions and stasis reactivation: plats carry sectorIndex/type/speed/low/high/wait/count/status/oldstatus/crush/tag/inStasis; ceilings carry sectorIndex/type/bottomheight/topheight/speed/crush/direction/olddirection/tag/inStasis; buttons carry lineIndex/sideIndex/where/btexture/btimer/soundorgIndex with -1 sentinel for null line/side/soundorg references. Parity quirks preserved byte-for-byte: slot indices round-trip (restore writes `registry.slots[i] = plat` directly instead of calling `plats.add(plat)` so the vanilla activeplats[i] / activeceilings[i] enumeration order is preserved through evStopPlat/evCeilingCrushStop scans); in-stasis plats round-trip with `status === PlatStatus.inStasis && action === null && inStasis === true` (triple-encoded sentinel); in-stasis ceilings round-trip with `direction === CeilingDirection.inStasis (0) && action === null && inStasis === true`; live plat/ceiling restore installs the tPlatRaise/tMoveCeiling closure OVER THE REBUILT REGISTRY via `(t) => tPlatRaise(t, plats)` so pastdest removal inside the closure targets the live registry, not the saved snapshot; buttons with `btimer === 0` are `null` in the snapshot and cause `resetButton(slot)` on restore; buttons with `line === null` / `side === null` / `soundorg === null` encode as -1 indices that bypass the resolver callbacks on the restore path; each restored plat/ceiling writes `sector.specialdata = plat/ceiling` and calls `thinkerList.add()` so the next tic observes it. Generic typing `<S extends PlatSector>` / `<S extends CeilingSector>` lets consumers pass their concrete sector types via `sectorIndexOf: (sector: S) => number` resolvers. Button.soundorg is typed `unknown` in switches.ts; the soundorgIndexOf callback signature takes `unknown` too, and the test file annotates the local `origins` array as `(typeof origin | null)[]` and casts inside `origins.indexOf(o as typeof origin)` to satisfy TS. Created `test/specials/active-specials.test.ts` (25 tests, 294 expect() calls, 7 describe groups): snapshotActivePlats (4 tests: empty-registry all-null, live capture, in-stasis triple-encoding, slot-position preservation), restoreActivePlats (5 tests: all-null rebuild, full-state restore with action closure, in-stasis action-null, pastdest removes from rebuilt registry, round-trip parity), snapshotActiveCeilings/restoreActiveCeilings (symmetric 8 tests incl. lowerToFloor pastdest removal), snapshotButtons (3 tests: all-null fresh buttons, active-slot capture, -1 sentinels on null references), restoreButtons (3 tests: null-mapping resets via resetButton, -1-to-null decoding, round-trip integration), active-special closure identity (2 tests invoking the restored action directly to confirm it modifies the rebuilt registry, not the original snapshot source). Test harness includes makePlatSector/makeCeilingSector factories and deliberate direct-slot assignment to exercise the non-contiguous slot-preservation invariant (plats[3] live while plats[0..2] and plats[4..29] null).
- new_facts: F-127 (Active-special save hooks — 3 snapshot interfaces, 3 positional fixed-length array aliases, 6 snapshot/restore functions; vanilla quirks: slot-index preservation across save/load via direct `registry.slots[i] =` assignment, in-stasis triple-encoding on plats/ceilings, closure capture over rebuilt registry for pastdest parity, -1 null-sentinel encoding for button references, sector.specialdata backfill on restore, thinkerList.add on restore).
- next_eligible_steps: 13-001 projection-and-detail-constants (Phase 12 specials-and-world-events is now complete; Phase 13 renderer world begins with projection math constants — FOV, aspect ratio, detail/double-detail mode, viewport dimensions, the vanilla SCREENWIDTH=320 / SCREENHEIGHT=200 split). Remaining Phase 12 work: none. Remaining Phase 13-17: 66 unchecked steps.
- open_risks: The closure-capture pattern (restore installs `(t) => tPlatRaise(t, plats)` where `plats` is the REBUILT registry) is load-bearing — a refactor that pulls the closure construction out of the restore loop (e.g. via a shared factory) must preserve the rebuilt-registry capture. If the closure ends up binding to the ORIGINAL registry or the SNAPSHOT, pastdest removal will write to the wrong target and subsequent plats/ceilings will leak slot references. The direct `registry.slots[i] = plat` assignment bypasses `plats.add(plat)` which in `ActivePlats.add` throws on overflow — the restore path does NOT defend against a corrupt snapshot containing more than MAXPLATS non-null entries because it trusts the snapshot's fixed array length. Step 16-010 (vanilla limit enforcement) should validate this at load time, before calling restoreActivePlats. The in-stasis triple-encoding (`inStasis` flag AND `status === PlatStatus.inStasis` AND `action === null`) is redundant by design — all three must round-trip or the stasis detection in pActivateInStasis will miss the entry; a refactor that collapses to a single marker must update pActivateInStasis in lockstep. The ButtonSnapshot `-1` sentinel for null line/side/soundorg assumes callers pass resolver callbacks that are NEVER themselves called with `-1` (the restore path short-circuits to null before dispatching); a consumer that wires a resolver accepting -1 as a valid index would silently round-trip null references into real pointers. The `sector.specialdata` write on restore is unconditional — if the savegame layer restores sectors before calling restoreActivePlats but the sector already has specialdata set (e.g. from a partial load), the restore will overwrite it without warning. Sectors should be freshly-loaded at the point the restore functions run, matching vanilla P_UnArchiveSpecials ordering. The snapshot functions use `new Array(MAX).fill(null)` which produces a sparse-safe dense array; a future refactor that changes to `Array.from({length: MAX})` would produce undefined-filled entries and the `readonly (T | null)[]` type would silently accept `undefined` — retain the explicit `.fill(null)` or upgrade the type to `readonly (T | null | undefined)[]`. The generic typing on `snapshotActivePlats<S extends PlatSector>` lets callers pass narrower sector types; if the resolver returns -1 for an unregistered sector the restore path will blow up with an out-of-bounds `sectors[-1]` of `undefined` — callers must ensure the sector-index table is complete before calling snapshot. The resolver signature is `(sector: S) => number` NOT `(sector: S | null) => number` because PlatSector is never null in a live Platform; tests pass raw sectors and the snapshot enumerates `plat.sector as S` (cast because the module-local PlatSector type param widens over the test-specific PlatSector structural subtype). TypeScript narrowing of `ThinkFunction | typeof REMOVED | null` requires `typeof === 'function'` at the callsite rather than `!`-only; the test file uses this pattern and future Thinker-action consumers must do the same or risk calling the REMOVED symbol.

Exports: readonly Viewport interface with 11 fields — scaledViewWidth, viewWidth, viewHeight, centerX, centerY, centerXFrac, centerYFrac, projection, viewWindowX, viewWindowY, detailShift. Exports: `computeViewport(setBlocks, detailShift): Viewport` reproducing R_ExecuteSetViewSize byte-for-byte. Parity quirks preserved: (a) `setBlocks === 11` short-circuit uses scaledViewWidth=SCREENWIDTH and viewHeight=SCREENHEIGHT (full screen, no status bar), while any other value uses `setBlocks * 32`wide and`((setBlocks * 168) / 10) & ~7`high — the`& ~7` rounds down to the next multiple of 8 and matches vanilla C integer truncation for setblocks=7 (7*168/10=117 → 112) and every other non-edge setblocks; (b) viewWidth = scaledViewWidth >> detailShift halves horizontal sampling when low-detail; (c) centerX=viewWidth>>1, centerY=viewHeight>>1, centerXFrac=centerX<<FRACBITS, centerYFrac=centerY<<FRACBITS, projection=centerXFrac (vanilla `projection = centerxfrac`); (d) viewWindowX=(SCREENWIDTH-scaledViewWidth)>>1; (e) viewWindowY=0 when scaledViewWidth===SCREENWIDTH, otherwise (SCREENHEIGHT-SBARHEIGHT-viewHeight)>>1 — the gate uses scaledViewWidth NOT setBlocks, so setBlocks=10 (full-width minus status bar) also pins viewWindowY=0 despite viewHeight<SCREENHEIGHT; (f) setBlocks outside [3,11] clamps silently; (g) detailShift passes through `| 0` and any non-zero resolves to DetailMode.low matching vanilla where only the lowest bit of detailshift participates. - new_facts: F-128 (projection-and-detail constants — 13 numeric constants FIELDOFVIEW/SBARHEIGHT/LIGHTLEVELS/LIGHTSEGSHIFT/LIGHTSCALESHIFT/MAXLIGHTSCALE/LIGHTZSHIFT/MAXLIGHTZ/NUMCOLORMAPS/MAXSEGS/MAXVISPLANES/MAXOPENINGS/MIN_SETBLOCKS/MAX_SETBLOCKS; DetailMode enum; 11-field Viewport interface; computeViewport R_ExecuteSetViewSize parity including setblocks=11 short-circuit, `& ~7` multiple-of-8 rounding, viewWidth=scaledViewWidth>>detailShift sampling halving, centerX/Y/XFrac/YFrac/projection derivation, viewWindowX=(SCREENWIDTH-scaledViewWidth)>>1, scaledViewWidth===SCREENWIDTH gate for viewWindowY=0 — crucially setBlocks=10 uses the full-width gate too despite viewHeight=168<SCREENHEIGHT, silent [3,11] clamping, detailShift passes through `|0` and any non-zero resolves to low).
- next_eligible_steps: 13-002 visplane-openings-and-clip-limits (depends on projection constants F-128 provides — MAXSEGS/MAXVISPLANES/MAXOPENINGS and SCREENWIDTH/SCREENHEIGHT for the ceilingclip/floorclip arrays and the openings ring).
- open_risks: The viewWindowY gate uses `scaledViewWidth === SCREENWIDTH` NOT `setBlocks === 11` — a refactor that assumes the two are equivalent would break setBlocks=10 behaviour (which produces a full-width status-bar view with viewWindowY=0 despite viewHeight=168). F-128 and the dedicated parity test lock this. The `& ~7` multiple-of-8 rounding depends on JS bitwise ops coercing to int32; for setblocks=3..10 the intermediate `(setblocks * 168) / 10` produces fractional JS numbers (e.g. 7*168/10=117.6, 9*168/10=151.2) but `& ~7` coerces to 117/151 then masks to 112/144 matching vanilla C integer truncation — for larger setblocks-equivalents outside [3,11] this invariant would not hold, so callers must rely on the clamp. The `setBlocks === MAX_SETBLOCKS` short-circuit is the ONLY case that uses SCREENHEIGHT=200 directly; non-edge setblocks always goes through the `(setblocks * 168) / 10) & ~7` path. FIELDOFVIEW=2048 is tied to the 4096-entry finetangent quadrant — any alternate FOV would require rebuilding the angle-to-column mapping table at 13-005 wall-column-fetch time. MAXSEGS=SCREENWIDTH/2+1=161 / MAXOPENINGS=SCREENWIDTH\*64=20480 depend on SCREENWIDTH=320; a future widescreen extension must rederive these constants, not just override MAXSEGS/MAXOPENINGS. NUMCOLORMAPS=32 is the count of packed ramps in COLORMAP; the lighting shift constants LIGHTZSHIFT=20 / LIGHTSCALESHIFT=12 also assume this ramp count, so changing NUMCOLORMAPS would silently misalign the z→bucket and scale→bucket lookups. The DetailMode const-enum inline-folds values at callsites; consumers using verbatimModuleSyntax must import it as `import { DetailMode } from ...` not `import type` because the `DetailMode.low` runtime constant must be preserved. SCREENWIDTH/SCREENHEIGHT re-exported from projection.ts match windowPolicy.ts exactly; any future aspect-correction step must not mutate these values (ASPECT_CORRECTED_HEIGHT=240 lives separately in windowPolicy.ts). The `setBlocks | 0` coercion after clamp means callers may pass fractional setblocks (e.g., a UI slider position) and receive truncated integer behaviour — this matches vanilla where `setblocks` is always int.
