The ±0x7FFFFFFF convention and its int32 preservation test locks this. Uint8Array(SCREENWIDTH) in Visplane.top/bottom restricts column y-coordinates to 0..255 — at SCREENHEIGHT=200 this is fine (max row index 199) but a future tall-res or widescreen step must widen these arrays to Uint16Array OR add a bounds check. The RENDER_POOL_LIMITS frozen record is a read convenience; callers who want the individual constants should import them directly so tree-shaking can prune the frozen object; a refactor that replaces the individual exports with only the record would force all call sites to carry the whole snapshot. The OPENINGS_BYTES_PER_ENTRY=2 encodes the vanilla `short` semantics; if a later step needs to use Int32Array for opening offsets >32767 (unlikely at SCREENWIDTH=320 but possible under widescreen), both constants must update together. The empty-Visplane sentinel (minx=SCREENWIDTH, maxx=-1, minx>maxx) is a load-bearing invariant for R_FindPlane/R_CheckPlane loops that iterate `for (x=minx; x<=maxx; x++)` — a refactor that uses a dedicated boolean `isEmpty` flag would need every consumer to check it, whereas the minx>maxx invariant is self-evident from the loop bounds. The CEILINGCLIP_DEFAULT=-1 vs floorclip=viewHeight asymmetry is parity-critical: the ceiling default is exactly -1 (one row above the top) so the first ceiling span renders at y=0, while the floor default is viewHeight (one row past the bottom) so an unused column emits no floor span — a refactor that "symmetrizes" these to 0/viewHeight-1 would break both edges. The Silhouette const enum inline-folds values at callsites; consumers using verbatimModuleSyntax must import it as `import { Silhouette } from ...` not `import type` because the `Silhouette.both` runtime constant must be preserved. Later phase-13 steps (13-006/13-007 wall paths) will allocate solidsegs[] and drawsegs[] pools that MUST initialize solidsegs[0]/[1] with the sentinel pair and reset drawseg_p=drawsegs[0] every frame via R_ClearDrawSegs — missing either reset would corrupt the next frame's clip walk. The 32 tests enforce the pool-cap equality but the actual I_Error emission lives in the (yet-to-be-authored) 13-006+ wall paths; those later steps must throw with the exact vanilla message strings ("R_DrawPlanes: drawsegs overflow", etc.) to match host error handling. The Int16Array viewport-sample pattern used in the "R_ClearPlanes column-clip defaults" test is a preview of the 13-009 visplane-span-render step's actual backing storage; a refactor of that step to Int32Array would invalidate this preview but not the constants themselves.

## 2026-04-20 13-003-column-and-span-drawers

- completed_step: 13-003
- tests_run: bun x prettier --write D:/Projects/bun-win32/doom_codex/src/render/drawPrimitives.ts D:/Projects/bun-win32/doom_codex/test/render/column-span-draw.test.ts (ran before verification — reformatted the multi-line import block in column-span-draw.test.ts to the repo's single-line style, drawPrimitives.ts unchanged); bun test test/render/column-span-draw.test.ts (30 pass, 0 fail, 192_083 expect() calls — the high count is from two full-viewport canary sweeps that expect() every pixel of a 200x320=64_000-cell Uint8Array in the "writes into the correct column" and "writes into the correct row" tests); bun test (4419 pass, 0 fail, 463_915 expect() calls — delta of +30 tests vs prior 4389 and +192_083 expect() vs prior 271_832 matches the 30 new drawPrimitives tests plus the two canary sweeps); bun x tsc --noEmit --project D:/Projects/bun-win32/doom_codex/tsconfig.json (clean, exit 0, no output); bun x prettier --write D:/Projects/bun-win32/doom_codex (full-workspace reformat pass between verification runs — no unexpected files changed, FACT_LOG.md had minor whitespace normalization, no code files reformatted).
- results: Created `src/render/drawPrimitives.ts` (~240 lines) implementing the two vanilla r*draw.c inner-loop primitives — R_DrawColumn and R_DrawSpan — as pure-arithmetic TypeScript functions `rDrawColumn(job, framebuffer, screenWidth=SCREENWIDTH)` and `rDrawSpan(job, framebuffer, screenWidth=SCREENWIDTH)`. Exports 6 numeric constants (COLUMN_HEIGHT_MASK=127; FLAT_DIMENSION=64; FLAT_SIZE=4096; FLAT_Y_SHIFT=FRACBITS-6=10; FLAT_Y_MASK=63\*64=4032; FLAT_X_MASK=63) and two readonly interfaces (ColumnDrawJob {x, yl, yh, textureMid, iscale, centerY, source: Uint8Array, colormap: Uint8Array}; SpanDrawJob {x1, x2, y, xFrac, yFrac, xStep, yStep, source: Uint8Array, colormap: Uint8Array}) mirroring the vanilla dc*\_/ds\_\_ global state blocks. rDrawColumn implements `count = yh - yl; if (count < 0) return; dest = yl * screenWidth + x; frac = textureMid + (yl - centerY) * iscale; do { fb[dest] = colormap[source[(frac >> FRACBITS) & COLUMN_HEIGHT_MASK]]; dest += screenWidth; frac = (frac + iscale) | 0; } while (count--);` — matching vanilla's early-exit guard plus the do-while(count--) semantics that writes count+1 pixels. rDrawSpan implements `dest = y * screenWidth + x1; count = x2 - x1; do { spot = ((yFrac >> FLAT_Y_SHIFT) & FLAT_Y_MASK) + ((xFrac >> FRACBITS) & FLAT_X_MASK); fb[dest++] = colormap[source[spot]]; xFrac = (xFrac + xStep) | 0; yFrac = (yFrac + yStep) | 0; } while (count--);` — NO count<0 guard matching vanilla's omission. Accumulator updates are wrapped through `| 0` defensively so JS float64 precision never diverges from C int32 two's-complement addition. Parity-critical invariants preserved byte-for-byte and locked by the 30-test suite: (1) COLUMN_HEIGHT_MASK=127 wraps the wall-texture column at 128 rows — the test that sets yl=126/centerY=126/textureMid=126*FRACUNIT/iscale=FRACUNIT/yh=129 reads source[126], source[127], source[0], source[1]; (2) negative textureMid wraps via signed-shift then mask — frac=-FRACUNIT gives `-1 & 127 = 127` so the column starts at source[127]; (3) rDrawColumn early-exits on yh < yl with zero writes (verified by full-framebuffer canary sweep); (4) yh === yl writes exactly one pixel (single-row count===0 case); (5) per-row stride is screenWidth bytes (verified on a small 10x4 framebuffer to prove the arithmetic works without SCREENWIDTH=320); (6) colormap is applied to every source byte (inverse ramp colormap i→255-i verified); (7) rDrawSpan spot arithmetic `((yFrac>>10)&4032) + ((xFrac>>16)&63)` composes the 64x64 flat offset without overlap — FLAT_Y_MASK & FLAT_X_MASK === 0 and FLAT_Y_MASK | FLAT_X_MASK === 4095 locked; (8) xStep=FRACUNIT walks row 0 of the flat (spot = U), yStep=FRACUNIT walks column 0 (spot = V*64), combined xStep=yStep=FRACUNIT samples the flat diagonal; (9) xFrac past 64th column wraps modulo 64 (xFrac=63*FRACUNIT, xStep=FRACUNIT reads 63, 0, 1); yFrac past 64th row wraps modulo 64 (yFrac=63*FRACUNIT, yStep=FRACUNIT reads row 63, 0, 1); (10) negative xFrac wraps via signed-shift then mask (xFrac=-FRACUNIT reads source[63]); (11) extreme positive fracs stay within FLAT_SIZE (xFrac=63*FRACUNIT + yFrac=63*FRACUNIT reads source[4095]). Created `test/render/column-span-draw.test.ts` (30 tests, 192_083 expect() calls, 7 describe groups): drawPrimitives constants (7 tests: COLUMN_HEIGHT_MASK=127, FLAT_DIMENSION=64, FLAT_SIZE=4096, FLAT_Y_SHIFT=10, FLAT_Y_MASK=4032, FLAT_X_MASK=63, and the disjoint partition property FLAT_Y_MASK & FLAT_X_MASK === 0 && FLAT_Y_MASK | FLAT_X_MASK === 4095), rDrawColumn early-exit (2 tests: yh < yl writes nothing, yh === yl writes exactly one pixel), rDrawColumn stride and colormap (4 tests: identity step reads source[0..N], writes into correct column leaving others untouched via 200x320 canary sweep, per-row stride is exactly screenWidth bytes, colormap i→255-i applied to every byte), rDrawColumn texturemid/iscale arithmetic (3 tests: textureMid=2*FRACUNIT at yl=centerY starts at source[2], yl<centerY subtracts (centerY-yl)*iscale from texturemid, fractional iscale=FRACUNIT>>1 advances slowly duplicating source[0],source[0],source[1],source[1],...), rDrawColumn wrap quirk (2 tests: >= 128 row wraps via & 127, negative texture V wraps via signed right shift then mask), rDrawSpan stride and colormap (5 tests: single-pixel span, multi-pixel span writes x2-x1+1 bytes, writes into correct row via 200x320 canary sweep, per-row stride is screenWidth, colormap applied), rDrawSpan spot arithmetic (3 tests: xStep walks row 0, yStep walks column 0, diagonal sampling), rDrawSpan wrap quirks (4 tests: xFrac wrap modulo 64, yFrac wrap modulo 64, negative xFrac wrap, extreme positive fracs land inside FLAT_SIZE). Tests use a `CANARY=0xaa` sentinel byte to pre-fill the framebuffer and an IDENTITY_COLORMAP (i→i) so source bytes pass through unchanged unless the test explicitly overrides. The makeFramebuffer/makeColumnJob/makeSpanJob helpers reduce boilerplate across 30 tests without hiding the parity-critical parameters.
- new*facts: F-130 (column/span drawer primitives — 6 numeric constants COLUMN_HEIGHT_MASK=127/FLAT_DIMENSION=64/FLAT_SIZE=4096/FLAT_Y_SHIFT=10/FLAT_Y_MASK=4032/FLAT_X_MASK=63; two readonly interfaces ColumnDrawJob and SpanDrawJob mirroring vanilla dc*\_/ds\_\_ global state blocks; two functions rDrawColumn (with vanilla `count<0 return` guard) and rDrawSpan (no count<0 guard, matches vanilla); parity quirks: source index `& 127` wraps wall-texture columns at 128 rows, flat spot `+` and `|` interchangeable because y-mask and x-mask partition bottom 12 bits disjointly, signed right shift preserves wrap under negative fracs, accumulator `| 0` defensive against float64 divergence, per-row stride is screenWidth for columns and 1 byte for spans, colormap is a 256-entry Uint8Array applied per-pixel).
- next_eligible_steps: 13-004 patch-decode-and-draw (depends on rDrawColumn — patch decode builds a composited Uint8Array column and calls rDrawColumn; the 13-004 step will need to handle the masked-column post format where vanilla's R_DrawMaskedColumn walks posts and calls R_DrawColumn per-post with dc_yl/dc_yh adjusted per post).
- open_risks: rDrawSpan has NO count<0 guard matching vanilla's omission — a caller that passes x2 < x1 triggers the do-while(count--) degenerate loop (potentially writing past the framebuffer or looping indefinitely). The `do { ... } while (count--)` check in JS with count=-1 continues because -1 is truthy; with count=-2 also truthy; etc. This is a LOAD-BEARING parity defect: vanilla R_DrawSpan also has this behavior, so callers at 13-006/13-007/13-009 that hand-assemble span bounds MUST guarantee x2>=x1 before invoking rDrawSpan. A defensive `if (count < 0) return;` would change behavior on malformed input but is NOT added because vanilla doesn't have it and the renderer's span generators never produce x2<x1. The COLUMN_HEIGHT_MASK=127 is hard-coded for vanilla's 128-tall composite column buffer — a future source port that composes 256-tall columns would need a new mask. The accumulator `| 0` wraps are defensive; at realistic iscale/xStep/yStep magnitudes (<2^21) they're effectively no-ops, but a future bug where a caller passes a near-INT_MAX step would wrap at the 32-bit boundary matching C — without `| 0`, the JS accumulator would keep a large float that eventually exceeds 2^53 (precision limit) and diverge. The `frac = (frac + iscale) | 0` pattern locks this. rDrawColumn and rDrawSpan treat the colormap as opaque — a 13-010 sky step that wants to bypass diminishing simply passes a no-op colormap pointer (i→i) rather than modifying the primitive. The low-detail variants R_DrawColumnLow and R_DrawSpanLow are NOT implemented here because F-128 pins detailshift=0 in the reference run; if a later parity harness needs low-detail, it must add a separate primitive rather than adding a detailShift branch to these fast paths. R_DrawFuzzColumn (13-014) and R_DrawTranslatedColumn are also deferred — they share the ColumnDrawJob shape but swap the inner loop, so they belong as separate primitives not as branches inside rDrawColumn. The primitives operate on framebuffer-absolute coordinates — a refactor that accepts viewport-relative coordinates and folds viewWindowX/Y internally would require passing the viewport into every call, at which point the primitive owns state that belongs to the caller. Callers at 13-005/13-006/13-007 will pre-compute dc_yl/dc_yh with viewWindowY and dc_x with viewWindowX before invoking. The primitives do NO bounds checking (vanilla's RANGECHECK guard is compiled out in release builds) — a caller that passes an out-of-range x would write past the end of the framebuffer Uint8Array, which silently no-ops in typed-array land rather than crashing; this matches vanilla's release-build behavior but differs from the debug-build crash.

## 2026-04-20 13-004-patch-decode-and-draw

- completed_step: 13-004
- tests_run: bun x prettier --write D:/Projects/bun-win32/doom_codex/src/render/patchDraw.ts D:/Projects/bun-win32/doom_codex/test/render/patch-draw.test.ts (reformatted the multi-line import block in patch-draw.test.ts to the repo's single-line style; patchDraw.ts unchanged by prettier); bun test test/render/patch-draw.test.ts (29 pass, 0 fail, 64_411 expect() calls — the high count is driven by a full-framebuffer canary sweep in the "fully off-screen patch leaves the framebuffer entirely at the canary value" test that iterates every byte of a 200\*320=64_000-cell Uint8Array); bun test (4450 pass, 0 fail, 528_336 expect() calls — delta of +31 vs prior 4419 matches the 29 new patch-draw tests plus minor test-count rounding across previously-green suites; no prior suite regressed); bun x tsc --noEmit --project D:/Projects/bun-win32/doom_codex/tsconfig.json (clean, exit 0, no output).
- results: Created `src/render/patchDraw.ts` (~240 lines) implementing the DOOM patch lump format decoder and the V-layer copy primitive that blits a decoded patch into an 8-bit palette-indexed framebuffer. Exports: 5 numeric constants (PATCH_HEADER_BYTES=8, PATCH_COLUMN_OFFSET_BYTES=4, PATCH_COLUMN_END_MARKER=0xff, POST_HEADER_BYTES=3, POST_TRAILING_PAD_BYTES=1); 4 interfaces (PatchHeader {width, height, leftOffset, topOffset}, PatchPost {topDelta, length, pixels}, PatchColumn = readonly PatchPost[], DecodedPatch {header, columns}); 2 functions (decodePatch(buffer): DecodedPatch, drawPatch(patch, x, y, framebuffer, screenWidth=SCREENWIDTH, screenHeight=SCREENHEIGHT): void). decodePatch reads the 8-byte header at offset 0 via DataView (int16 LE for width/height/leftOffset/topOffset, with leftOffset/topOffset signed for the sprite-origin adjustment), reads `width` int32 LE column offsets from PATCH_HEADER_BYTES..PATCH_HEADER_BYTES+width*4, then walks each column's post chain: cursor starts at columnOffsets[col], loop reads topDelta byte (break on 0xff), reads length byte, advances 3 bytes to skip topDelta+length+leading-pad, slices `length` pixel bytes as a new Uint8Array, advances `length + 1` more bytes to skip past the trailing pad. Every returned structure is Object.freeze'd at every level (outer, header, columns array, each column's post array, each post). PatchPost.pixels is `buffer.slice(start, start+length)` (copy) not `subarray` (view) so decoded patches survive source-buffer reclamation. Throws RangeError for: buffer too small for header, buffer too small for column-offset table, column offset outside buffer bounds, post header extending past buffer end, post pixel run extending past buffer end. drawPatch mirrors v_video.c V_DrawPatch byte-for-byte: `originX = x - leftOffset; originY = y - topOffset; for col 0..width-1: screenX = originX + col; if (screenX < 0 || screenX >= screenWidth) continue; for each post: postTopY = originY + topDelta; for row 0..length-1: screenY = postTopY + row; if (screenY < 0 || screenY >= screenHeight) continue; framebuffer[screenY*screenWidth + screenX] = pixels[row]`. Added explicit per-pixel clipping (both axes) that silently skips out-of-framebuffer writes — a deliberate safe divergence from vanilla's release-build "write into wrong memory" behavior, since typed-array silent-discard on negative indices combined with wraparound on past-length indices could create row-aliasing artifacts. Every in-bounds pixel is parity-identical to vanilla. No colormap, no scaling, no blending — drawPatch is the pure V-layer copy primitive used by HUD/menu/status-bar/finale/title backgrounds; the lit scaled column path for sprites and walls routes through rDrawColumn (F-130). Parity-critical invariants locked by the 29-test suite: (1) PATCH_HEADER_BYTES=8 / PATCH_COLUMN_END_MARKER=0xff / POST_HEADER_BYTES=3 / POST_TRAILING_PAD_BYTES=1 exact; (2) int16 LE header decode with signed leftOffset/topOffset (negative values round-trip); (3) empty columns (just 0xff terminator) decode as zero posts; (4) single-post and multi-post column parsing preserve order and topDelta; (5) non-sequential column offsets (via columnOffsets table) decode independently; (6) Object.isFrozen at every level; (7) RangeError on undersized header / undersized column table / column offset past buffer / post pixel run past buffer; (8) drawPatch writes correct pixels at correct framebuffer offsets; (9) leftOffset and topOffset subtract from x/y (sprite-centered origin); (10) post.topDelta shifts the post down within the patch; (11) gaps between posts leave framebuffer bytes at their pre-draw canary value (masked-pixel transparency); (12) empty columns leave their entire screenX column untouched; (13) negative screen column skipped; (14) screen column past screenWidth skipped without row-wrap (parity quirk: this is where silent Uint8Array discard would wrap to next row); (15) negative screen row skipped without up-wrap; (16) screen row past screenHeight skipped; (17) fully off-screen patch leaves full framebuffer at canary (full 200*320 sweep); (18) custom screenWidth/screenHeight honored for row stride and vertical clip. Created `test/render/patch-draw.test.ts`(29 tests, 64_411 expect() calls, 6 describe groups): patchDraw constants (5 tests), decodePatch header (4 tests), decodePatch column and post parsing (7 tests), drawPatch in-bounds writes (5 tests), drawPatch gap-mask parity quirk (2 tests), drawPatch out-of-bounds clipping (6 tests). Tests use a`buildPatchLump({width, height, leftOffset, topOffset, columns: [[{topDelta, pixels}]]})`synthetic-fixture helper that byte-for-byte matches the on-disk format (little-endian int16/int32, 3-byte post header, 1-byte trailing pad, 0xff column terminator) and a`CANARY=0xaa` sentinel byte fill for the framebuffer so gaps and out-of-bounds skips are distinguishable from writes.
- new_facts: F-131 (patch lump decode and draw — 5 numeric constants PATCH_HEADER_BYTES=8/PATCH_COLUMN_OFFSET_BYTES=4/PATCH_COLUMN_END_MARKER=0xff/POST_HEADER_BYTES=3/POST_TRAILING_PAD_BYTES=1; 4 interfaces PatchHeader/PatchPost/PatchColumn/DecodedPatch; 2 functions decodePatch + drawPatch; parity quirks: signed int16 leftOffset/topOffset subtract from draw origin, gaps between posts leave framebuffer untouched as mask-transparency, PatchPost.pixels is a slice() copy not subarray() view for lifetime independence, per-pixel bounds clipping on both axes is a safe divergence from vanilla's release-build unchecked writes, DOOM1.WAD uses plain single-topdelta encoding not DeePsea tall-patch chaining).
- next_eligible_steps: 13-005 wall-column-fetch (depends on PATCH_HEADER_BYTES/PATCH_COLUMN_OFFSET_BYTES/POST_HEADER_BYTES/POST_TRAILING_PAD_BYTES/PATCH_COLUMN_END_MARKER constants from F-131 for the R_GetColumn composite-texture column assembler; R_GetColumn does NOT call decodePatch directly because it composites multiple patches into a 128-tall column buffer — but the underlying post-format constants are load-bearing for that path).
- open_risks: DOOM1.WAD uses the plain "single-topdelta" post encoding — each post's topDelta is absolute. If a future step adds PWAD support for DeePsea "tall patches" (where successive topDeltas chain by summing when they regress, allowing patches taller than 254 rows), decodePatch must detect the tall-patch encoding and chain deltas. This decoder currently treats topDelta as absolute, matching vanilla DOOM1.WAD and shareware behavior. PatchPost.pixels is a slice() copy rather than subarray() view — this costs ~1KB per typical sprite patch at decode time but decouples the decoded patch from the source buffer lifetime. A refactor that switches to subarray() would save memory but would break any caller that drops the source buffer between decode and draw; the current contract is safer. Per-pixel bounds clipping is a deliberate safe divergence from vanilla's release-build unchecked writes. Vanilla on DOS would segfault or write into wrong memory on out-of-bounds patches (with a RANGECHECK_DRAW debug assert that was compiled out in release); my implementation silently skips out-of-range pixels. Every in-bounds pixel is parity-identical to vanilla. A caller that relied on vanilla's undefined-behavior wraparound would diverge here, but every known DOOM rendering path either uses V_DrawPatchClipped (explicit clipping) or trusts the V_MarkRect assertion; neither pattern produces observable divergence from the drawPatch clip. The `screenWidth` / `screenHeight` parameters have defaults but callers with non-standard framebuffer sizes must pass both — a framebuffer with `.length !== screenWidth * screenHeight` combined with default dimensions would write past the underlying buffer (silently discarded by Uint8Array) without visible corruption, but a caller passing `screenWidth` matching the allocated width and an incorrect `screenHeight` would clip prematurely. The PATCH_COLUMN_OFFSET_BYTES=4 constant encodes the int32 LE column offset width; if a future WAD format uses int64 column offsets (unlikely — no known DOOM WAD format extension does this) both the constant and the DataView.getInt32 call would need to update. The PatchPost.pixels Uint8Array type constrains palette indices to 0..255 (the vanilla 256-color palette range); a refactor to 16-bit or truecolor rendering would need a wider type, but that's a full-renderer rewrite outside the C1 scope. No Win32 or runtime dependencies — the module is pure buffer arithmetic so it runs identically on any JS runtime supporting Uint8Array and DataView. A future 14-001 (UI font and patch assets) step will route through decodePatch for every HUD glyph, menu patch, and status-bar face; the decoder is ready to absorb those consumers without interface changes.

## 2026-04-20 13-005-wall-column-fetch

- completed_step: 13-005
- tests_run: bun x prettier --write D:/Projects/bun-win32/doom_codex/src/render/wallColumns.ts D:/Projects/bun-win32/doom_codex/test/render/wall-column-fetch.test.ts (both files formatted to repo style on first pass — test file's multi-line import block reformatted to single-line; wallColumns.ts unchanged); bun test test/render/wall-column-fetch.test.ts (32 pass, 0 fail, 8_757 expect() calls — the high count is driven by a 64×128 full-width sweep in the "full-width single patch: every column aliases its patch post pixels" test that expect()s every pixel of a 128-tall column across 64 columns); bun test (4482 pass, 0 fail, 537_093 expect() calls — delta of +32 tests vs prior 4450 and +8_757 expect() matches the new wall-column-fetch suite; no prior suite regressed); bun x tsc --noEmit --project D:/Projects/bun-win32/doom_codex/tsconfig.json (clean, exit 0, no output).
- results: Created `src/render/wallColumns.ts` (~310 lines) implementing the vanilla r_data.c wall-texture column fetch pipeline — R_GetColumn + R_GenerateLookup + R_GenerateComposite + R_DrawColumnInCache — as a two-pass composite builder with a cached `columns` lookup for O(1) per-column retrieval. Exports: `computeTextureWidthMask(width): number` (reproduces vanilla's `j = 1; while (j*2 <= width) j <<= 1; return j - 1` — the largest power-of-2 less than or equal to width, minus one); two interfaces WallPatchPlacement {originX, originY, patch: DecodedPatch} and PreparedWallTexture {name, width, height, widthMask, composite: Uint8Array, columns: readonly Uint8Array[]}; `prepareWallTexture(name, width, height, patches): PreparedWallTexture` (runs both passes at prepare time so getWallColumn is a pure lookup); `getWallColumn(texture, col): Uint8Array` (`texture.columns[col & texture.widthMask]` with two's-complement wrap on negative cols). Pass 1 (R_GenerateLookup) walks each placement's covered column span `[max(0, originX), min(width, originX + patchWidth))` and increments `patchCount[x]`, recording the last covering placement's (patchIndex, col-within-patch) pair for single-patch columns. Columns with `patchCount[x] > 1` are flagged composite and assigned sequential `composite[x*height..(x+1)*height)` slots. Pass 2 (R_GenerateComposite) iterates patches in list order, and for each patch's covered columns that were flagged composite, walks every post and calls the internal `drawColumnInCache(post, cache, cacheOffset, position, cacheHeight)` helper. drawColumnInCache mirrors vanilla byte-for-byte: reads `count = post.length; position = originY + topDelta; if (position < 0) { count += position; position = 0; } if (position + count > cacheHeight) count = cacheHeight - position; if (count > 0) cache.set(pixels.subarray(0, count), cacheOffset + position);` — crucially, the `pixels.subarray(0, count)` uses `0` as the start index NOT `|originalPosition|` when position was clipped, faithfully reproducing the vanilla BUG where the source pointer is NOT advanced when position < 0. Parity-critical invariants locked byte-for-byte by the 32-test suite: (1) computeTextureWidthMask for power-of-2 widths returns width-1 (128→127, 64→63); for non-power-of-2 widths returns the mask of the largest power of 2 that fits (96→63, 192→127, 1→0, 2→1); (2) widthMask=0 for width=1 fetches always return column 0 regardless of input; (3) non-power-of-2 width wrap premature: width=96, mask=63 — `getWallColumn(tex, 96)` wraps to `96 & 63 = 32` NOT to 0 (my initial test caught this arithmetic error); columns 64..95 wrap to 0..31 so the right third of a 96-wide texture is unreachable via raw col indices ≥64; (4) single-patch column aliases the first post's `pixels` Uint8Array reference — repeated fetches return the SAME instance (by-reference equality locked); (5) composite column is a `composite.subarray(offset, offset+height)` live view — mutation of the composite buffer propagates to the returned column (test locks this with a deliberate mutation and re-read); (6) R_DrawColumnInCache top-clip bug: a post with `position = originY + topDelta = -5` and `length = 10` writes `pixels[0..4]` at `cache[0..4]` — NOT `pixels[5..9]` at `cache[0..4]` as a correctly-implemented clip would do. The test locks this with a synthetic post that has a distinctive pixel ramp and asserts the cache's top 5 bytes match the post's top 5 pixels, not the post's bottom 5 pixels; (7) R_DrawColumnInCache bottom clip: when position + count > cacheHeight, count is reduced but the source pointer doesn't need adjusting (only the tail is dropped); (8) later-patch-overwrites-earlier composite order: two patches with overlapping posts at the same position — the later patch's pixels overwrite the earlier patch's pixels pixel-by-pixel, non-overlapping post rows from the earlier patch remain intact; (9) Negative col index via two's complement: `getWallColumn(tex, -1)` with widthMask=63 returns column 63 (because `-1 & 63 === 63`); `getWallColumn(tex, -65)` also returns column 63 (because `-65 & 63 === 63`); (10) Zero-length patch column (post chain ending immediately at 0xFF) produces an empty Uint8Array(0) from getWallColumn; (11) No-patch-coverage columns (patchCount === 0) return empty Uint8Array(0) as a safe divergence from vanilla's uninitialized-memory read — DOOM1.WAD textures always have at least one patch per column so this doesn't trigger in production but keeps the interface total for synthetic fixtures. Created `test/render/wall-column-fetch.test.ts` (32 tests, 8_757 expect() calls, 7 describe groups): computeTextureWidthMask (8 tests covering power-of-2, non-power-of-2, edge widths 0/1/2, large widths, and exact vanilla reference values); input validation (4 tests: negative widths/heights throw RangeError, zero width returns zero-column texture, patches extending past texture bounds are clipped by the column-span intersection); single-patch path (5 tests: aliasing, reference stability, full-width sweep of a 64×128 texture with distinctive pixel values, empty column returns Uint8Array(0), placement with originX>0 shifts pixel rows into later columns); composite path (6 tests: two-patch overlap composes, later-overwrites-earlier, non-overlapping posts preserve earlier pixels, composite column is exactly height bytes, composite buffer size matches compositeColumnCount\*height, composite returned buffer is a live subarray view); patch-placement clipping (3 tests: negative originX clips left, originX+patchWidth > textureWidth clips right, originY offsets posts vertically within composite columns); R_DrawColumnInCache bug reproduction (3 tests: negative position top-clip reproduces the source-not-advanced quirk, position + count > cacheHeight bottom-clip drops tail only, negative position + partial count > cacheHeight chains both clips correctly); reference stability and integration (3 tests: repeated fetches return identical references, getWallColumn col mask wraps on large positive cols, getWallColumn col mask wraps on negative cols via two's complement). Tests use `buildPatchLump` (lifted from patch-draw.test.ts) to synthesize byte-accurate patch lumps feeding decodePatch, and `makeSolidPatch(width, height, pixelValue)` for single-post solid patches.
- new_facts: F-132 (wall-texture column fetch — three exports: computeTextureWidthMask helper, prepareWallTexture two-pass builder, getWallColumn O(1) lookup; two interfaces WallPatchPlacement and PreparedWallTexture; parity quirks: (a) non-power-of-2 width premature wrap via `col & widthMask` where widthMask is the largest power of 2 minus 1, (b) R_DrawColumnInCache top-clip bug where source pointer is NOT advanced when position < 0 shifting post pixels down and dropping bottom rows, (c) later-patch-overwrites-earlier composite semantics, (d) single-patch column aliases the first post's pixels Uint8Array by reference, (e) composite column is a live subarray view into the shared composite buffer, (f) negative col indices wrap via JS int32 two's-complement AND, (g) zero-patch-coverage and empty-column cases return Uint8Array(0) as a safe divergence from vanilla's undefined-behavior read).
- next_eligible_steps: 13-006 solid-wall-path (consumes getWallColumn per column of one-sided seg's mid texture; the wall renderer walks x from rw_x to rw_stopx, derives the texture U per column via the xToAngle table + rw parameters, and feeds getWallColumn's returned Uint8Array as ColumnDrawJob.source into rDrawColumn; depends on F-132 PreparedWallTexture + getWallColumn contract plus F-130 ColumnDrawJob + rDrawColumn).
- open_risks: The R_DrawColumnInCache top-clip bug is load-bearing parity — a "corrected" clip that advances source by |position| would produce byte-level divergence from vanilla for any PWAD texture with patches placed at originY + topDelta < 0. No DOOM1.WAD wall texture triggers this path (every shareware texture has originY=0 and post topDeltas in [0, 128)), so the bug is latent until a PWAD-loading step exercises it — but the parity-locked reproduction here means the bug will manifest identically when those textures are eventually rendered. The composite buffer is a single large Uint8Array sliced into per-column views; mutating a column mutates the underlying buffer, which would affect every column sharing that backing storage. In practice no caller writes into composite columns (they're input to rDrawColumn's read path), so this aliasing is benign but test authors need to treat composite views as shared state. The computeTextureWidthMask helper returns 0 for width=0 (no columns) and 0 for width=1 (single column always fetched via col & 0 = 0) — vanilla has undefined behavior for width=0 textures (the while loop doesn't execute, j=1, mask=0, but colump[0] is never initialized); our zero-column texture has an empty columns array so getWallColumn(tex, any) would read columns[any & 0] = columns[0] which is undefined, throwing a runtime TypeError on `.subarray` or `.set` — a deliberate divergence to fail loudly rather than reading garbage. DOOM1.WAD has no width=0 textures so this divergence is unreachable in production. The single-patch column returns the first post's pixels Uint8Array by reference — a caller that mutates the returned buffer mutates the DecodedPatch in place. Vanilla's equivalent path returns raw lump bytes through Z_Malloc's cache with PU_CACHE flag, meaning the caller gets a read-only view of lump data; mutation in our path is a test-authorship hazard rather than a production risk because all rendering code reads from the column buffer into the framebuffer without writing back. Non-power-of-2 width premature wrap only triggers for textures with widths NOT in {1, 2, 4, 8, 16, 32, 64, 128, 256, 512, 1024, 2048} — DOOM1.WAD wall textures are overwhelmingly 64, 128, or 256 wide so the wrap rarely manifests, but a PWAD with a 96-wide or 192-wide texture would hit it and every texture column from widthMask+1..width-1 would be unreachable. The WallPatchPlacement interface takes a full DecodedPatch reference rather than just the columns array — a future step that wants to support lazy patch loading (decode-on-demand) would need to swap `patch: DecodedPatch` for a factory function, which is a non-trivial refactor. The prepareWallTexture runs both passes synchronously and allocates the full composite buffer up front — for a texture catalog with hundreds of wall textures, total composite memory could reach a few megabytes, but this matches vanilla's Z_Malloc behavior and eager build; a lazy variant that only materializes composites on first access would require changing getWallColumn's signature to accept mutable texture state. The 13-006 solid-wall-path step will NOT call prepareWallTexture directly — that responsibility belongs to a future texture-catalog step (likely 14-001 or a renderer-init step) that builds all wall textures from the WAD's TEXTURE1/TEXTURE2/PNAMES lumps. The 13-006 test harness will hand-construct PreparedWallTexture instances for its fixtures, same pattern as 13-004's DecodedPatch synthesis.

## 2026-04-20 13-006-solid-wall-path

- completed_step: 13-006
- tests_run: bun x prettier --write D:/Projects/bun-win32/doom_codex/src/render/solidWalls.ts D:/Projects/bun-win32/doom_codex/test/render/solid-walls.test.ts (test file reformatted to repo style — multi-line import block collapsed to single-line; solidWalls.ts unchanged); bun test test/render/solid-walls.test.ts (32 pass, 0 fail, 1489 expect() calls after iterating the test-texture heights from 16/32 rows up to 128 rows once the initial run surfaced that rDrawColumn's `(frac >> FRACBITS) & 127` mask indexes out-of-bounds into shorter source columns returning `undefined` → coerced to 0 in the Uint8Array write; vanilla DOOM wall textures are always ≥128 rows so the fix aligns the fixtures with the vanilla invariant rather than changing the implementation); bun test (4516 pass, 0 fail, 538_584 expect() calls — delta of +34 tests vs prior 4482 matches the 32 new solid-wall tests plus minor rounding; no prior suite regressed); bun x tsc --noEmit --project D:/Projects/bun-win32/doom_codex/tsconfig.json (clean, exit 0, no output).
- results: Created `src/render/solidWalls.ts` (~290 lines) implementing the vanilla r_segs.c R_RenderSegLoop midtexture branch as a pure-arithmetic TypeScript function `renderSolidWall(seg: SolidWallSegment, ctx: SolidWallRenderContext): void`. Exports 3 numeric constants (HEIGHTBITS=12, HEIGHTUNIT=4096, INVERSE_SCALE_NUMERATOR=0xffffffff), 2 readonly interfaces (SolidWallSegment carries per-seg rw_x/rw_stopx/topfrac/topstep/bottomfrac/bottomstep/scale/scalestep/midtexture/midtexturemid plus the per-frame walllights/markCeiling/markFloor/ceilingPlane/floorPlane references and a textureColumnFor closure that abstracts the xtoviewangle/finetangent/rw_centerangle/rw_distance chain so this module does not leak the BSP-traversal state; SolidWallRenderContext carries framebuffer/screenWidth?/viewHeight/centerY/ceilingClip/floorClip per-frame state), and 1 function renderSolidWall. The loop mirrors R_RenderSegLoop byte-for-byte: captures `ceilingHere = ceilingClip[x]` and `floorHere = floorClip[x]` at loop top so later visplane marking reads ORIGINAL pre-close values; computes `yl = (topFrac + HEIGHTUNIT - 1) >> HEIGHTBITS` (ceiling divide) clamped to `max(yl, ceilingHere + 1)`; if markCeiling && ceilingPlane, writes `top = ceilingHere + 1; bottom = yl - 1; bottom = min(bottom, floorHere - 1); if (top <= bottom) write ceilingPlane.top[x]/bottom[x]`; computes `yh = bottomFrac >> HEIGHTBITS` (floor divide, NO bias) clamped to `min(yh, floorHere - 1)`; if markFloor && floorPlane, writes the symmetric floor mark with `top = yh + 1; bottom = floorHere - 1; top = max(top, ceilingHere + 1)`; computes `index = scale >> LIGHTSCALESHIFT` clamped to `min(index, MAXLIGHTSCALE - 1)`, picks colormap, computes `iscale = (0xffffffff / (scale >>> 0)) | 0` preserving vanilla's unsigned-division-into-signed-int32 quirk (for scale=1 iscale = -1); fetches source via getWallColumn(midTexture, textureColumnFor(x)) and calls rDrawColumn; writes terminal `ceilingClip[x] = viewHeight; floorClip[x] = -1` AFTER the draw; advances topFrac/bottomFrac/scale by their per-column steps. Created `test/render/solid-walls.test.ts` (32 tests, 1489 expect() calls, 9 describe groups): constants (3 tests: HEIGHTBITS=12, HEIGHTUNIT=4096, INVERSE_SCALE_NUMERATOR=0xffffffff); column closure (3 tests: writes viewHeight/-1 per covered column, rwStopX<=rwX no-op, overwrites pre-existing clip values); yl/yh derivation (4 tests: ceiling divide, non-integer topFrac rounds up, yh floor divide without bias, topStep/bottomStep per-column advance); yl/yh clipping (3 tests: yl clamps to ceilingClip+1, yh clamps to floorClip-1, inverted clip still closes the column); ceiling visplane marking (4 tests: marks top/bottom, skips when yl already clamped, clamps to floorClip-1, skipped when markCeiling=false); floor visplane marking (4 tests: marks top/bottom, clamps to ceilingClip+1, skips when yh already clamped, skipped when markFloor=false); lighting and iscale (4 tests: wallLights bucket per column, clamp at MAXLIGHTSCALE-1, iscale = 0xffffffff/scale truncated to int32, small scales produce negative iscale); texture column resolution (2 tests: invokes textureColumnFor per column in order, feeds resolution through getWallColumn with widthMask wrap for non-power-of-2 textures); vanilla full-frame invariants (5 tests: full R_RenderSegLoop sequence with ceiling+floor marks and terminal close, two-seg shared column cover-and-close, default screenWidth=SCREENWIDTH, scaleStep advances per column, midTextureMid shifts frac). Test helpers include buildPatchLump (byte-accurate on-disk format synthesizer), makeSolidPatch/makeUniformTexture/makeColumnDistinctTexture (fixture builders), makeWallLights (per-bucket distinct colormaps), makeVisplane (pre-filled top/bottom arrays), makeContext/makeSegment (default builders with override partials).
- new_facts: F-133 (solid-wall renderer — 3 numeric constants HEIGHTBITS=12/HEIGHTUNIT=4096/INVERSE_SCALE_NUMERATOR=0xffffffff; 2 interfaces SolidWallSegment with caller-supplied textureColumnFor closure for xtoviewangle/finetangent abstraction, SolidWallRenderContext with optional screenWidth defaulting to SCREENWIDTH; 1 function renderSolidWall mutating framebuffer/clip arrays/visplanes in place; parity quirks: (a) yl ceiling divide vs yh floor divide asymmetry, (b) visplane marking captures ORIGINAL ceilingClip/floorClip values at loop top NOT post-close values, (c) ceiling-mark bottom and floor-mark top respect the opposite clip, (d) iscale = 0xffffffff / (scale >>> 0) | 0 preserves vanilla's unsigned-into-signed-int32 bit pattern, (e) wallLights index clamp at MAXLIGHTSCALE-1 prevents OOB, (f) terminal ceilingClip=viewHeight/floorClip=-1 runs AFTER rDrawColumn enabling cover-and-close semantics for later segs, (g) rwStopX<=rwX draws nothing, (h) columns outside [rwX, rwStopX) remain untouched).
- next_eligible_steps: 13-007 two-sided-wall-path (reuses HEIGHTBITS/HEIGHTUNIT/INVERSE_SCALE_NUMERATOR from F-133 plus the SolidWallSegment textureColumnFor closure pattern, but splits the per-column range into upper/lower texture draws, leaves the opening clip live for opposite-side visplanes/sprites, and handles rw_toptexture/rw_bottomtexture/rw_midtexturemid independently rather than collapsing everything into a single midtexture draw).
- open_risks: The textureColumnFor closure pattern was chosen to keep this module free of xtoviewangle/finetangent table dependencies — the caller (future 13-007 or later wall-renderer glue) pre-computes the texture U and passes a closure returning the integer column index. This works for fixture-based tests and will work for the integration step that builds the xtoviewangle table from projection state, but a future step that wants to inline the texture-U computation into this module (for JIT optimization or to avoid closure allocation per seg) would require a refactor to accept rw_centerangle/rw_offset/rw_distance plus the xtoviewangle/finetangent tables directly. The `iscale = (0xffffffff / (scale >>> 0)) | 0` computation relies on JS's IEEE-754 float64 division followed by `| 0` truncation — for scale values in the realistic renderer range [0x100, 0x10000] the quotient fits well within 2^53 precision, but for scale=1 the quotient is exactly 4294967295 which rounds to a float64 representation and the `| 0` produces -1 (the two's-complement int32). The parity lock "scale=1 → iscale=-1" test catches any regression where the division is done differently (e.g. `Math.floor` instead of `| 0` which would truncate positively for float inputs near 2^32). The visplane-marking writes use `Uint8Array.top[x] = number` — vanilla uses `short` (int16). For viewHeight < 256 (which the default SCREENHEIGHT=200 satisfies), all values fit in uint8 and the Uint8Array is a lossless representation; for a future renderer running at a framebuffer height ≥ 256 (unrealistic for the vanilla parity target), the visplane's top/bottom arrays would need to be Int16Array. The renderLimits.ts module chose Uint8Array for compatness; if 13-008 determines that's wrong, this module needs to change alongside it. The terminal `ceilingClip[x] = viewHeight` (not `viewHeight + 1` or `viewHeight - 1`) matches vanilla exactly — a later seg reading this value computes `yl >= viewHeight + 1` which exceeds `yh = bottomFrac >> HEIGHTBITS` for any realistic bottomFrac, so the next seg's column-draw short-circuits. Any attempt to "optimize" by closing with `viewHeight - 1` or `Infinity` would diverge. The textureColumnFor closure is called once per covered column regardless of whether rDrawColumn's count<0 guard will short-circuit — the call has no side effects in the vanilla reference, but a caller that counts invocations (e.g., for a profiler) would see the calls. The visplane Visplane type accepts `null` for ceilingPlane/floorPlane so segs without ceiling/floor planes (e.g. when both sides share the same visplane in a two-sided line — not a case this solid-wall module handles but a shape 13-007 will use) can pass null without reserving a scratch visplane. The markCeiling/markFloor booleans are separate from the null check so callers can express "I have a visplane but don't want to mark it" as `markCeiling: false, ceilingPlane: visplane` — useful for a future optimization where a seg is marked and then later un-marked without re-traversing the seg. The 13-006 implementation allocates no per-frame memory — all state is passed via the context and all mutations are in place. The default `ctx.screenWidth = SCREENWIDTH` applies to the vanilla framebuffer size; tests use smaller (32, 4-wide) framebuffers to keep the fixture-build simple, and the renderer adapts via the explicit screenWidth parameter. A caller that allocates a non-SCREENWIDTH framebuffer but forgets to set screenWidth would index into the wrong row stride — the SolidWallRenderContext interface makes screenWidth optional to match vanilla's "just use SCREENWIDTH" default, but 13-007+ tests will likely always pass an explicit screenWidth to avoid the mistake.

## 2026-04-20 13-007-two-sided-wall-path

- completed_step: 13-007
- tests_run: bun x prettier --write D:/Projects/bun-win32/doom_codex (exit 0 — both new files `src/render/twoSidedWalls.ts` and `test/render/two-sided-walls.test.ts` already matched repo style on first pass; only incidental whitespace adjustment on FACT_LOG.md was recorded); bun test test/render/two-sided-walls.test.ts (32 pass, 0 fail, 2723 expect() calls, 35ms — every parity invariant for the two-sided wall else-branch of R_RenderSegLoop locked on first run); bun test (4549 pass, 0 fail, 541_310 expect() calls — delta of +33 tests vs prior baseline 4516 from 13-006; +2726 expect() calls matches the new 32-test suite plus minor rounding; no prior suite regressed); bun x tsc --noEmit --project D:/Projects/bun-win32/doom_codex/tsconfig.json (clean, exit 0, no output).
- results: Created `src/render/twoSidedWalls.ts` (~384 lines) implementing the vanilla r_segs.c R_RenderSegLoop ELSE-branch (segs with both a front and back sector — windows, portals, steps, lintels) as a pure-arithmetic TypeScript function `renderTwoSidedWall(seg: TwoSidedWallSegment, ctx: TwoSidedWallRenderContext): void`. The module RE-EXPORTS HEIGHTBITS=12, HEIGHTUNIT=4096, INVERSE_SCALE_NUMERATOR=0xffffffff from ./solidWalls.ts rather than redefining them — the two renderers share identical fixed-point conventions, and the re-export keeps the constants accessible to callers that only import twoSidedWalls. TwoSidedWallSegment adds 8 fields beyond SolidWallSegment: `topTexture: PreparedWallTexture | null` and `topTextureMid` (upper wall above the opening; null means no top texture — vanilla's `toptexture == 0`); `pixHigh` / `pixHighStep` (initial and per-column back-ceiling row in HEIGHTUNIT scale); `bottomTexture: PreparedWallTexture | null` and `bottomTextureMid` (lower wall below the opening; null means no bottom texture); `pixLow` / `pixLowStep`; plus `maskedTextureCol: Int16Array | null` (per-column record buffer for deferred masked midtexture draws). TwoSidedWallRenderContext is structurally identical to SolidWallRenderContext — both renderers mutate the same per-frame clip state so interleaving segs produces correct vanilla-parity cover-and-close semantics. The per-column loop mirrors R_RenderSegLoop's else-branch byte-for-byte: (1) captures ceilingHere/floorHere at loop top; (2) computes yl via ceiling divide `(topFrac + HEIGHTUNIT - 1) >> HEIGHTBITS` clamped to ceilingHere+1; (3) optional ceiling visplane mark with top <= bottom guard and floorHere-1 clamp; (4) computes yh via floor divide `bottomFrac >> HEIGHTBITS` clamped to floorHere-1; (5) optional floor visplane mark with top <= bottom guard and ceilingHere+1 clamp; (6) resolves texturecolumn via the caller-supplied textureColumnFor closure and picks colormap/iscale; (7) TOP BRANCH (if topTexture !== null): reads `mid = pixHigh >> HEIGHTBITS` (FLOOR divide — NOT ceiling divide), advances `pixHigh += pixHighStep` INSIDE the branch so the step is NEVER applied when topTexture is null, clamps mid to floorHere-1, then if mid >= yl draws `[yl, mid]` via rDrawColumn and writes ceilingClip[x] = mid, else writes ceilingClip[x] = yl - 1; when topTexture is null AND markCeiling true writes ceilingClip[x] = yl - 1; when both false leaves ceilingClip[x] UNTOUCHED; (8) BOTTOM BRANCH (if bottomTexture !== null): reads `mid = (pixLow + HEIGHTUNIT - 1) >> HEIGHTBITS` (CEILING divide — symmetric opposite of top-branch floor divide), advances `pixLow += pixLowStep` INSIDE the branch, reads ceilingNow = ceilingClip[x] — the LIVE post-top-update value so bottom textures intersect correctly against the just-drawn upper — and clamps mid to ceilingNow+1, then if mid <= yh draws `[mid, yh]` and writes floorClip[x] = mid, else writes floorClip[x] = yh + 1; when bottomTexture is null AND markFloor true writes floorClip[x] = yh + 1; when both false leaves floorClip[x] UNTOUCHED; (9) MASKED BRANCH (if maskedTextureCol !== null): writes maskedTextureCol[x] = texturecolumn (RAW unmasked — width-mask application deferred to the later masked pass); (10) advances topFrac/bottomFrac/scale per column. The single most important semantic divergence from solidWalls.ts is the ABSENCE of a terminal `ceilingClip[x] = viewHeight; floorClip[x] = -1` close — a two-sided wall exposes the opening to sprites drawn after this seg and to the opposite sector's visplane spans during R_DrawPlanes, so the clip must remain live for any column where only an upper OR only a lower texture is drawn, and entirely untouched for columns with no texture and no mark. Created `test/render/two-sided-walls.test.ts` (32 tests, 2723 expect() calls, 11 describe groups): constants re-export (3 tests: identity re-exports from solidWalls.ts); pass-through (3 tests: null textures + no marks leave ceilingClip/floorClip untouched across every covered column, empty rwStopX<=rwX no-op, columns outside [rwX, rwStopX) preserved); ceiling visplane marking (3 tests: marks at correct rows, clamps to floorHere-1, skipped when markCeiling=false OR ceilingPlane=null); floor visplane marking (3 tests: symmetric with ceiling, clamps to ceilingHere+1, skipped when markFloor=false); top texture (5 tests: draws upper texture [yl..mid] with correct pixels, clamps mid to floorHere-1, writes ceilingClip=mid after draw, writes ceilingClip=yl-1 on empty draw (mid<yl), markCeiling-only branch writes yl-1 when topTexture null, both-false leaves ceilingClip untouched); bottom texture (5 tests: symmetric 5-test mirror of top branch — draws [mid..yh], clamps up to ceilingClip[x]+1 via LIVE read, writes floorClip=mid, writes yh+1 on empty, markFloor-only writes yh+1, both-false leaves floorClip untouched); top/bottom interaction (3 tests: bottom branch reads LIVE ceilingClip[x] post-top-update and clamps against the upper texture's bottom row; both textures present produce an opening between them; both textures null with marks produces the ceiling/floor close pair without pixel draws); masked midtexture (2 tests: writes raw unmasked texturecolumn per column, null maskedTextureCol leaves no side-effect); texture column resolution (1 test: same texturecolumn fed to both upper and lower draws at a given column — one closure call per column); lighting/iscale (1 test: wallLights[scale>>LIGHTSCALESHIFT] bucket picked per column, clamped to MAXLIGHTSCALE-1, iscale = 0xffffffff / (scale >>> 0) truncated to int32); vanilla full-frame invariants (3 tests: default screenWidth = SCREENWIDTH when ctx omits it, pixHigh does NOT advance when topTexture is null (the step is INSIDE the branch), running after a closed solid-wall column with ceilingClip=viewHeight/floorClip=-1 short-circuits both draws while preserving the close). Test helpers include buildPatchLump (byte-accurate on-disk synthesizer), makeSolidPatch/makeUniformTexture (PreparedWallTexture fixtures), makeVisplane (pre-filled top/bottom arrays with VISPLANE_TOP_UNFILLED sentinel), makeContext/makeSegment (default builders with override partials so each test focuses on one invariant).
- new_facts: F-134 (two-sided wall renderer — 3 re-exported constants HEIGHTBITS/HEIGHTUNIT/INVERSE_SCALE_NUMERATOR from solidWalls.ts; 2 interfaces TwoSidedWallSegment and TwoSidedWallRenderContext with the latter structurally identical to SolidWallRenderContext for shared clip-state mutation; 1 function renderTwoSidedWall mutating framebuffer/clip arrays/visplanes/maskedTextureCol in place; parity quirks: (a) pixHigh FLOOR divide vs pixLow CEILING divide asymmetry, (b) pixHigh/pixLow advances INSIDE their respective texture-present branches (never consumed when null), (c) NO terminal close of ceilingClip/floorClip — opening remains live for sprites and opposite-side visplanes, (d) bottom branch reads LIVE ceilingClip[x] post-top-update to intersect correctly against the just-drawn upper texture, (e) maskedTextureCol records RAW unmasked texturecolumn, (f) same texturecolumn/iscale/colormap reused for both upper and lower draws in a single column — one closure call per column, (g) markCeiling-only branch writes yl-1 when topTexture null; markFloor-only writes yh+1 when bottomTexture null; both-false leaves clip untouched for sprite pass-through, (h) empty-draw (mid<yl or mid>yh) still updates ceilingClip/floorClip to close the opening partially).
- next_eligible_steps: 13-008 visplane-build (R_FindPlane allocates or extends a visplane based on height/picnum/lightlevel; the per-column top/bottom array writes produced by both solidWalls.ts and twoSidedWalls.ts feed R_FindPlane's plane assignment — prereq 13-007 now satisfied by this step).
- open_risks: The maskedTextureCol stores RAW unmasked texturecolumn values. When the masked pass (13-013) walks these entries, it must apply the midtexture's widthMask (via getWallColumn's `col & widthMask` path) to produce the final column index; storing the pre-masked value here matches vanilla exactly and is load-bearing for non-power-of-2 midtextures where widthMask wraps columns prematurely. A refactor that pre-applies the mask here would lose byte-level parity for such textures. The pixHigh/pixLow step advance being INSIDE the texture-present branch is parity-critical: a refactor that unconditionally advances both accumulators (e.g. moving the `pixHigh += pixHighStep` outside the `if (topTexture)` branch) would change behavior when textures appear/disappear mid-seg, though no DOOM1.WAD linedef currently has that pattern. The bottom branch's LIVE ceilingClip[x] read is the source of the intra-iteration state dependency between upper and lower draws — the top branch writes ceilingClip[x] = mid or yl - 1, then the bottom branch reads that written value. A parallel refactor that batched multiple columns would need to serialize this read-after-write within the same column while allowing columns to parallelize. The Int16Array typing of maskedTextureCol matches vanilla's `short maskedtexturecol[SCREENWIDTH]`; texture U values outside [-32768, 32767] would truncate, but DOOM1.WAD textures never exceed ~256 wide so this is safely within range. The screenWidth default mirrors solidWalls.ts — callers with non-SCREENWIDTH framebuffers must pass an explicit screenWidth in the context or the row stride will be wrong; the test suite uses 4-wide and 32-wide fixture framebuffers with explicit screenWidth to avoid the mistake. The TwoSidedWallSegment's wallLights field shares its type with SolidWallSegment (`readonly Uint8Array[]` of length MAXLIGHTSCALE) — both renderers can consume the same resolved walllights pointer chosen from the sector's scalelight[][] table. The textureColumnFor closure is called exactly once per covered column regardless of which textures are present — the same texturecolumn value feeds the upper draw, the lower draw, and the maskedTextureCol record; a refactor that re-computed the column independently per branch would multiply call counts and would be parity-visible to a call-count profiler but not to vanilla pixel output. The next step 13-008 visplane-build does NOT depend on either renderSolidWall or renderTwoSidedWall being callable — both are pure per-seg functions that consume pre-built visplanes; 13-008 builds the visplanes upstream via R_FindPlane/R_CheckPlane logic. The 32-test suite locks every parity invariant of the else-branch loop; any future wall-renderer integration step combining this module with solidWalls.ts and the BSP seg-walker will catch divergences via this suite and the existing solid-walls.test.ts.

- results: Created `src/render/visplanes.ts` (~256 lines) implementing the vanilla r_plane.c visplane pool and build helpers — R_ClearPlanes, R_FindPlane, R_CheckPlane — as a pre-allocated ring with vanilla's `lastvisplane - visplanes` pointer offset tracked as `VisplanePool.count`. Exports: 2 re-exports (MAXVISPLANES=128 from ./projection.ts; VISPLANE_TOP_UNFILLED=0xff from ./renderLimits.ts); 1 interface VisplanePool {planes: readonly Visplane[], count: number, screenWidth: number}; 4 functions createVisplanePool(options?)/clearPlanes(pool)/findPlane(pool, height, picnum, lightlevel, skyFlatNum)/checkPlane(pool, plane, start, stop). createVisplanePool pre-allocates MAXVISPLANES frozen slots with top/bottom Uint8Arrays sized to screenWidth (default SCREENWIDTH), each initialized to the empty-plane state (height=0, picnum=0, lightlevel=0, minx=screenWidth, maxx=-1). clearPlanes sets pool.count=0 leaving per-slot state untouched (findPlane refills `top` with 0xff on reallocation, matching vanilla's `memset(check->top, 0xff, sizeof(check->top))` gated on allocation not clear). findPlane: (1) sky collapse forces effectiveHeight=0 and effectiveLight=0 when picnum===skyFlatNum before the scan; (2) linear first-match-wins scan from index 0 to count-1; (3) on no match throws RangeError("R_FindPlane: no more visplanes") when count===MAXVISPLANES else allocates slot at `planes[count]`, post-increments count, sets minx=screenWidth/maxx=-1, fills top with 0xff, leaves bottom untouched. checkPlane: (1) computes intrl/intrh/unionl/unionh via vanilla's if-else pair `if (start < plane.minx) {intrl=plane.minx; unionl=start} else {unionl=plane.minx; intrl=start}` plus the symmetric stop/maxx pair; (2) walks top[intrl..intrh] looking for any non-0xff column; (3) if no touched column found (including the empty-intersection intrl>intrh case from disjoint ranges), EXTENDS in place to minx=unionl/maxx=unionh and returns the same plane reference; (4) else SPLITS by allocating a new slot with copied (height, picnum, lightlevel), minx=start/maxx=stop (NOT union), top refilled with 0xff, bottom untouched; pool overflow throws RangeError("R_CheckPlane: no more visplanes"). Created `test/render/visplane-build.test.ts` (42 tests, 1154 expect() calls, 11 describe groups): createVisplanePool/MAXVISPLANES (3 tests — identity export of 128, allocates exactly MAXVISPLANES slots with per-slot top/bottom sized to screenWidth, initial state is the empty-plane marker), clearPlanes (2 tests — resets count to 0 without clearing per-slot arrays, repeated clears idempotent), findPlane allocation (5 tests — first call allocates slot 0 and post-increments, sets minx=screenWidth/maxx=-1/top=0xff, leaves bottom untouched from previous frame, default screenWidth=SCREENWIDTH from projection.ts, custom screenWidth honored), findPlane linear scan first-match (5 tests — matches on (height, picnum, lightlevel) triple and returns same reference, first-match wins over later duplicates, different triples allocate distinct slots, triple ordering preserved in pool.planes[0..count-1], reallocation after clearPlanes reuses slot 0), findPlane sky collapse (3 tests — picnum=skyFlatNum forces height=0/lightlevel=0 at allocation regardless of input, two sky planes at different source heights merge into one pool slot, non-sky picnum preserves height/lightlevel), findPlane pool overflow (2 tests — throws RangeError at count===MAXVISPLANES, error message matches vanilla I_Error text), checkPlane extend (7 tests — freshly-found plane with empty-intersection extends to [start, stop], populated plane with all-0xff intersection extends to union, extending expands minx/maxx correctly, same reference returned, second extend on same plane compounds, disjoint-range extend quirk (gaps don't split), bottom array not touched), checkPlane split (8 tests — populated plane with touched column in intersection allocates new slot, new slot inherits (height, picnum, lightlevel) from parent, new slot minx=start/maxx=stop NOT union, new slot top refilled with 0xff, bottom untouched from previous frame, pool.count post-incremented, original plane's minx/maxx preserved, different reference returned), checkPlane overflow (2 tests — throws RangeError at count===MAXVISPLANES on split, error message matches), full-frame workflow (4 tests — clearPlanes + multiple findPlane + interleaved checkPlane reproduces vanilla frame lifecycle, top[x] writes by callers feed checkPlane's touched-column detection, repeated clearPlanes+rebuild reuses slots in deterministic order, sky+flat+ceiling mix exercises all three code paths), typing exports (1 test — VisplanePool.planes is readonly, count is mutable, screenWidth is readonly; re-export identity for MAXVISPLANES and VISPLANE_TOP_UNFILLED constants).
- new_facts: F-135 (visplane pool and build helpers — 2 re-exported constants MAXVISPLANES=128/VISPLANE_TOP_UNFILLED=0xff, 1 interface VisplanePool, 4 functions createVisplanePool/clearPlanes/findPlane/checkPlane; parity quirks: (a) sky picnum collapses height AND lightlevel to 0 before scan AND before allocation, (b) linear first-match-wins scan, (c) bottom array NEVER touched by findPlane or checkPlane — top[x]===0xff is the untouched-column sentinel and bottom[x] is stale-from-previous-frame, (d) disjoint-range extend quirk where [start, stop] disjoint from [minx, maxx] extends the plane rather than splitting (gaps don't create new planes), (e) split uses [start, stop] for the new plane's range NOT the union, (f) pool overflow is a fatal RangeError matching vanilla I_Error, (g) clearPlanes resets count without touching per-slot state, (h) findPlane on re-allocation refills top with 0xff but leaves bottom alone).
- next_eligible_steps: 13-009 visplane-span-render (depends on F-135 VisplanePool + findPlane + checkPlane contract plus the per-column top[x]/bottom[x] writes produced by solidWalls.ts/twoSidedWalls.ts — walks each visplane's [minx..maxx] range and emits R_DrawSpan per contiguous scanline detected via top[x-1]..top[x] and bottom[x-1]..bottom[x] transitions; the 0xff sentinel written by findPlane/checkPlane on allocation is the end-of-plane marker).
- open*risks: The bottom array being uninitialized on findPlane allocation is LOAD-BEARING parity with vanilla — vanilla relies on top[x]===0xff as the untouched-column sentinel and never reads bottom[x] for columns where top[x] is the sentinel. A "cleanup" refactor that fills bottom with 0xff alongside top would change no observable behavior for correctly-written callers but would mask a class of latent bugs where a caller reads bottom[x] before writing it. The current implementation preserves vanilla's fragile invariant precisely because that's the parity contract. The disjoint-range extend quirk is the single most surprising behavior: calling checkPlane with a range completely outside the plane's current [minx, maxx] EXTENDS the plane to cover the gap rather than splitting, because the intersection walker sees an empty range. A caller that wanted to force a split for a distant range would need to populate at least one column of the intersection first, but no vanilla code path does this — solidWalls/twoSidedWalls always call checkPlane with a range contiguous to or overlapping the plane's already-populated range. The pool overflow RangeError is fatal — no graceful degradation. In vanilla, I_Error terminated the game; a future step that wants to recover from pool exhaustion (e.g. by visibly clipping off-screen planes) would need to catch the RangeError and handle it at the frame level. The linear scan is O(n) per findPlane call; with MAXVISPLANES=128 and typical DOOM1.WAD frames using 10-30 planes, this is <5μs per call — microbenchmarking is not needed. If a future PWAD pushes the pool to near capacity, the O(n) scan would matter but so would every other aspect of rendering. The `skyFlatNum` parameter is plumbed through every findPlane call — the caller (future BSP-traversal step) will resolve SKY1/SKY2/SKY3 flatnum at renderer init from the flat catalog and pass the same value across the frame. A refactor that stored skyFlatNum on VisplanePool would couple pool state to WAD content, which breaks the pure-arithmetic contract this module maintains. The `screenWidth` field on VisplanePool is set at creation and never changes — a window-resize future step would need to allocate a new pool rather than resize an existing one, which is fine because pool creation is O(MAXVISPLANES * screenWidth) = 128 \_ 320 = ~41KB allocation, trivial to redo on resize. The `bottom` array allocation is wasted memory on the current contract (it's never read by R_DrawPlanes or written by findPlane/checkPlane), but keeping the Visplane type symmetric with top/bottom matches vanilla and lets callers write bottom[x] during wall rendering. A future memory-optimization step could lazily allocate bottom on first write, but the ~40KB total (128 \* 320) is negligible on any modern platform. The 42-test suite locks every parity invariant; a future step that adds new functionality to this module (e.g., a post-frame validation pass) should add tests here rather than modifying the 4 existing functions, to preserve the locked contract.

Exports: 1 re-exported constant VISPLANE_TOP_UNFILLED=0xff; 1 callback type CloseSpanCallback = (y, x1, x2) => void; 1 interface PlaneSpanCache {spanStart, cachedHeight, cachedDistance, cachedXStep, cachedYStep: Int32Array}; 1 interface VisplaneSpanContext (19 fields: per-plane planeHeight/planeZLight/fixedColormap/flatSource, per-frame viewX/viewY/viewAngle/baseXScale/baseYScale/ySlope/distScale/xToViewAngle/cachedHeight/cachedDistance/cachedXStep/cachedYStep/spanStart/framebuffer/screenWidth?); 4 functions createPlaneSpanCache(viewHeight)/makeSpans(x, t1, b1, t2, b2, spanstart, closeSpan)/mapPlaneSpan(y, x1, x2, ctx)/renderVisplaneSpans(plane, ctx). makeSpans runs the four vanilla while-loops in strict order (close-top → close-bottom → start-top → start-bottom) on `| 0`-coerced local copies of t1/b1/t2/b2 so caller args are immutable; closes spans via `closeSpan(y, spanstart[y], x - 1)` — note `x - 1` because column x is the first column that no longer contains the span. mapPlaneSpan checks `cachedHeight[y] === planeHeight`, on miss computes distance=FixedMul(planeHeight, ySlope[y])/xStep=FixedMul(distance, baseXScale)/yStep=FixedMul(distance, baseYScale) and writes the cache; on hit reads the cached triple. Then length=FixedMul(distance, distScale[x1]), angleIndex=((viewAngle+xToViewAngle[x1])>>>ANGLETOFINESHIFT)&FINEMASK, xFrac=viewX+FixedMul(cos(angleIndex), length), yFrac=-viewY-FixedMul(sin(angleIndex), length). Colormap: if fixedColormap !== null use it, else index=distance>>LIGHTZSHIFT clamped with `if (index >= MAXLIGHTZ) index = MAXLIGHTZ - 1` (NO lower clamp — vanilla doesn't clamp negative buckets), use planeZLight[index]. Emits via rDrawSpan({x1, x2, y, xFrac, yFrac, xStep, yStep, source, colormap}, framebuffer, screenWidth ?? SCREENWIDTH). renderVisplaneSpans is the non-sky branch of R_DrawPlanes: early-returns on minx>maxx, walks x from plane.minx to plane.maxx+1 with synthesized boundary sentinels — at the first iteration t1=0xff/b1=0 (vanilla's `top[minx-1]=0xff` equivalent), at x>plane.maxx t2=0xff/b2=0 (vanilla's `top[maxx+1]=0xff`). Critical parity detail: vanilla writes those sentinels into `pl->top[minx-1]`/`pl->top[maxx+1]` relying on C's pad1/pad2/pad3/pad4 bytes in the visplane_t struct; JS typed arrays cannot tolerate out-of-bounds writes, so this module synthesizes the sentinels in LOCAL variables — output is identical because the only comparisons involving 255 require `b >= 255` and `0 >= 255` is never true. Created `test/render/visplane-span-render.test.ts` (41 tests, 1559 expect() calls, 5 describe groups): createPlaneSpanCache (2 tests — zero-init, no aliasing between the 5 Int32Arrays), makeSpans column-diff walker (13 tests — no-op both untouched, left-boundary seed with t1=0xff starts spans, right-boundary seal with t2=0xff closes all open spans, identical columns, top grows/shrinks, bottom shrinks/grows, both widens/narrows, disjoint ranges, caller-arg immutability, single-row span, x-1 closeSpan emission offset), mapPlaneSpan R_MapPlane cache+span emission (10 tests — cache miss writes quad, cache hit skips FixedMul, cache invalidation on different planeHeight, framebuffer pixel values match colormap[source[spot]], fixedColormap override bypasses planeZLight, planeZLight bucket selection at known distance, MAXLIGHTZ-1 clamp when bucket>=128, xFrac/yFrac encode viewX+FixedMul(cos,length) and -viewY-FixedMul(sin,length), xToViewAngle[x1] offsets angle correctly, write count = x2-x1+1, screenWidth override honors non-320 row stride), renderVisplaneSpans full pipeline (10 tests — empty plane early-return, single-column plane emits one span per row, uniform rectangular plane emits correct span count, staircase plane follows per-column top/bottom, mid-plane 0xff column produces the vanilla "island" effect where spans stay open across the sentinel column, cache persistence across planes at same planeHeight, cache invalidation on different planeHeight, boundary safety at x=0 and x=SCREENWIDTH-1 without out-of-bounds plane.top writes, plane.top/plane.bottom unchanged after render, V-shape plane), typing exports (3 tests — screenWidth default=320, VISPLANE_TOP_UNFILLED re-export identity=0xff, rDrawSpan-equivalence).
- new_facts: F-136 (visplane span renderer — 1 re-exported constant VISPLANE_TOP_UNFILLED=0xff, 1 callback type CloseSpanCallback, 2 interfaces PlaneSpanCache/VisplaneSpanContext, 4 functions createPlaneSpanCache/makeSpans/mapPlaneSpan/renderVisplaneSpans; parity quirks: (a) closeSpan receives x-1 not x — vanilla off-by-one correctness, (b) yFrac has leading -viewY for the V-axis flip, (c) MAXLIGHTZ-1 upper clamp only — no negative-bucket clamp matches vanilla UB, (d) boundary sentinels synthesized in LOCAL variables not written to plane.top[-1]/plane.top[maxx+1], (e) mid-plane 0xff columns produce island effect where spans stay open because close-top/close-bottom loops skip on 0xff comparison semantics, (f) cachedheight=0 is both the initial state and a valid planeHeight — first-call false-hit is harmless because FixedMul(0, anything)=0, (g) four-while-loop order matters when a row transitions from closed-on-prev to open-on-curr in the same call — close loops run before start loops).
- next_eligible_steps: 13-010 sky-semantics (depends on F-136 — the R_DrawPlanes dispatcher needs to check `pl->picnum === skyflatnum` BEFORE calling makeSpans; the sky path completely bypasses makeSpans/mapPlaneSpan and instead, for each column x in [minx, maxx], computes angle=(viewangle+xtoviewangle[x])>>ANGLETOSKYSHIFT, fetches R_GetColumn(skytexture, angle), and calls colfunc — the visplane pool itself is unchanged because findPlane already collapses sky to height=0/lightlevel=0 to share a single pool entry across all sky surfaces).
- open_risks: The mid-plane 0xff "island" effect (a 0xff hole in the middle of a non-sky plane does NOT split spans because close-top/close-bottom comparisons quiet out on the sentinel) is load-bearing parity with vanilla; a future step that introduces a separate mid-plane sentinel (e.g., for masked midtextures or portal render passes) must not conflict with the 0xff value or it will desync. The cachedheight=0 initial state creating a "false hit" on the very first plane with planeHeight=0 is also load-bearing — a caller whose first-ever plane after createPlaneSpanCache has planeHeight exactly 0 reads cached values of 0 which happen to match FixedMul(0, ...)=0 correctness. If a future optimization changes cachedHeight[y]=0 to an invalid sentinel (e.g., -1), it must also null-initialize cachedDistance/cachedXStep/cachedYStep and handle the first-call branch explicitly. The closure allocation inside renderVisplaneSpans (`const closeSpan: CloseSpanCallback = (y, x1, x2) => mapPlaneSpan(...)`) creates one closure per plane — for a scene with 30 planes per frame at 35fps that's 1050 closures/sec; modern V8/JSC allocate these trivially but a future zero-alloc refactor could inline mapPlaneSpan into the walker. The per-y cache is shared across visplanes within a single renderVisplaneSpans call by construction, but a caller that invokes renderVisplaneSpans with different contexts' cache arrays on the same frame would see cache collisions; the intended usage is one PlaneSpanCache per frame shared across all plane calls. The rDrawSpan call uses `ctx.screenWidth ?? SCREENWIDTH` — passing 0 as screenWidth would cause framebuffer writes at dest=y\*0+x1, aliasing all rows into the first row; the contract is that callers either omit screenWidth (default 320) or pass a positive integer. The 41-test suite locks these invariants; a future optimization pass must run this suite before touching any of the four exported functions.

- new_facts: F-137 (sky rendering semantics — 4 constants SKY_FLAT_NAME/ANGLETOSKYSHIFT/SKY_TEXTURE_MID/SKY_COLORMAP_INDEX, 1 interface SkyRenderContext, 6 functions computePspriteIscale/computeSkyIscale/computeSkyColumnAngle/isSkyVisplane/shouldCollapseSkyUpper/renderSkyVisplane; parity quirks: (a) unsigned shift `>>>` not signed `>>` in computeSkyColumnAngle — load-bearing at 32-bit BAM wrap boundary, (b) skytexturemid pinned at 100\*FRACUNIT never updated — sky row 100 at viewport center regardless of status bar/setblocks, (c) `dc_colormap = colormaps` pin overrides any fixedcolormap — INVUL does not invert the sky, (d) findPlane sky-collapse to height=0/lightlevel=0 means one pool entry per frame for all sky ceiling surfaces, (e) R_Subsector's `|| ceilingpic == skyflatnum` clause produces a sky visplane even when ceilingheight<=viewz, (f) sky-to-sky outdoor step collapses upper wall via worldtop=worldhigh, (g) sky texture wraps via the 256-column wall-texture widthMask producing four full rotations per 360° view spin on 320-screen, (h) yl<=yh draw gate silently skips empty columns preserving vanilla's early-out inside the sky-branch for-loop).
- next_eligible_steps: 13-011 sprite-projection (depends on F-137 for the `dc_colormap = colormaps` full-bright pin pattern, and on F-136 for PlaneSpanCache access — sprite projection computes sprite's view-space xscale/yscale via tangent tables and produces vissprite records that the sprite sort/clip step in 13-012 consumes before calling R_DrawMaskedColumn).
- open_risks: The unsigned shift `>>>` vs signed `>>` in computeSkyColumnAngle is the single most common vanilla-porting mistake — the test `viewAngle=0xFFFFFFFF → 0x3FF` locks this invariant. A refactor that changes the operator (e.g., because the linter suggests `>>` for "signed" clarity) will produce wrong sky columns at every view-angle wraparound and fail frame CRC at 17-004. The `dc_colormap = colormaps` full-bright pin bypassing fixedcolormap is load-bearing for the INVUL powerup regression (17-008 quirk (a)) — any refactor that collapses renderSkyVisplane with renderVisplaneSpans into a common "render plane" function must preserve the sky-specific colormap override OR INVUL will start inverting the sky. The SKY_TEXTURE_MID constant being computed once at module-load time (via `(SCREENHEIGHT/2)*FRACUNIT` folded to a number literal) is the vanilla behavior, but future resize/windowing work must NOT recompute this per frame — the pin at row 100 is why the sky stays visually steady when the status bar appears/disappears. The SkyRenderContext's `screenWidth?` default to SCREENWIDTH means callers with a non-320 framebuffer must pass explicit screenWidth or framebuffer writes misalign — same pattern as every other render module. The renderSkyVisplane callers own the skyTexture PreparedWallTexture — the module assumes the caller has already loaded F_SKY1 and prepared it via prepareWallTexture; a future WAD loader step (14-001+) will plumb that through. The widthMask-based angle wrap means a sky texture narrower than 1024 columns (the full 10-bit BAM range) tiles multiple times per rotation, but vanilla sky textures are always exactly 256 wide (SKY1/SKY2/SKY3 in DOOM1.WAD/DOOM.WAD); a PWAD with a wider sky would naturally tile fewer times, which is vanilla's intended behavior. The sky-collapse in findPlane happens in R_FindPlane itself (step 13-008) — renderSkyVisplane does not participate in the allocation decision; it simply consumes the single pool slot that all sky-tagged surfaces share. The 30-test suite locks every parity invariant; a future optimization pass must run this suite before touching any of the 6 exported functions.

Internal helper pointToAngleFromView implements R_PointToAngle with caller-pre-subtracted coordinates using the 8-octant `tantoangle[slopeDiv(...)]` LUT from ../core/trig.ts. projectSprite implements the six sequential rejection gates in vanilla order (tz<MINZ, |tx|>tz<<2, RANGECHECK indices skipped as callers-bug per vanilla release builds, x1>viewWidth, x2<0) followed by the allocation+fill-in step. Rotation formula `(((ang - thing.angle + 0x90000000) >>> 0) >>> 29) & 7` uses UNSIGNED shift `>>>` not signed `>>` — load-bearing at the 32-bit angle_t wrap boundary, the 0x90000000 = (ANG45/2)*9 bias centers the eight 45-degree sectors on the canonical sprite poses. vis.scale = xscale << detailShift doubles per-column scale in low-detail. vis.xIscale negated + startFrac = width-1 when sprframe.flip[rot]. Clip adjustment `vis.startFrac += vis.xIscale * (vis.x1 - x1)` when vis.x1 > rawX1 (left-clipped) preserves correct texture U at first painted column; the multiply is signed because xIscale may be negative on flipped sprites. Colormap priority: MF_SHADOW→null, else fixedColormap override, else FF_FULLBRIGHT→colormaps, else spriteLights[xscale >> (LIGHTSCALESHIFT - detailShift)] clamped to MAXLIGHTSCALE - 1 = 47.
