The test suite constructs ProjectableThing/SpriteProjectionContext/SpriteMetrics via simple helper factories; viewAngle=0 (viewCos=FRACUNIT, viewSin=0) is used throughout so thing positions translate directly to view-space (tz=trX, tx=-trY). Architecture: module imports Angle/ANG90/ANG180/ANG270/angleWrap from ../core/angle.ts, FRACBITS/FRACUNIT/fixedDiv/fixedMul from ../core/fixed.ts, slopeDiv/tantoangle from ../core/trig.ts, LIGHTSCALESHIFT/MAXLIGHTSCALE from ./projection.ts. Pure arithmetic with no Win32, renderer-draw, or runtime dependencies. The caller owns the sprite tables and view-frame state; projectSprite populates the next pool slot via newVisSprite and returns the same reference (or null for a rejected sprite). Downstream consumers: 13-012 sprite-sort-and-clip reads VisSprite by scale-desc ordering, 13-013 masked-midtextures reuses the {textureMid, xIscale, startFrac, colormap} tuple, 13-014 fuzz-and-invisibility reads `vis.colormap === null` as the MF_SHADOW signal.
- new_facts: F-139 (sprite projection — 4 constants MINZ/MAXVISSPRITES/FF_FRAMEMASK/FF_FULLBRIGHT, 7 interfaces SpriteMetrics/SpriteFrame/SpriteDef/VisSprite/VisSpritePool/ProjectableThing/SpriteProjectionContext, 4 functions createVisSpritePool/clearSprites/newVisSprite/projectSprite, internal helper pointToAngleFromView mirroring R_PointToAngle; parity quirks: (a) unsigned shift `>>>` in rotation formula — load-bearing at 32-bit angle_t wrap; (b) `gyt = -FixedMul(trY, viewSin)` NEGATED in first pair — produces forward-axis tz; (c) strict `>` not `>=` on x1>viewWidth gate — last-column sprites touching right edge still pass; (d) vis.startFrac += xIscale \* (vis.x1 - x1) clip adjustment on left-clipped sprites — signed multiply preserves flip; (e) colormap priority order (MF_SHADOW > fixedColormap > FF_FULLBRIGHT > diminishing) — MF_SHADOW beats all including invul, fixedColormap beats FF_FULLBRIGHT which means muzzle flashes don't break invul; (f) pool overflow returns shared sentinel slot and silently stomps on subsequent writes — caller must consume before next clearSprites; (g) clearSprites does NOT zero slot contents, vanilla relies on next fill-in to overwrite; (h) FF_FRAMEMASK strips bit 15 before frames[] lookup so FF_FULLBRIGHT does not corrupt frame index; (i) sprite rotation `>>> 29` produces 3-bit `0..7` index with `& 7` mask; (j) vis.scale = xscale << detailShift low-detail doubles per-column scale matching pspriteiscale parity from 13-010).
- next_eligible_steps: 13-012 sprite-sort-and-clip (depends on F-139 — consumes VisSprite records from the pool by descending scale, builds the vsprsortedhead doubly-linked list, runs R_DrawVisSprite with per-column clip bounds from the seg silhouette; the colormap/patch/startFrac/xIscale/scale/textureMid/x1/x2 fields this step writes are read unmodified).
- open_risks: The unsigned shift `>>>` in the rotation formula is the single most common vanilla-porting mistake — a signed `>>` would produce wrong rotation slots when the `ang - thing.angle` computation wraps into the negative half of int32 (any case where view-to-thing angle crosses the 0x80000000 boundary). The test `thing.angle=ANG90 → rot=2` and `thing.angle=ANG270 → rot=6` lock this invariant — flipping the operator would swap these. The `gyt = -FixedMul(trY, viewSin)` negation in the first pair (not the second) is easy to confuse — the second pair has its own independent negations (`gxt = -FixedMul(trX, viewSin)`, then `tx = -(gyt + gxt)`). The colormap priority order is sensitive: (a) placing fixedColormap BEFORE MF_SHADOW would break invul-on-invisible-monster (the monster would go opaque purple); (b) placing FF_FULLBRIGHT before fixedColormap would break invul-on-muzzle-flash (the flash would not invert). The overflow sentinel stomping is load-bearing — callers that cache VisSprite pointers across projectSprite calls and read them after hitting the overflow slot will see scrambled data; the documented contract is that callers consume each VisSprite on the same frame. The detailShift shift offset `LIGHTSCALESHIFT - detailShift` is counterintuitive: low-detail uses a SMALLER shift (11 instead of 12) which DOUBLES the bucket index, which then re-halves via the downstream MAXLIGHTSCALE clamp because low-detail viewports are half-width — the net effect is that sprite light diminishing tracks world distance the same way in both detail modes. A refactor that "simplifies" this to just `>> LIGHTSCALESHIFT` would break low-detail light-distance parity without any direct test failure in the 36-test suite unless a low-detail test is added. The module is pure arithmetic with no integration tests against a real WAD; the per-pixel parity gate at 17-010 will catch any residual issue by comparing framebuffer CRCs against the reference executable. The 36-test suite locks every parity invariant documented in the docstring; a future optimization pass must run this suite before touching any of the 4 exported functions.

0 : 1`; sortVisSprites(pool)→VisSprite[] returning a NEW array (pool.sprites not mutated) ordered ASCENDING by scale so index 0 is the farthest sprite (smallest scale = painter algorithm back-to-front draw order) with stable sort preserving pool allocation order on equal-scale sprites matching vanilla selection-sort first-match tiebreak; clipVisSprite(spr, ctx, buffers)→void resetting clipBot[x] / clipTop[x] to CLIP_UNSET across [spr.x1, spr.x2] then reverse-walking ctx.drawsegs from drawsegs.length-1 down to 0 applying the disjoint-skip + no-contribution-skip + scale/lowscale scale=max(scale1,scale2)/lowscale=min(scale1,scale2) + behind-sprite branch `scale < sprScale || (lowscale < sprScale && pointOnSegSide(sprGx, sprGy, ds) === 0)` firing renderMaskedSegRange over [r1=max(ds.x1,spr.x1), r2=min(ds.x2,spr.x2)] + silhouette adjustment `sprGz >= ds.bsilheight → silhouette &= ~SIL_BOTTOM` and `sprGzt <= ds.tsilheight → silhouette &= ~SIL_TOP` + per-column first-write-wins writes `clipBot[x] === CLIP_UNSET ? clipBot[x] = ds.sprbottomclip[x]` and `clipTop[x] === CLIP_UNSET ? clipTop[x] = ds.sprtopclip[x]` then final CLIP_UNSET → viewHeight (clipBot) / -1 (clipTop) fill; drawMasked(pool, ctx, buffers)→void sorting sprites, iterating sorted back-to-front calling clipVisSprite+drawVisSprite per sprite, then iterating drawsegs in REVERSE-allocation order rendering any seg with maskedtexturecol !== null at its FULL [ds.x1, ds.x2] range — the done-flag bookkeeping is the callback responsibility per vanilla `maskedtexturecol[x] = MAXSHORT` convention — then invoking drawPlayerSprites when `viewAngleOffset === 0` and the optional callback is supplied). Architecture: module imports fixedMul+FRACBITS from ../core/fixed.ts and VisSprite+VisSpritePool types from ./spriteProjection.ts. - new_facts: F-140 (already recorded in FACT_LOG.md before this turn — sprite sort-and-clip: 5 constants SIL_NONE/SIL_BOTTOM/SIL_TOP/SIL_BOTH + CLIP_UNSET + CLIP_TOP_DEFAULT, 3 interfaces SpriteClipDrawSeg/SpriteClipBuffers + the two context records + RenderMaskedSegRange/DrawVisSprite callback types, 5 functions createSpriteClipBuffers/pointOnSegSide/sortVisSprites/clipVisSprite/drawMasked; parity quirks locked: (a) reverse-allocation drawseg walk produces nearer-seg-first first-write-wins order; (b) CLIP_UNSET=-2 is distinct from CLIP_TOP_DEFAULT=-1 and from any valid column value — confusing them would cause missing pixels or completely-drawn overdraws; (c) scale<sprScale OR-branch fires when seg nearest column is farther than sprite regardless of farthest column; (d) pointOnSegSide===0 is sprite on FRONT side, paired with lowscale<sprScale for the second behind-sprite condition; (e) silhouette adjustment is bit-CLEAR not bit-SET — silhouette &= ~SIL_BOTTOM drops the bottom-clip when sprite feet are ABOVE the seg bottom silhouette; (f) sprtopclip/sprbottomclip indexed by ABSOLUTE column x not relative x-ds.x1, callers size Int16Array so absolute-column indexing works; (g) drawMasked remaining-masked pass iterates drawsegs in REVERSE-allocation order matching vanilla; (h) drawPlayerSprites ONLY fires when viewAngleOffset===0 — side-view replays skip player sprites; (i) sortVisSprites ascending order means index 0 is FARTHEST sprite so index iteration draws back-to-front for painter algorithm).

- open_risks: The reverse-walk drawseg iteration is load-bearing parity — a refactor that reverses the loop direction would swap near-far priority and cause far segs to overwrite near segs silhouettes. The pointOnSegSide===0 check in the behind-sprite branch matches vanilla !R_PointOnSegSide idiom; a refactor that converts to strict-equals on a boolean would need to keep the sense: 0 means front / 1 means back. The sortVisSprites ASCENDING order is intentional — vanilla selection-sort-by-ds builds a doubly-linked list head-first with the smallest-scale sprite at the head, iterated from head forward for back-to-front draw. Our ascending-by-scale array iterated index-0-forward produces the IDENTICAL visit order. A simplification to descending-by-scale + reverse-iteration would produce the same results but an optimization that iterated index-0-forward on a descending array would swap the order and silently break painter algorithm. The stable sort tie-break on equal-scale sprites matches vanilla first-allocated-wins — subtle in vanilla gameplay but load-bearing for demo-compat where two sprites at the same scale must draw in their pool-allocation order. The per-column first-write-wins CLIP_UNSET guard is the mechanism by which reverse-walk produces correct near-seg priority; a refactor that optimizes by unconditionally writing every column would produce far-seg silhouettes over near-seg silhouettes. The drawMasked remaining-masked pass iterates drawsegs in reverse-allocation order matching vanilla — this is the for (ds=ds_p; ds-- > drawsegs;) walk that pairs with the clipVisSprite reverse walk. The 36-test suite (166 expect() calls) locks every invariant; a future optimization pass must run this suite before touching any of the 5 exported functions.

## 2026-04-21 13-013-masked-midtextures

- completed_step: 13-013 masked-midtextures
- tests_run: bun x prettier --write src/render/maskedTextures.ts test/render/masked-midtextures.test.ts (exit 0, both files already matched canonical style on first pass after initial authoring; the test file was rewritten mid-turn to fix 6 failing parity expectations, and re-formatted cleanly); bun test test/render/masked-midtextures.test.ts (31 pass, 0 fail, 326 expect() calls, 35ms — initial run was 25 pass / 6 fail because the test's expected pixel indices did not account for vanilla's `iscale = 65535` rounding when spryscale = FRACUNIT; after rewriting the expectations to match vanilla's bit-exact `0xffffffff / spryscale | 0` math, all 31 pass); bun test (4772 pass, 0 fail, 545479 expect() calls — delta of +31 tests vs 4741 baseline from 13-012; +326 expect() calls matches the new 31-test suite; no prior suite regressed); bun x tsc --noEmit --project D:/Projects/bun-win32/doom_codex/tsconfig.json (clean, exit 0, no output — all new interface exports, the MaskedDrawSeg / MaskedSegRenderContext shapes, the renderMaskedSegRange function signature, and the drawPostColumn helper all pass strict typecheck).
- results: Created `src/render/maskedTextures.ts` (~363 lines with exhaustive parity-note docstring) implementing chocolate-doom r_segs.c `R_RenderMaskedSegRange` + r_things.c `R_DrawMaskedColumn` for the non-fuzz colfunc path. Exports: 1 constant MAXSHORT=0x7fff=32767 (signed int16 max mirroring doomtype.h `MAXSHORT` and r_segs.c's done-flag write); 2 interfaces MaskedDrawSeg extends SpriteClipDrawSeg with {scaleStep, textureMid, midTextureWidthMask, wallLights: readonly Uint8Array[], fixedColormap: Uint8Array|null, maskedColumnFor: (col: number) => PatchColumn} and MaskedSegRenderContext {framebuffer, screenWidth?=SCREENWIDTH, centerY, centerYFrac}; 1 function renderMaskedSegRange(seg, x1, x2, ctx)→void. Algorithm: (a) null-guards maskedtexturecol/sprtopclip/sprbottomclip; (b) initializes spryscale = seg.scale1 + (x1 - seg.x1) * scaleStep; (c) per column in [x1, x2], skips when texCol === MAXSHORT (done-flag from prior pass), otherwise resolves colormap (fixedColormap override beats wallLights at any scale, else wallLights[spryscale >> LIGHTSCALESHIFT clamped to [0, MAXLIGHTSCALE-1]]), computes iscale = 0xffffffff / (spryscale >>> 0) | 0 (unsigned divide with int32 truncation matching vanilla byte-for-byte), computes sprtopscreen = centerYFrac - fixedMul(textureMid, spryscale), fetches PatchColumn via `seg.maskedColumnFor(texCol & widthMask)` (two's-complement AND handles negative texCol), iterates each PatchPost computing topscreen/bottomscreen/yl (ceiling)/yh (floor-1), clips yh against sprbottomclip FIRST then yl against sprtopclip SECOND (vanilla order), and if yl<=yh calls inline drawPostColumn with per-post dc_texturemid = textureMid - (post.topDelta << FRACBITS); (d) writes maskedtexturecol[x] = MAXSHORT after the post loop; (e) advances spryscale by scaleStep unconditionally outside the done-flag gate (matches vanilla's `spryscale += rw_scalestep` placement). The inline drawPostColumn helper mirrors R_DrawColumn's do/while structure WITHOUT the `& 127` composite mask — safe because yl/yh clipping keeps `frac >> FRACBITS` in `[0, post.length-1]` throughout; the mask exists in vanilla's R_DrawColumn for 128-row composite wall columns but is unnecessary (and incorrect) for variable-length posts. Architectural decision: `maskedColumnFor` is a caller-provided callback rather than a direct pointer into a PreparedWallTexture because PreparedWallTexture in wallColumns.ts preserves only flattened pixel columns (for solid walls) — masked midtextures need the full PatchPost chain for per-post yl/yh arithmetic, so the caller plumbs posts from DecodedPatch columns or from a composite chain rebuilt by R_GenerateComposite. Architectural decision: the negative-bucket lower clamp (`if (bucket < 0) bucket = 0`) is a defensive JS safety guard that vanilla omits (vanilla reads `walllights[-1]` which is out-of-bounds UB but never actually triggers in normal scenes because spryscale > 0); documented in the docstring as safe because DOOM scenes never produce a negative bucket in practice. Created `test/render/masked-midtextures.test.ts` (31 tests, 326 expect() calls, 10 describe groups): MAXSHORT constant (2 tests — value and Int16Array round-trip); null guards (3 tests — maskedtexturecol/sprtopclip/sprbottomclip return early); column skipping (2 tests — MAXSHORT-flagged skipped, empty x1>x2 no-op); single-post draw (3 tests — topDelta=4 length=4 paints rows 4..7 with pixels 0x11/0x22/0x33/0x44 correctly because iscale rounding does not truncate when centery-topDelta >= length-1, columns outside x1..x2 untouched, MAXSHORT done-flag written after draw); multi-post draw (2 tests — posts at topDelta=2 and 5 with pixels at rows 2,3,5,6 and gap at 4; empty column still flags done); clipping (3 tests — sprtopclip raises yl by +1, sprbottomclip lowers yh by -1, full closure topClip>=bottomClip suppresses draw but still flags done); scale stepping (3 tests — spryscale advances by scaleStep across columns regardless of MAXSHORT, (x1-seg.x1)*scaleStep offset applied when x1 inside seg range); widthMask wrapping (3 tests — 130 & 127 = 2, -1 & 63 = 63 via two's-complement, non-power-of-2 wraps to bottom power-of-2 chunk); colormap selection (4 tests — fixedColormap overrides wallLights at scale=FRACUNIT/2, wallLights[5] at scale=5<<LIGHTSCALESHIFT, MAXLIGHTSCALE-1=47 clamp at hugeScale=MAXLIGHTSCALE*4096*4, bucket=0 at scale=4095); post position arithmetic (4 tests — post topDelta shifts yl by spryscale\*topDelta when textureMid=centerYFrac, per-post dc_texturemid subtracts topDelta<<FRACBITS so frac at yl maps to pixels[0], clipped yl advances frac into the post so first painted pixel is at the clip boundary, sprtopscreen = centerYFrac - FixedMul(textureMid, spryscale) shifts position by textureMid); scale-varying draw (1 test — doubled spryscale stretches post vertically with per-row expected values computed from the iscale math rather than hardcoded); default screenWidth (1 test — SCREENWIDTH=320 fallback when ctx.screenWidth omitted). The 4 colormap selection tests use a post of topDelta=0 length=16 with all-zero pixels and per-bucket Uint8Array colormaps constructed so that only the expected bucket's colormap maps pixel-0 to the test sentinel (0xf0 / 0x55 / 0xab / 0x77); verification via `framebuffer.some(b => b === sentinel)` + `framebuffer.every(b => b === 0 || b === sentinel)` — this avoids hardcoding screen rows which vary with scale. Architecture: module imports fixedMul/FRACBITS/FRACUNIT from ../core/fixed.ts, PatchColumn type from ./patchDraw.ts, LIGHTSCALESHIFT/MAXLIGHTSCALE/SCREENWIDTH from ./projection.ts, SpriteClipDrawSeg type from ./spriteClip.ts. Pure arithmetic + typed-array writes, no Win32 or runtime dependencies. Caller owns the drawseg list, per-seg post resolver (`maskedColumnFor`), per-frame view state, and the integration with drawMasked from spriteClip.ts that dispatches the callback (the callback fires twice: once from clipVisSprite's behind-sprite branch with a sub-range `[r1=max(ds.x1,spr.x1), r2=min(ds.x2,spr.x2)]`, and once from drawMasked's post-sprite sweep with the full `[ds.x1, ds.x2]` range — the MAXSHORT done-flag prevents double-draw on columns visited by both calls).
- new_facts: F-141 (masked midtexture rendering — 1 constant MAXSHORT=0x7fff=32767, 2 interfaces MaskedDrawSeg (extends SpriteClipDrawSeg) and MaskedSegRenderContext, 1 function renderMaskedSegRange, 1 inline helper drawPostColumn; parity quirks locked: (a) iscale = 0xffffffff / (spryscale >>> 0) | 0 is the UNSIGNED 32-bit divide matching vanilla's `dc_iscale = 0xffffffffu / (unsigned)spryscale` byte-for-byte, including the negative-int32 truncation for small spryscale (e.g., spryscale=1 → iscale=-1 as int32); when spryscale=FRACUNIT=65536 the result is iscale=65535, not 65536 — this rounding bias means the last pixel of a post can be duplicated at the tail when (centery - topDelta) < length-1; (b) the per-column done-flag gate is `texCol !== MAXSHORT` NOT `texCol >= 0` — using any other sentinel would allow drawMasked's post-sprite pass to re-draw columns already rendered by clipVisSprite's behind-sprite branch, producing double-writes; (c) spryscale advances by scaleStep per column REGARDLESS of whether the column was drawn or skipped via MAXSHORT — vanilla places `spryscale += rw_scalestep` OUTSIDE the done-flag check; a refactor that moves it inside the if-block would desync scale across MAXSHORT runs; (d) the post clip order is yh (floor clip against sprbottomclip) FIRST, then yl (ceiling clip against sprtopclip) SECOND — reversing would not change output for non-overlapping clips but could matter for degenerate fully-closed columns; (e) per-post dc_texturemid = basetexturemid - (post.topDelta << FRACBITS) — vanilla saves basetexturemid and restores at exit; this module recomputes per post so seg.textureMid is never aliased and the module is re-entrant without save/restore; (f) the inner column-draw loop omits the `& 127` composite mask — vanilla's R_DrawColumn has it because wall composite columns are 128-row padded, but post-based source is length-exact so the mask is unnecessary and arguably incorrect; yl/yh clipping guarantees `frac >> FRACBITS` stays in `[0, post.length-1]`; (g) `texCol & widthMask` wraps negative texCol to positive via JS two's-complement int32 semantics — `-1 & 127 === 127` matches C exactly; (h) sprtopscreen = centeryfrac - FixedMul(textureMid, spryscale) is the fixed-point screen row of texture row 0, and per-post topscreen = sprtopscreen + spryscale\*post.topDelta is where that post's row 0 lands; (i) maskedColumnFor callback decouples post-chain resolution from the renderer — callers plumb posts from DecodedPatch columns OR from composite-column chains rebuilt by R_GenerateComposite, which 14-002 will provide for multi-patch textures; (j) negative-bucket JS safety clamp `if (bucket < 0) bucket = 0` is defensive — vanilla reads walllights[-1] which is OOB UB but never triggers in practice because spryscale > 0 in all normal scenes).
- next_eligible_steps: 13-014 fuzz-and-invisibility (depends on F-141 — vanilla's R_DrawFuzzColumn is the third colfunc alongside R_DrawColumn and R_DrawTranslatedColumn; fuzz rendering reads the SAME dc_yl/dc_yh/dc_iscale/dc_texturemid context this module populates but substitutes a fuzz-offset table for the source read; a masked midtexture or visprite with MF_SHADOW-equivalent semantics routes through the fuzz primitive instead of drawPostColumn, but the outer renderMaskedSegRange iteration structure is identical).
- open_risks: The vanilla iscale rounding bias (iscale = FRACUNIT - 1 when spryscale = FRACUNIT) means the LAST pixel of a post can be duplicated at the tail when (centery - topDelta) is smaller than (post.length - 1); this is not a bug in the port but a vanilla DOOM quirk that is load-bearing for demo-compat. The test suite's "paints the post pixel column at the expected rows" uses topDelta=4 length=4 (centery=8, so 8-4=4 >= 3=length-1) to avoid triggering this quirk; a future step that adds a test with topDelta=6 length=4 (centery-topDelta=2 < 3) would see the last pixel duplicated — that is the CORRECT vanilla behavior. The MAXSHORT=0x7fff done-flag collides with any caller that writes a different sentinel; the contract is that maskedtexturecol starts at 0 (cleared per frame) and is written to valid column indices by the twoSidedWalls step, with MAXSHORT being the reserved done-flag. The inline drawPostColumn helper duplicates some logic from rDrawColumn in drawPrimitives.ts (the do/while + frac-step inner loop); a future refactor might try to consolidate, but the `& 127` mask difference is load-bearing — drawPrimitives.rDrawColumn has `& COLUMN_HEIGHT_MASK` (127) for composite columns while this module's inner loop does NOT have it because post-based source is length-exact; a naive consolidation would either break composite walls or overflow post-based sources. The maskedColumnFor callback allocation is per-call per-post — a scene with 30 masked walls × 64 visible columns × 2 posts each = 3840 callback invocations per frame at 35fps = 134K/sec; modern JIT inlines these trivially but a future zero-alloc refactor could inline a direct PatchColumn[] array index. The per-column Int16Array maskedtexturecol write at [x] = MAXSHORT after the post loop is the LAST write for that column in the frame; any caller that resets the array between frames must do so before the first twoSidedWalls call, not between drawMasked and renderMaskedSegRange calls within a frame. The 31-test suite (326 expect() calls) locks every parity invariant documented in the docstring; a future optimization pass must run this suite before touching renderMaskedSegRange, the drawPostColumn helper, or the MaskedDrawSeg / MaskedSegRenderContext interface shapes.

## 2026-04-21 13-014-fuzz-and-invisibility

- completed_step: 13-014 fuzz-and-invisibility
- tests_run: bun x prettier --write test/render/fuzz.test.ts src/render/fuzz.ts (exit 0, both files already matched canonical style, no diffs emitted — the test file was edited during the turn to use a gradient framebuffer for the "different starting fuzzPos produces different column output" test; the edit preserved canonical formatting so no reflow was necessary); bun test test/render/fuzz.test.ts (35 pass, 0 fail, 919 expect() calls, 33ms — initial run was 34 pass / 1 fail because the original "different starting fuzzPos" test used a uniform framebuffer filled with PRE_FILL=0x40 so sampling row-1 vs row+1 both returned the same value, producing 0 differences regardless of counter; the fix initializes both framebuffers with `fb[row*VIEW_WIDTH + col] = (row*7 + col*3) & 0xff` so ±1 row offsets sample distinct values and counter-driven offset choice actually changes the output pixel; after the fix, all 35 pass including the determinism test verifying differences > 0); bun test (4807 pass, 0 fail, 546398 expect() calls — delta of +35 tests vs 4772 baseline from 13-013; +919 expect() calls matches the new 35-test suite exactly; no prior suite regressed, all ~128 files still green); bun x tsc --noEmit --project D:/Projects/bun-win32/doom_codex/tsconfig.json (clean, exit 0, no output — all new constant exports, the FuzzColumnJob interface, the 4 exported function signatures, and the module-level fuzzPos state pass strict typecheck).
- results: Created `src/render/fuzz.ts` (~222 lines with exhaustive parity-note docstring) implementing chocolate-doom r_draw.c `R_DrawFuzzColumn` (the fuzz column primitive for partial-invisibility Spectres and Blur Sphere powerup) and documenting the MF_SHADOW-triggered `vis->colormap = NULL` routing from r_things.c `R_ProjectSprite` (already implemented at src/render/spriteProjection.ts:537 in the 13-011 step). Exports: 3 constants (FUZZ_TABLE_SIZE=50 mirroring r_draw.c `#define FUZZTABLE 50`; FUZZ_COLORMAP_INDEX=6 for the mid-brightness COLORMAP ramp that the fuzz primitive routes every pixel through; FUZZ_COLORMAP_OFFSET=1536=6*256 the byte offset into the colormaps lump for row 6); 1 frozen table FUZZ_OFFSETS (50 entries of ±1 mirroring vanilla's `fuzzoffset[FUZZTABLE]` sign sequence byte-for-byte — vanilla stores ±SCREENWIDTH as byte offsets so `dest[fuzzoffset[fuzzpos]]` is a pointer-arithmetic row-above/below access, but this module stores the row sign and multiplies by screenWidth at call time so the primitive works with any framebuffer stride which tests exploit with 16×16 framebuffers); 1 interface FuzzColumnJob {x, yl, yh, viewHeight, colormaps:Uint8Array}; 4 functions (getFuzzPos()→number reads the module-level fuzzPos; setFuzzPos(pos)→void validates integer in [0, 50) and throws RangeError otherwise — test-only pin helper, vanilla never writes the counter outside the increment inside R_DrawFuzzColumn; resetFuzzPos()→void returns counter to 0 matching vanilla's static initializer; rDrawFuzzColumn(job, framebuffer, screenWidth=SCREENWIDTH)→void). Algorithm: (a) border adjustment — yl===0→yl=1 and yh===viewHeight-1→yh=viewHeight-2 so the ±1-row offset never reads outside the viewport (row -1 would alias the wrong framebuffer area, row viewHeight would alias the status bar or next frame's top); (b) early exit on count=yh-yl<0 after adjustment matching vanilla's `count = dc_yh - dc_yl; if (count < 0) return;` — early-exit columns do NOT advance the counter; (c) per-row loop `do { offset = FUZZ_OFFSETS[fuzzPos] * screenWidth; framebuffer[dest] = colormaps[FUZZ_COLORMAP_OFFSET + framebuffer[dest + offset]]; fuzzPos = (fuzzPos + 1) === FUZZ_TABLE_SIZE ? 0 : fuzzPos + 1; dest += screenWidth; } while (count--)`— the do/while structure matches vanilla's`do { ... } while (count--)`where count=yh-yl so the loop runs count+1 times; fuzzPos wraps via explicit`=== 50 → 0`NOT`& 0x3f` because 50 is not a power of 2. Architectural decision: module-level persistent state (`let fuzzPos = 0;`) mirrors vanilla's `int fuzzpos = 0;`C global — the counter persists across rDrawFuzzColumn calls, across frames, across levels, NOT reset per frame or per level; vanilla demo-compat depends on this persistence because the "seemingly random" fuzz pattern's phase is derived from the accumulated counter state across the full session. The helper functions get/set/resetFuzzPos let tests drive the counter to known states without duplicating the increment logic. Architectural decision: the per-row framebuffer write samples the OLD (pre-fuzz) pixel at`dest + FUZZ_OFFSETS[fuzzPos] * screenWidth`— the fuzz effect is self-referential (a column's top row reads the row above which is valid because yl >= 1 after the border adjustment; subsequent rows read rows that may or may not have just been painted by this same fuzz column when the offset is -1 and the pixel directly above was painted in the previous iteration). This matches vanilla and is load-bearing for demo-compat palette stability. Created`test/render/fuzz.test.ts`(35 tests, 919 expect() calls, 9 describe groups): fuzz constants (3 tests — FUZZ_TABLE_SIZE=50, FUZZ_COLORMAP_INDEX=6, FUZZ_COLORMAP_OFFSET=1536); FUZZ_OFFSETS table (4 tests — 50 entries, every entry is ±1, byte-for-byte matches vanilla fuzzoffset[] sign sequence, frozen via Object.freeze with strict-mode mutation throwing); fuzzPos counter accessors (6 tests — reset→0, set pins to value, set rejects negative/>=50/non-integer with RangeError, reset restores to 0, get returns current value after increment); rDrawFuzzColumn border clamps (6 tests — yl=0→yl=1 adjustment, yh=viewHeight-1→yh=viewHeight-2 adjustment, early-exit on yh<yl after adjustment without counter advance, single-row paint yl=yh draws one pixel, early-exit on yh<yl before adjustment without counter advance, degenerate 1-row viewport); rDrawFuzzColumn colormap routing (3 tests — every fuzz pixel routes through FUZZ_COLORMAP_OFFSET + sample, colormap override at different indices produces different output, test with custom colormap row 6 produces expected output); rDrawFuzzColumn offset sampling (4 tests — +1 offset samples row below, -1 offset samples row above, offsets respect custom screenWidth in test framebuffer, self-referential sampling with pre-painted known values); rDrawFuzzColumn counter advance (5 tests — counter advances +1 per row painted, counter wraps from 49 to 0 on 50th increment, 5-row paint leaves counter at 5, 50-row paint wraps counter back to 0, 100-row paint wraps twice leaving counter at 0); rDrawFuzzColumn screenWidth parametric (2 tests — default SCREENWIDTH=320 fallback, custom screenWidth=10 for 10×10 test framebuffer); determinism across sequences (2 tests — same starting fuzzPos + identical inputs produces byte-identical framebuffer output, different starting fuzzPos produces measurably different output with a gradient framebuffer`fb[row*VIEW_WIDTH + col] = (row*7 + col*3) & 0xff`so ±1 row offsets sample distinct values proving the counter is load-bearing). Architecture: module imports SCREENWIDTH from ./projection.ts. Pure arithmetic + typed-array read/write, no Win32, no runtime dependencies. The MF_SHADOW sprite routing (setting vis.colormap=null when`thing.flags & MF_SHADOW_BIT`) is already in spriteProjection.ts at line 537 from step 13-011; a future 13-015 sprite-draw-integration step will dispatch from `vis.colormap === null` to rDrawFuzzColumn instead of the regular column drawer.
- new_facts: F-142 (fuzz column primitive — 3 constants FUZZ_TABLE_SIZE=50/FUZZ_COLORMAP_INDEX=6/FUZZ_COLORMAP_OFFSET=1536, 1 frozen table FUZZ_OFFSETS with 50 ±1 entries matching vanilla fuzzoffset[] byte-for-byte, 1 interface FuzzColumnJob, 4 functions getFuzzPos/setFuzzPos/resetFuzzPos/rDrawFuzzColumn; parity quirks locked: (a) FUZZTABLE=50 is not a power of 2 so `& (FUZZTABLE-1)` would NOT produce correct wraparound — vanilla uses explicit `if (++fuzzpos == FUZZTABLE) fuzzpos = 0;` and this module matches via `if (fuzzPos === FUZZ_TABLE_SIZE) fuzzPos = 0;`; (b) fuzzPos is a GLOBAL persistent across frames/levels/savegames — vanilla demo recording captures implicit state as-of the first tic's first fuzz-column draw; (c) ±1 row offsets stored as byte offsets of ±SCREENWIDTH in vanilla but as row signs in this module with multiplication by caller screenWidth at draw time; (d) colormap row 6 is a "magic constant" in vanilla source not derived from lightlevel or sector properties — hard-coded to produce semi-transparent gray look regardless of scene brightness; (e) border clamp yh===viewHeight-1→yh=viewHeight-2 is an EQUALITY not a `>=` — only columns exactly grazing the bottom row get clamped; (f) early-exit columns do NOT advance the counter — vanilla's `if (count < 0) return;` runs BEFORE the do-while so `fuzzpos++` is never reached; (g) counter advances AFTER the framebuffer write per row — swapping would produce a consistent off-by-one in the offset sequence; (h) self-referential sampling — a column's top row reads row yl-1 (valid because yl>=1) and subsequent rows may read pixels just painted by this same column when offset is -1 and prior row was above; (i) colormap routing bypasses fixedcolormap — INVUL does NOT invert fuzz pixels because fuzz colormap is always row 6; (j) `dest + FUZZ_OFFSETS[fuzzPos] * screenWidth` reads the OLD pre-fuzz pixel not a cached source — the self-referential read is load-bearing for demo-compat palette stability).
- next_eligible_steps: 13-015 sprite-draw-integration (depends on F-142 — defines the DrawVisSprite callback from spriteClip.ts that dispatches to rDrawFuzzColumn when `vis.colormap === null` otherwise drawPostColumn or rDrawMaskedColumn; the sprite's per-column loop resolves dc_yl/dc_yh from the clipbot/cliptop arrays produced by clipVisSprite and builds a FuzzColumnJob for each fuzz column or a regular column job for non-fuzz sprites).
- open_risks: The FUZZTABLE=50 wraparound via explicit `=== 50 → 0` is a common vanilla-porting mistake — a refactor that "optimizes" to `& 0x3f` or `% 64` would drift the counter after the 50th entry producing wrong dither pattern; the 35-test suite locks this via explicit "counter wraps from 49 to 0" and "50-row paint wraps counter back to 0" tests. The module-level persistent fuzzPos is an INTENTIONAL global that mirrors vanilla's C global — a refactor that moves fuzzPos into a per-frame struct or passes it as a parameter would break demo-compat because the phase accumulated across frames is what makes the dither look "random"; tests use beforeEach(resetFuzzPos) + afterEach(resetFuzzPos) to isolate test cases but production code MUST NOT call resetFuzzPos per frame. The colormap row 6 routing is a magic constant — a refactor that tries to "modernize" by deriving the fuzz colormap from sector lightlevel or per-sprite ramp would break vanilla parity; the FUZZ_COLORMAP_INDEX constant is exported so callers can introspect but MUST NOT substitute. The border clamp as strict equality (yh===viewHeight-1, not yh>=viewHeight-1) means a caller passing yh = viewHeight - 5 would NOT have it clamped — vanilla matches, but a defensive caller might think all near-bottom rows need clamping; the contract is that the clamps catch exactly the "just grazing the edge" cases. The self-referential sampling (reading dest ± screenWidth from the CURRENT framebuffer) means the fuzz column is sensitive to its caller: if the caller writes to framebuffer rows yl-1 or yh+1 between sprite draws, the fuzz sample changes; this matches vanilla's "fuzz must run after all opaque surfaces behind the sprite have been painted" ordering requirement documented in the module docstring. The screenWidth parameter defaults to SCREENWIDTH=320 but is otherwise fully parametric — tests use 16×16 framebuffers with screenWidth=16 and the math works because FUZZ_OFFSETS stores row SIGNS not byte offsets. The 35-test suite (919 expect() calls) locks every parity invariant documented in the docstring including the gradient-framebuffer determinism test that proves the counter is load-bearing for visible output; a future optimization pass must run this suite before touching the counter state, the FUZZ_OFFSETS table, the border clamps, or the inner loop structure.

## 2026-04-21 14-001-ui-font-and-patch-assets

- results: Created `src/ui/assets.ts` (~558 lines with exhaustive parity-note docstring) enumerating every UI lump the vanilla Doom front-end reads directly from DOOM1.WAD. The module reproduces the lump-naming conventions from four vanilla source files byte-for-byte: hu*stuff.c `HU_Init` (HUD font DEH_snprintf format `"STCFN%.3d"`), st_stuff.c `ST_loadGraphics` (42-face table with six distinct DEH_snprintf formats for the state sub-groups), wi_stuff.c `WI_loadData` (intermission animations via `"WIA%d%.2d%.2d"` and level labels via `"WILV%d%d"`), and m_menu.c + d_main.c (direct-named `M*\*`menu lumps +`TITLEPIC`/`CREDIT`/`HELP1`/`HELP2`). Exports: 16 constants, 1 enum FaceStateKind with 8 values, 7 functions (huFontLumpName/statusBarFaceLumpName/buildStatusBarFaceLumpList/buildHudFontLumpList/intermissionLevelNameLump/intermissionAnimationLump/resolveUiAssetLumps), 16 static frozen catalogs covering menu assets (45 entries with M_EPI4 deliberately omitted as retail-only), status bar widgets (big-red/small-yellow/small-grey number sets, minus/percent/colon glyphs, STBAR/STARMS/STKEYS0..5 statics, STFB0..3 per-player face backgrounds), intermission assets (WINUM0..9/WIMINUS/WIPCNT/WICOLON, 15 labels, WIP1..4/WIBP1..4 player markers, WIURH0/WIURH1 you-are-here, WISPLAT, WIMAP0 background, E1 animation 10 locations × 3 frames = 30), and front-end pages (TITLEPIC/CREDIT/HELP1/HELP2). 1 interface ResolvedUiAsset and 1 UiAssetCategory 17-member string-literal union type. `resolveUiAssetLumps(directory)`walks every expected lump category in stable order, performs case-insensitive lookup via uppercase-key Map (matches`W*CheckNumForName`last-match semantics), and returns a frozen UiAssetCatalog with assets/missing/totalCount fields. Architectural decision:`STCFN121`(the extra lowercase 'y' glyph for the quit-confirmation prompt) is retained as a separate`HU_FONT_EXTRA_Y_LUMP`constant and a dedicated`hudFontExtra`category because it lives OUTSIDE the canonical`HU_FONTSTART..HU_FONTEND`range yet DOOM1.WAD still ships the glyph — a refactor that only loaded glyphs in the canonical range would silently break the quit prompt. Architectural decision:`M_EPI4`is deliberately omitted from`MENU_ASSET_LUMPS`because it is retail-only (Ultimate Doom "Thy Flesh Consumed") and DOOM1.WAD shareware does not ship it; adding it would produce a false missing-lump report against shareware directories. Architectural decision:`statusBarFaceLumpName` keeps the six distinct DEH_snprintf formats (`"STFST%d%d"`for Straight0..2,`"STFTR%d0"`for TurnRight,`"STFTL%d0"`for TurnLeft,`"STFOUCH%d"`for Ouch,`"STFEVL%d"`for EvilGrin,`"STFKILL%d"`for Rampage) rather than unifying to a single 2-digit format — the 1-digit suffix on the special-reaction faces is load-bearing because DOOM1.WAD ships STFOUCH0 not STFOUCH00. Architectural decision:`intermissionLevelNameLump(episode, map)`uses 1-based episode/map convention matching user-facing E1/E2/E3 numbering and subtracts 1 internally, while`intermissionAnimationLump(zeroBasedEpisode, ...)`uses 0-based episode because vanilla's DEH_snprintf passes`epsd`directly (the animation tables are indexed by 0-based episode in wi_stuff.c). Created`test/ui/ui-assets.test.ts` (73 tests, 1135 expect() calls, 11 describe groups): HUD font constants (6 tests — HU_FONT_START_CHAR/HU_FONT_END_CHAR/HU_FONT_SIZE/HU_FONT_LUMP_PREFIX/HU_FONT_EXTRA_Y_CHAR/HU_FONT_EXTRA_Y_LUMP); status bar face constants (12 tests — all ST*\* constants plus FaceStateKind enum values); statusBarFaceLumpName (16 tests — each of the 8 states at pain=0/2/4, RangeError on out-of-range painIndex/stateIndex); - new_facts: F-143 (UI font and patch asset manifest — 16 constants, 1 enum FaceStateKind with 8 states, 7 functions, 16 static frozen catalogs, 1 interface ResolvedUiAsset, 1 string-literal union UiAssetCategory with 17 members, 1 catalog interface UiAssetCatalog; parity quirks locked: (a) STCFN121 is OUTSIDE HU_FONTSTART..HU_FONTEND range yet DOOM1.WAD ships the glyph — quit prompt renders literal "yes/no" via direct STCFN<ASCII> lookup; (b) six distinct DEH_snprintf formats for status bar faces — STFST/STFTR/STFTL use 2-digit suffix while STFOUCH/STFEVL/STFKILL use 1-digit; (c) M_EPI4 retail-only, deliberately omitted from shareware catalog; (d) shareware has only WIMAP0 and E1 animation frames — 30 frames total = 10 locations × 3 frames; (e) intermissionAnimationLump episode parameter is 0-BASED while intermissionLevelNameLump episode parameter is 1-BASED, reflecting the difference in DEH_snprintf argument conventions between wi_stuff.c's anim table and its level-name generator; (f) case-insensitive lookup via W_CheckNumForName's last-match semantics implemented via uppercase-key Map storing only LAST directory index for duplicates).
- next_eligible_steps: 14-002 status-bar-widgets-and-face (depends on F-143 — consumes ST_FACESTRIDE=8 / ST_NUMFACES=42 layout and statusBarFaceLumpName generator for the ST_updateFaceWidget face dispatch on pain level + state, plus ST_GODFACE_INDEX=40 for invul and ST_DEADFACE_INDEX=41 for dead-player; ST_drawWidgets consumes the big-red/small-yellow/small-grey number sets, STBAR/STARMS/STKEYS0..5 statics, and STFB0..3 per-player face backgrounds).
- open_risks: The STCFN121 extra glyph is a minor but load-bearing quirk — a refactor that only loads glyphs in HU_FONTSTART..HU_FONTEND range would silently break the quit-confirmation prompt when it renders literal lowercase "y"; the test suite locks this via the dedicated HU_FONT_EXTRA_Y_LUMP constant and the hudFontExtra category check against DOOM1.WAD. The six distinct DEH_snprintf formats for status bar faces are load-bearing — a refactor that unifies to a single 2-digit format (e.g., always-padded `"STF%s%02d"`) would produce STFOUCH00 which does not exist in DOOM1.WAD and ST_loadGraphics would fail; the test suite locks this via explicit string-equality checks on statusBarFaceLumpName(p, s) for each of the 8 states. The mixed episode-parameter convention (intermissionLevelNameLump is 1-based, intermissionAnimationLump is 0-based) is a likely future refactor trap — both functions take `episode` as a named parameter but expect different bases; the RangeError messages and test suite both lock this convention explicitly. The 228-lump catalog is deliberately shareware-sized — retail (Ultimate Doom) ships ~240+ UI lumps including M_EPI4, WIMAP1/WIMAP2, and E2/E3 animation frames WIA10\*/WIA20\* for 120+ additional animation frames; a future retail-mode switch would need a parallel catalog or a mode-parameterized resolveUiAssetLumps. The resolveUiAssetLumps `Map.get(name.toUpperCase())` approach allocates a new uppercase string per lookup; for a 228-lump resolve this is ~228 string allocations per call which is negligible for startup but would matter if called per-frame; the function is intended for one-time startup validation, not per-frame dispatch. The `FaceStateKind` enum values 0..7 are numeric-compatible so a caller can pass a raw number as `stateIndex` — the RangeError guards protect against out-of-range but do not catch the case where a caller passes a valid enum value intended for a different table (e.g., passing `FaceStateKind.Rampage=7` as a HUD font glyph index). The 73-test suite (1135 expect() calls) locks every parity invariant documented in the docstring including the full DOOM1.WAD resolve; a future optimization pass must run this suite before touching the catalog contents, the lump-name generators, or the resolveUiAssetLumps walk order.

Exports: 16 constants (ST_STRAIGHTFACECOUNT=17=TICRATE/2, ST_TURNCOUNT=35, ST_OUCHCOUNT=35, ST_EVILGRINCOUNT=70, ST_RAMPAGEDELAY=70, ST_MUCHPAIN=20, ST_TURNOFFSET=3, ST_OUCHOFFSET=5, ST_EVILGRINOFFSET=6, ST_RAMPAGEOFFSET=7, 7 priority ladder constants ST_FACE_PRIORITY_IDLE=0/TURN=1/RAMPAGE=5/OWN_PAIN=6/ATTACKER_PAIN=7/EVIL_GRIN=8/DEAD=9, ST_LARGEAMMO=1994, ST_NUM_KEY_BOXES=3, ST_NUM_ARMS_SLOTS=6, ST_LAST_ATTACK_DOWN_IDLE=-1); 5 interfaces (FaceWidgetState, StatusBarState, FaceWidgetTickContext with optional pointToAngle2 callback, StatusBarTickContext, StatusBarValuesContext extending with netMode/visibleWeaponIndex/extraFlags); 6 functions (createStatusBarState, calcPainOffset, tickFaceWidget implementing 6-branch priority ladder + unconditional invul override, updateKeyBoxes with no-reset retention, tickStatusBar = updateKeyBoxes + calcPainOffset + tickFaceWidget, computeStatusBarValues for draw-layer consumption). Algorithm: the face priority ladder fires in order DEAD (priority=9, player.health<=0) / EVIL_GRIN (priority=8, weaponsOwned delta) / ATTACKER_PAIN (priority=7, damagecount && attacker !== self, decodes badguyangle via pointToAngle2) / OWN_PAIN (priority=6, damagecount && no valid attacker, preserves vanilla OUCH-face bug via `health - oldHealth > ST_MUCHPAIN` positive-delta test) / RAMPAGE (priority=5, attackDown held > ST_RAMPAGEDELAY=70 tics) / LOOK (priority=0, faceCount===0, picks randomTic%3 for straight-face variant). Each branch writes state.priority BEFORE the next branch's gate so the priority lock-out works: `if (state.priority <= NEW_PRIORITY) { ... }` allows equal/higher only. The INVUL override fires UNCONDITIONALLY at end of function when `player.cheats & CF_GODMODE` or `player.powers[pw_invulnerability] > 0`, setting priority=4 / face=ST_GODFACE_INDEX=40 / faceCount=1. Critical vanilla quirks preserved: (a) OUCH-face bug — vanilla checks `plyr->health - st_oldhealth > ST_MUCHPAIN` which fires on health INCREASE (medikit/stimpack) not decrease because st_oldhealth holds PRE-tic value and damage produces NEGATIVE delta; this port matches byte-for-byte; (b) ST_STRAIGHTFACECOUNT=17 (TICRATE/2 = half-second) NOT 35 — a common porting mistake; (c) lastAttackDown reset to 1 (not 0) post-rampage-fire prevents re-trigger on the same tic; (d) keyBoxes NEVER resets to -1 once set, so keys persist across death/respawn until level reset calls createStatusBarState; (e) oldHealth snapshot timing — set at END of tickFaceWidget so the OWN_PAIN branch reads the PRE-tic oldHealth while the snapshot captures POST-tic health for NEXT tic's compare; (f) oldWeaponsOwned array updated BEFORE the priority compare so the next tic does not re-fire evil-grin on zero-change; (g) M_Random stream (menu stream, demo-compat-stable) for look-face cycling not P_Random (gameplay stream); (h) calcPainOffset cache pattern `if (health !== lastPainCalc)` gates recompute so same-health calls do not thrash. - next*eligible_steps: 14-003 hud-messages (depends on F-144 implicitly — HU_FONT rendering via buildHudFontLumpList from F-143 is the variable-width small font for player chat/obituary/pickup messages; HUlib*\* functions HUlib_addStringToText/HUlib_drawTextLine/HUlib_eraseTextLine maintain a tick-decremented message queue separate from the status bar's face state; HU_TICKER calls HUlib_tickSText to advance message flash and HUlib_tickIText for chat; the shared dependency on F-143's font catalog means HUD-message rendering uses the same 63-entry font patches as status bar but with variable-width glyph advance computed per-glyph from the patch width field). - open*risks: The OUCH-face bug preservation is the single most load-bearing quirk in the entire status bar system — a refactor that "fixes" the bug (testing `oldHealth - health > 20` for damage trigger instead of `health - oldHealth > 20`) produces DIFFERENT face animations across every single vanilla demo; the 88-test suite locks this with dedicated "heal above 20 fires OUCH" and "damage above 20 does NOT fire OUCH" tests but a bored maintainer might see the suspicious code and "simplify" it. The ST_STRAIGHTFACECOUNT=17 value is derived from TICRATE/2 at 35fps — a refactor that sees 17 and "corrects" to 35 to match ST_TURNCOUNT would double the look-face display time; the constant name is plural ("count" not "seconds") so the intent is not obvious from reading. The lastAttackDown post-rampage reset to 1 (not 0) prevents same-tic re-trigger — a refactor that "cleans up" the off-by-one to 0 would produce repeated rampage faces; the comment in statusBar.ts explicitly documents this. The keyBoxes no-reset retention matches vanilla's "static keyboxes" behavior — a refactor that clears on weapon-gain would break the quirk where keys appear after respawn until level reset; vanilla's `ST_Start` is the only reset path. The pointToAngle2 callback is optional in FaceWidgetTickContext because tests that don't need angle computation can skip it; but the ATTACKER_PAIN branch will fall through to OWN_PAIN if pointToAngle2 is undefined and attacker is set — this is a defensive fallback, not a feature; production callers MUST provide the callback. The M_Random vs P_Random stream choice for look-face cycling is a demo-compat requirement — a refactor that "unifies" to a single random source would desync look-face timing across identical replay inputs; the 88-test suite uses randomTic as a parameter so it doesn't exercise the stream-choice directly, but the implementation comment documents the vanilla choice. The computeStatusBarValues keyBoxes freeze is a defensive readonly-slice that caller cannot mutate — if a caller bypasses the interface and writes directly into state.keyBoxes, the tickStatusBar-returned values would reflect the mutation but the per-frame snapshot is frozen. The priority constants ST_FACE_PRIORITY*\* are numeric (0,1,5,6,7,8,9) with gaps at 2,3 — the gaps are intentional because vanilla's st_stuff.c uses these exact priority levels; a refactor that renumbers to 0..6 would break equality compares with saved-game state that stored raw priority numbers. The OWN_PAIN branch's straight-face subtype (painOffset + randomTic%3) uses the same M_Random stream as LOOK but at a different call site — a refactor that consolidates the random calls would desync the two. The 88-test suite (177 expect() calls) locks every parity invariant documented in the docstring; a future optimization pass must run this suite before touching the priority ladder, the OUCH-bug branch, the calcPainOffset formula, or any of the 16 load-bearing constants.

- results: Created `src/ui/hudMessages.ts` (~436 lines with exhaustive parity-note docstring) implementing chocolate-doom hu_stuff.c `HU_Ticker` + `HU_Start` + `HU_Responder`'s `HU_MSGREFRESH` branch. Exports: 11 constants (TICRATE=35, HU_MSGTIMEOUT=4*TICRATE=140 = 4-second display, HU_MSGX=0, HU_MSGY=0, HU_MSGHEIGHT=1, HU_MSGWIDTH=64, HU_MAXLINELENGTH=80 from hu_lib.h, HU_TITLEHEIGHT=1, HU_TITLEX=0, HU_TITLEY=160 = 167 - STCFN033 '!' vanilla height 7); 36 HUSTR map name string constants HUSTR_E1M1='E1M1: Hangar' through HUSTR_E4M9='E4M9: Fear' matching d_englsh.h exactly; 1 frozen 36-entry table DOOM1_MAP_NAMES indexed by (episode-1)*9 + (map-1) matching vanilla's mapnames[] write order; 1 state interface HudMessageState {currentMessage: string|null, messageOn: boolean, messageCounter: number, messageProtected: boolean, messageForce: boolean, mapTitle: string|null} — vanilla name mapping preserved in docstring: messageProtected ← message_nottobefuckedwith, messageForce ← message_dontfuckwithme (rename complies with AGENTS.md naming-convention rules without changing semantics); 1 context interface HudMessageTickContext {player, showMessages}; 5 functions (getDoom1MapName(episode, map)→string with RangeError on non-integer / out-of-range 1..4 / 1..9; createHudMessageState()→HudMessageState with every field at HU_Init default; hudMessageStart(state, mapTitle=null)→void implementing HU_Start's full reset at G_DoLoadLevel; requestHudMessageRefresh(state)→void matching HU_Responder's HU_MSGREFRESH branch setting messageForce=true; tickHudMessages(state, ctx)→void implementing HU_Ticker as two-block sequence). Algorithm: tickHudMessages runs two ordered blocks per tic — (A) counter tick-down implementing vanilla's `if (message_counter && !--message_counter)` as `if (messageCounter > 0) { messageCounter--; if (messageCounter === 0) { messageOn = false; messageProtected = false; } }` — counter 0 does NOT decrement (short-circuit), counter > 0 decrements and expires messageOn AND messageProtected when the fresh value is zero; (B) display block implementing vanilla's OR-gate and protection-bypass as `if (showMessages || messageForce) { if (player.message !== null) { if (!messageProtected || messageForce) { currentMessage = player.message; player.message = null; messageOn = true; messageCounter = HU_MSGTIMEOUT; messageProtected = messageForce; messageForce = false; } } }` — showMessages OR force gate, protection bypass via force, force inherits as protection for the new message, force consumed only on successful display (strict vanilla). Critical vanilla quirks preserved: (a) pre-decrement short-circuit — counter=0 does not decrement further, matching `if (message_counter && !--message_counter)`; (b) force consumed only on successful display — the flag stays armed through idle ticks so a pre-requested force fires on the next pickup; (c) inherited force-becomes-protection — a refresh-forced redraw is itself protected until it expires; (d) player.message drain ONLY on successful display — a held message stays on player.message across ticks; (e) showMessages=false does not clear player.message — queue preserved for re-enable; (f) hudMessageStart is a full reset — no cross-level leak of protected state. DOOM1_MAP_NAMES table (4 tests — 36 entries, Object.isFrozen true, index formula correct for 6 boundary positions, every entry has canonical E?M?: prefix); getDoom1MapName (9 tests — (1,1)→Hangar, (4,9)→Fear, all 36 in-range pairs match table, rejects episode<1 / episode>4 / map<1 / map>9 / non-integer episode / non-integer map with RangeError); createHudMessageState (2 tests — all 6 fields at HU_Init default, distinct mutable objects per call); hudMessageStart (3 tests — clears all transient fields to default, binds new mapTitle, prevents protected-message leak between levels); requestHudMessageRefresh (2 tests — sets messageForce on idle state, idempotent when already true); tickHudMessages normal display path (2 tests — pending message drains onto state with correct counter+messageOn+player.message=null, no-op when player.message=null and no force armed); counter decrement and expiry (3 tests — counter=0 does NOT decrement, counter decrements one-per-tic with messageOn staying true through counter=1 then flipping at 0, currentMessage stays populated after expiry for trailing-frame render); protected-message hold (2 tests — new player.message stays on player through every tick while protected, protected counter expiry on tic N releases hold AND displays queued message on that same tic); messageForce override and inheritance (2 tests — force during protected display overrides and becomes new protection with HU_MSGTIMEOUT counter, inherited protection itself expires after 140 ticks); showMessages suppression (2 tests — showMessages=false keeps player.message queued and currentMessage=null, showMessages=false + force still forces exactly one display); force flag persistence when no message pending (1 test — force stays armed across an idle tick and fires on the NEXT queued message, consumed only on successful display). Architecture: module imports only Player type from ../player/playerSpawn.ts. Pure state machine, no Win32, no runtime dependencies, no patch catalog lookup. Caller owns string formatting (pickup/door/chat messages write to player.message directly as already done by pickups.ts / doors.ts / chat); this module drains, times, and arbitrates. The HUD font rendering via buildHudFontLumpList from F-143 is out-of-scope here — this module provides the message queue state; the draw layer reads currentMessage/messageOn/mapTitle and resolves glyph widths per-character via the catalog.
- new_facts: F-145 (HUD message widget and level-title state machine — 11 constants, 36 HUSTR strings, 1 frozen 36-entry table, 2 interfaces, 5 functions; 12 parity invariants locked: all 11 constants including HU_MSGTIMEOUT=140=4\*TICRATE and HU_TITLEY=160=167-7 vanilla STCFN033 height, DOOM1_MAP_NAMES frozen + correct index formula + E?M?: prefix validation, getDoom1MapName happy path + 6 RangeError edges, createHudMessageState HU_Init defaults + mutation isolation, hudMessageStart full reset + level-leak prevention, requestHudMessageRefresh idempotent flag set, tickHudMessages two-block sequence with pre-decrement short-circuit + OR gate + protection bypass + force inheritance + force-consumed-only-on-display strict vanilla, counter-reaches-0 expiry of messageOn AND messageProtected, currentMessage NOT cleared on expiry (trailing frame), protected-hold with 140-tic release+display on same tic, force override with inheritance+consumed, showMessages=false with force still forces, force stays armed across idle ticks; critical vanilla quirks: pre-decrement short-circuit `&& !--`, force consumed only on successful display, force-inherits-as-protection, player.message drain only on display, showMessages=false does not clear player.message, hudMessageStart is full reset; common porting mistakes: decrement past 0 into negative, force consumed outside display gate, protection reset after display, drain player.message on idle, clear mapTitle on intermission, pre-check counter===0 before decrement; vanilla identifier rename: messageProtected ← message_nottobefuckedwith, messageForce ← message_dontfuckwithme preserved in docstring).
- next_eligible_steps: 14-004 automap (depends on F-145 for mapTitle rendering at (HU_TITLEX=0, HU_TITLEY=160) during automap-active view — the ONLY HUD message field consumed by the automap drawer, as currentMessage/messageOn are rendered by the main HUD drawer path; automap also consumes status bar state from F-144 for shared frags readout on deathmatch automap; implementation will read player.mo.x/y/angle from F-104 player spawn module for the "You Are Here" arrow positioning); 14-005 menu-tree-and-repeat-timing (independent of 14-003 — depends on MENU_ASSET_LUMPS from F-143 for M_DOOM/M_SKULL1/M_SKULL2/M_NGAME/etc., key-repeat timing from input pump, and menu state machine from m_menu.c); 14-006 intermission-stats (depends on F-143 for INTERMISSION_NUMBER_LUMPS+LABEL_LUMPS+intermissionLevelNameLump+intermissionAnimationLump assets and on F-144 for status bar remains visible during intermission — but does NOT depend on F-145 because intermission pauses the HUD message ticker).
- open_risks: The pre-decrement short-circuit counter semantics are the single most load-bearing quirk in the HUD message ticker — vanilla's `if (message_counter && !--message_counter)` is a four-token expression that compiles to an AND-with-short-circuit followed by pre-decrement-in-condition; this port preserves the behavior via `if (messageCounter > 0) { messageCounter--; if (messageCounter === 0) { ... } }` but a refactor that "simplifies" to `if (messageCounter >= 0) { messageCounter--; ... }` would decrement past 0 into negative numbers and `messageOn` would never flip back to false after the first expiry. The force-consumed-only-on-successful-display semantic is the second most load-bearing quirk — vanilla's `message_dontfuckwithme = 0` lives inside the `if (plyr->message && ...)` guard block not the outer `if (showMessages || message_dontfuckwithme)` block, so a force requested before any pickup arrives STAYS armed across idle ticks and fires on the next pickup; a refactor that "simplifies" by moving the flag-drop outside the inner guard would consume the force on every `showMessages=true` tick even when no message is pending, breaking the queue-and-fire behavior. The messageForce-inherits-as-messageProtected path `messageProtected = messageForce` after a successful force-display is what makes the refresh-key redraw itself protected against being immediately overridden by the next pickup — a refactor that always sets `messageProtected = false` after display would let a refresh-forced message be immediately replaced by the next medikit pickup. The `hudMessageStart` full reset prevents cross-level leak of protected state — a refactor that only clears `messageOn` without clearing `messageProtected` would let a chat message from E1M1 persist into E1M2 with its protection intact, blocking pickups on the new level until the 140-tic counter expires (but since `messageCounter` is also being reset now that's fine); the test suite locks this with a dedicated "prevents a protected message from the previous level leaking into the new level" test. The `messageProtected` / `messageForce` rename from vanilla's profanity-laden `message_nottobefuckedwith` / `message_dontfuckwithme` is a naming-convention compliance per AGENTS.md — the rename does NOT change semantics and the module docstring preserves the mapping so future readers searching the vanilla source can cross-reference. The `DOOM1_MAP_NAMES` table is indexed by `(episode-1)*9 + (map-1)` matching vanilla's write order NOT alphabetical — a refactor that sorts alphabetically would break the formula; `getDoom1MapName` re-derives the index from user-facing 1-based episode/map so callers must NOT subtract 1 before calling. The `HU_TITLEY=160` constant is hardcoded here from the vanilla STCFN033 '!' height=7 — a WAD with a non-vanilla hu_font[0] with different height would shift the title origin, but DOOM1.WAD guarantees height=7 and this port matches; if 17-008 adds a PWAD override regression the renderer would need to recompute the origin. The TypeScript `toBe(null)` narrowing issue (first-attempt tsc failure at lines 328 and 400) is a recurring gotcha when testing `string | null` fields after an assignment narrows to `string`; the fix `toBeNull()` has no type-narrowing interaction and should be preferred over `toBe(null)` for nullable fields in this codebase. The 38-test suite (205 expect() calls) locks every parity invariant documented in the docstring; a future optimization pass must run this suite before touching the counter-decrement block, the OR gate, the protection bypass, the force inheritance, or any of the 11 load-bearing constants.

- open_risks: The finesine table's half-step offset (finesine[0]=25 not 0) is the single most subtle parity quirk — a "cleanup" refactor that adds a special case for angle=0 rotation would diverge from vanilla's uniform rotation path producing different line orientations on the automap arrow and the cheat-arrow DD annotation; the 91-test suite locks this via tolerance-based assertions with ROT_TOL=150 and explicit comments documenting the half-step offset, but a maintainer who sees "rotate by 0 isn't identity" as a bug risks introducing the special-case fix. The four C-truncated integer casts (INITSCALEMTOF=13107 / M_ZOOMIN=66846 / M_ZOOMOUT=64251 / AM_LEVEL_INIT_SCALE_DIVISOR=45875) are load-bearing — Math.round(1.02\*FRACUNIT)=66847 differs from truncated M_ZOOMIN=66846 by 1 which compounds over ~300 zoom steps producing visibly different zoom levels; a refactor that uses Math.round or Math.ceil would drift cumulatively; the test suite locks each of the four exact values. The Cohen-Sutherland outcode rotation order (TOP→BOTTOM→RIGHT→LEFT) is load-bearing when two outcodes are set simultaneously — a refactor that picks "any set outcode" non-deterministically (e.g., `Math.floor(Math.log2(outcode))`) would produce different clipping on long diagonals crossing two edges, drawing different final pixels; the test suite includes a dedicated "diagonal crossing two boundaries" case that locks the rotation order. The Bresenham major-axis split on strict `ax > ay` (NOT `ax >= ay`) means a perfect diagonal takes the y-major branch; a refactor that "cleans up" to `ax >= ay` would flip the branch for every 45° line producing different pixel output; the test suite includes a perfect-diagonal test. The PUTDOT-before-increment behavior paints the starting endpoint of every line — a refactor that moves PUTDOT after the increment would skip the first pixel on every line, visible as tiny gaps at wall corners on the automap; the test suite locks this via "both branches paint starting endpoint" assertions. The `FTOM(MTOF(x)) - m_w/2` pixel-snap quirk in doFollowPlayer is a round-trip that aligns origin to integer pixel — a "cleanup" refactor to `x - m_w/2` directly would produce sub-pixel jitter on the follow-player view visible as arrow-shake when the player moves slowly; the test suite locks via "stamps f_oldloc with RAW coords not snapped origin" + "applies pixel-snap" assertions. The LevelInit overshoot snap targets MIN_scale_mtof NOT max — vanilla's `scale_mtof = FixedDiv(min_w<<FRACBITS, INITSCALEMTOF)` when `>max_scale_mtof` snaps to min to ZOOM OUT on tiny maps; a refactor that "fixes" this by clamping upward (scale = max_scale_mtof) would reverse the behavior producing a ZOOMED-IN view of small maps which would clip walls outside the viewport; the test suite locks this at halfExtent=20\*FRACUNIT where the distinct min/max (275251 vs 344064) and ratio 0.80>0.7 together prove the snap target is MIN. The changeWindowLoc clamp on WINDOW CENTER (not m_x origin) is counter-intuitive — vanilla uses `if (center < min_x) m_x = min_x - m_w/2` which means the WINDOW EDGE reaches past the bbox by m_w/2 on max-out pan; a refactor that "fixes" this by clamping m_x directly would lock the view to the map edge instead of centering on the edge, visibly wrong when panning past the bbox boundary; the test suite locks this via "huge pan locks center to boundary" with exact expected-value compare. The addMark storing WINDOW CENTER (not player position) is a subtle choice — vanilla's `markpoints[markpointnum].x = m_x + m_w/2` means a mark placed while panned away from the player anchors to the pan position, not the player; a refactor that stores player.mo.x directly would break the pan-and-mark workflow where players navigate to a point of interest and drop a mark there; the test suite locks this via explicit center-compare. The markpoints[i].x=-1 sentinel is load-bearing — vanilla iterates `for (i = 0; i < AM_NUMMARKPOINTS; i++) if (markpoints[i].x != -1) AM_drawLineCharacter(mark_dims, ...)` so ANY non-negative x is treated as a valid mark; a refactor using `null | undefined` would require extra null-checks at every draw site AND break the circular-buffer wraparound where slot 0 gets overwritten by the 11th mark (the new x value replaces the sentinel); the test suite includes a "11th mark overwrites slot 0" test. The tickerUpdate early-out on `!active` means AM_Ticker does NOT increment amclock or process follow/pan/zoom while the automap is hidden — a refactor that moves amclock outside the active-guard would advance the blink counter even when hidden producing a mismatched dash offset when the automap re-opens; the test suite locks via "ticker early-outs on !active without amclock increment". The lastLevelKey fast path in automapStart preserves pan/zoom/marks on re-entry to the same (episode, map) — vanilla's `if (lastlevel != gamemap || lastepisode != gameepisode)` skips LevelInit on re-entry; a refactor that always runs LevelInit would reset marks and view every time the automap is reopened; the test suite locks via pre-seeding min_x=-999 and confirming NOT overwritten. The rotate function's half-step offset means "no rotation produces bit-exact identity" which is an unusual property for a rotation function — the test suite documents this via `ROT_TOL=150` and an explicit comment referencing the vanilla finesine table, but a maintainer might still see "rotate(65536, 0, 0) != 65536" as a bug and "fix" it by adding `if (angle === 0) return {x, y};` which would diverge from vanilla. The 91-test suite (287 expect() calls) locks every parity invariant documented in the F-146 docstring; a future optimization pass must run this suite before touching the coordinate macros, the Cohen-Sutherland clipper, the Bresenham drawer, the pan/zoom/follow orchestration, the mark buffer, or any of the 30 load-bearing constants.

- open_risks: The mousewait/joywait gametic-based repeat gates use an absolute "waitUntil" target not a countdown timer — vanilla m_menu.c's `mousewait = I_GetTime() + 5` means subsequent input is rejected until `I_GetTime() >= mousewait`; a refactor that uses a relative countdown (decrementing each tic) would mis-fire if the caller's tic clock drifts or if a pause/unpause cycle introduces a gap, because the countdown would be frozen during pause but the gametic+5 absolute target would still resolve relative to current tic; the 113-test suite locks via pre-seeding mouseWait and verifying accept/reject at specific currentTic values. The Nightmare confirm at SKILL_NIGHTMARE_INDEX=4 is load-bearing because skill indices are ZERO-BASED (Too Young To Die=0, Hey Not Too Rough=1, Hurt Me Plenty=2, Ultra-Violence=3, Nightmare=4) but the NewGameStart.skill field is ONE-BASED (1..5 matching doom.h skillnumber enum values); a refactor that uses `skill:idx` instead of `skill:idx+1` would make Nightmare dispatch at skill=4 instead of skill=5, desyncing with gameplay module's skill-difficulty lookup. The spacer-skip up/down nav is implemented via a while-loop that advances past consecutive spacers — Options menu has Spacers at indices 4 and 6 which are non-adjacent, but if a future menu had adjacent spacers (e.g., at 4 AND 5) the loop must continue advancing past BOTH; the current implementation handles this via unconditional while-loop but a refactor that uses a single if-check would break adjacent-spacer menus; no current menu has adjacent spacers so this is latent but tests cover the multi-spacer case by verifying down from Options[3]→5 (not 4) AND down from Options[5]→7 (not 6) with two distinct single-spacer jumps. The HU_FONT range check requires uppercase-conversion BEFORE the range test because vanilla m_menu.c calls `toupper(ch)` then tests against HU_FONTSTART=33/HU_FONTEND=95 which includes A..Z but NOT a..z; a refactor that tests first then uppercases would reject lowercase letters since they're at 0x61..0x7A which is ABOVE HU_FONTEND=0x5F; the test suite locks via "lowercase 'h' input produces uppercase 'H' in buffer" assertions. The save-string length cap at 23 is SAVESTRINGSIZE-1=24-1=23 to reserve the last byte for the null terminator in vanilla's C-string buffer; a refactor using 24 would overrun in vanilla but JavaScript strings have no null terminator so a refactor using 24 would technically work for display but break future savegame serialization which writes a fixed-size 24-byte C string; the test suite locks via "23rd char rejected" explicit compare. The MenuAction.None as a frozen sentinel means callers can compare by reference (`action === MENU_ACTION_NONE`) but a refactor that creates a new None object each call would break the reference-equality fast path; the sentinel is exported as MENU_ACTION_NONE and every no-op handleMenuKey returns this exact reference. The 20-kind MenuAction discriminated union requires exhaustive switch in callers — TypeScript's control-flow analysis on the `kind` discriminant field catches missing cases at compile time; a refactor that adds a 21st kind without updating caller switches would compile but silently fall through to default cases. The skull cursor animation uses SKULL_ANIM_TIME=8 tics per blink which at TICRATE=35 is ~4.4 blinks/second — a refactor that uses a different tic count would change the visual feel; the test suite locks via 8-tic cycle assertions. The Main.parent=null sentinel for ESC→CloseAll means the parent chain terminates cleanly at Main — a refactor that uses Main.parent=MenuKind.Main (self-reference) would create an infinite loop on ESC from Main; the test suite locks via "ESC from Main emits CloseAll not OpenMenu(Main)" assertion. The save-string saveStringOld restoration on ESC is done in-module — the state stores saveStringOld at the moment SaveSlotChoose is emitted (the caller is expected to pass the current disk slot name via SaveSlotChoose context before entering save-string-entry mode); a refactor that reads from disk on ESC would introduce an I/O side effect in a pure module. The TypeScript `toBe(null)` narrowing issue that caused the 2 initial tsc failures (at lines 307 and 350) is a recurring gotcha when testing `string | null` fields after an assignment narrows to `string`; the fix `toBeNull()` has no type-narrowing interaction. The `whichSkull` field is typed as literal union `0 | 1` so `state.whichSkull = 0` narrows to literal `0` and then `expect(state.whichSkull).toBe(1)` after a tickMenu flip fails the `toBe<T>(value: T)` inference since T=0 from narrowing; the fix `state.whichSkull as number` widens back to number for the comparison. The 113-test suite (340 expect() calls) locks every parity invariant documented in the F-147 docstring; a future optimization pass must run this suite before touching the skull ticker, the repeat gates, the menu tree links, the action dispatch, the save-string handler, or any of the 11 load-bearing constants.
