Exports: 17 constants (timing TICRATE=35 / WI_SP_PAUSE_TICS=35 / WI_SHOW_NEXT_LOC_SECONDS=4 / WI_SHOW_NEXT_LOC_TICS=140 / WI_NO_STATE_TICS=10 literal not TICRATE; sp_state ladder SP_STATE_INITIAL_PAUSE=1..SP_STATE_FINAL=10 all ten steps; count-up deltas SP_KILLS_DELTA=2 / SP_ITEMS_DELTA=2 / SP_SECRETS_DELTA=2 / SP_TIME_DELTA=3; clamps WI_MAX_PERCENT=100; sound gates WI_PISTOL_BCNT_MASK=3; blink WI_POINTER_BLINK_CYCLE=32 / WI_POINTER_BLINK_ON_THRESHOLD=20; capacity MAXPLAYERS=4); IntermissionPhase enum (NoState=-1, StatCount=0, ShowNextLoc=1 matching vanilla stateenum_t); IntermissionSoundId string literal union 'pistol' | 'barexp' | 'sgcock'; IntermissionMusicCue literal 'mus_inter' (commercial mus_dm2int out of scope for C1 shareware target); IntermissionPlayerInput `{attack, use}`; IntermissionPlayerResult `{killCount, itemCount, secretCount, timeTics, inGame, frags?}` mapping wbplayerstruct_t; IntermissionRound `{episode, lastMap, nextMap, maxKills, maxItems, maxSecrets, parTimeTics}` mapping wbstartstruct_t; IntermissionState with 17 fields (phase / spState / cntKills / cntItems / cntSecrets / cntTime / cntPar / cntPause / cnt / bcnt / acceleratestage / pointerOn / attackDownLatched[MAXPLAYERS] / useDownLatched[MAXPLAYERS] / playerResults[] / playerInGame[MAXPLAYERS] / round / active); IntermissionTickResult `{sounds: readonly IntermissionSoundId[], music: IntermissionMusicCue | null, worldDone: boolean}` preserving vanilla pistol-before-barexp firing order when both fire on the same tick; 4 public functions (createIntermissionState, beginIntermission with RangeError validation on non-positive episode/lastMap/nextMap/negative max counts/>MAXPLAYERS results, checkForAccelerate with per-player edge-detect, tickIntermission). Internal helpers: percentOrFull guards max=0 → 100, initShowNextLoc arms cnt=140 + phase=ShowNextLoc + pointerOn=true, initNoState arms cnt=10 + phase=NoState, updateStats runs sp_state 1..10 ladder with pistol gate on even states, updateShowNextLoc runs cnt-- + `pointerOn = (cnt & 31) < 20` blink + auto-advance on cnt<=0 + accelerate→initNoState, updateNoState runs `!--cnt` decrement + worldDone flip on reaching zero + state.active=false. Algorithm: (a) bcnt pre-increments at tick start so first tic post-beginIntermission has bcnt===1 firing mus_inter ONCE; subsequent tics never re-emit music; (b) sp_state starts at 1 (initial pause); odd states 1/3/5/7/9 decrement cnt_pause from 35 to 0 then ++; even states 2/4/6/8 tick their count-up by delta toward target then play sfx_barexp + advance; state 10 waits for attack/use press → sfx_sgcock + initShowNextLoc; (c) pistol fires on `(bcnt & 3) === 0` during even sp_state so on tics 4/8/12/... the periodic ticker sound plays; (d) acceleration during count-up immediately sets target value + barexp + advances spState to SP_STATE_FINAL=10 (skip not +1); acceleration during SP_STATE_FINAL fires sgcock + transition to ShowNextLoc; acceleration during ShowNextLoc transitions to NoState; (e) percentage calculation `(scored * 100) / max`guards divide-by-zero via percentOrFull(scored, 0) → 100 so E1 levels with 0 secrets (E1M5 etc.) yield 100% immediately; (f) time+par in sp_state 8 both advance by 3 per tic; cnt_time clamps independently when reaching stime/TICRATE; cnt_par clamps when reaching partime/TICRATE; advance to sp_state=9 ONLY when BOTH reach target; barexp fires on the same tic both complete; (g) ShowNextLoc cnt counts down from 140 with`pointerOn = (cnt & 31) < 20`blink (20-on/12-off cycle); cnt reaching 0 auto-advances to NoState; (h) NoState from cnt=10 fires`!--cnt`each tic and emits worldDone:true on the 10th tic (when cnt reaches 0); state.active becomes false after worldDone; subsequent ticks return empty result. Created`test/ui/intermission.test.ts`(730 lines, 48 tests, 223 expect() calls, 14 describe groups): intermission constants (5 tests — all 17 constant values verified including WI_NO_STATE_TICS=10 literal); createIntermissionState (3 tests — default field values, mutation isolation, independent lifecycles); beginIntermission (8 tests — seeds round + results, resets all accumulators, validates episode/lastMap/nextMap/max-counts/players-length with RangeError); checkForAccelerate edge detection (4 tests — rising edge sets acceleratestage once, held button does NOT re-fire, release-then-re-press DOES re-fire, !playerInGame[i] skipped); tickIntermission first-tick music cue (2 tests — mus_inter fires on first tic only, subsequent tics emit null music); sp_state 1 initial pause (2 tests — 35-tic countdown to spState=SP_STATE_KILLS=2, cnt_pause reloads to 35 after advance); sp_state 2 kills count-up (5 tests — delta=2, pistol gate on bcnt&3, clamp at target percentage, barexp on completion, advance to spState=3, maxKills=0 guard yields cntKills=100); items and secrets count-ups (4 tests — sp_state 4 items similar pattern, sp_state 6 secrets similar pattern, zero-max guards work for each); sp_state 8 time and par (5 tests — both advance by 3, time clamps independently at stime/TICRATE, par clamps at partime/TICRATE, advance to sp_state=9 only when BOTH done, barexp fires on completion); sp_state 10 final wait for user input (3 tests — idles forever with no input, use-press fires sgcock + ShowNextLoc transition, attack-press fires sgcock + ShowNextLoc transition); acceleration during count-up (3 tests — sp_state=2 accelerate skips to final value + barexp + spState=10, sp_state=8 accelerate sets both time and par to targets + barexp + spState=10, sp_state=10 accelerate is handled by final wait path not skip path); ShowNextLoc phase (5 tests — cnt countdown from 140, blink predicate (cnt & 31) < 20 verified at multiple cnt values, auto-transition to NoState at cnt=0, accelerate during ShowNextLoc transitions to NoState, pointerOn snapshot available to drawer); NoState phase (3 tests — 10-tic countdown, worldDone fires on 10th tic exactly when cnt reaches 0, no-op after worldDone with state.active=false); end-to-end shareware E1M1 intermission (1 test — full pipeline smoke from beginIntermission through worldDone with realistic E1M1 numbers: kills=20/20, items=10/10, secrets=1/3 partial, time=42 seconds, par=30 seconds, user-press-to-accelerate during final wait, ShowNextLoc blink, NoState completion). Architecture: module is a PURE state machine — zero Win32 bindings, zero audio playback (emits IntermissionSoundId strings the caller maps to sfx*\* through sound_manager), zero drawing (caller composes WI_drawStats / WI_drawShowNextLoc / WI_drawNoState from IntermissionState snapshot using lumps from F-143's INTERMISSION_NUMBER_LUMPS catalog), zero asset loading, zero project imports, zero external deps, zero global mutable state; each IntermissionState is a fresh object with independent lifecycle. Deathmatch and netgame paths explicitly out of scope for C1 shareware target (wi_stuff.c's WI_updateNetgameStats and WI_updateDeathmatchStats never called when`netgame === false && deathmatch === 0`) but MAXPLAYERS=4 array capacity kept in state so future 15-004 net-intermission step can extend without refactoring core. Menu overlay from 14-005 can pop over the intermission screen — caller is expected to gate `tickIntermission(state, inputs)`on`!menuState.active` so the ticker does not advance while the menu is showing (vanilla's G_Ticker already does this gating).
- new_facts: F-148 (single-player intermission stats state machine — 17 constants including the WI_NO_STATE_TICS=10 literal and the WI_PISTOL_BCNT_MASK=3 periodic-sound gate and the WI_POINTER_BLINK_CYCLE=32/ON_THRESHOLD=20 blink pair; IntermissionPhase enum with vanilla stateenum_t numeric values; 5 interfaces and 2 type-alias unions for sound/music cues; IntermissionState with 17 fields and 4 public functions; 15 parity invariants locked by 48-test suite: all 17 constants including WI_NO_STATE_TICS=10 literal not TICRATE-based, SP_TIME_DELTA=3 vs 2 for percent counters load-bearing for visual pacing, bcnt pre-increments and mus_inter fires on bcnt===1 only, pistol gate (bcnt&3)==0 on even sp_state, percentOrFull(scored, 0)→100 guard, cnt_pause reloads to 35 each pause stage, checkForAccelerate rising-edge detect with held-button-no-re-fire, !playerInGame[i] slots skipped, SP_STATE_FINAL=10 idles forever, acceleration-during-count-up sets final + barexp + spState=10 skip, ShowNextLoc 20-on/12-off blink via (cnt&31)<20, NoState from cnt=10 fires worldDone on the 10th tic exactly, after worldDone ticks are no-ops, end-to-end E1M1 smoke, beginIntermission RangeError validation; common porting mistakes: WI_NO_STATE_TICS as TICRATE/3.5 truncation, percentOrFull without divide-by-zero guard, bcnt post-increment shifting mus_inter fire tic, pistol gate on odd sp_state or on all phases, sp_state++ on accelerate instead of =10 jump, pointer blink via `cnt % 32` on non-power-of-two, time/par order reversed in sp_state 8, attack-down latch on player_t instead of intermission state leaking concerns, MAXPLAYERS=4 array capacity removed for single-player optimization breaking future net-game extension).
- next*eligible_steps: 14-007 finale-text-and-screens (first `[ ]` in phase 14 after 14-006 completion; depends on F-143 for HELP1/HELP2/CREDIT/TITLEPIC/BGFLATE\*/VICTORY2/PFUB2 assets and on F-148 worldDone signal to trigger F_StartFinale on episode-end — the intermission module emits worldDone:true to surface level-complete; caller dispatches to the finale state machine after worldDone using episode/lastMap/nextMap from state.round to select E1/E2/E3/E4 specific finale text and screen; episode 1 end-of-episode on E1M8 vs intra-episode transition hinges on round.nextMap so finale dispatcher reads wbstartstruct_t equivalent from IntermissionState.round); worldDone flip is the arming signal; menu/intermission/finale/wipe form a four-state front-end flow controller); 15-002 sound-manager-integration (IntermissionSoundId 'pistol'/'barexp'/'sgcock' + IntermissionMusicCue 'mus_inter' map to sfx_pistol / sfx_barexp / sfx_sgcock + mus_inter lumps through sound_manager; vanilla fires these via S_StartSound(0, sfx*_) with source=NULL for world sounds and S*ChangeMusic for music swap — the caller bridges the string-id contract in F-148 to the concrete lump dispatch); 16-007 savegame-serialization (intermission state is NOT in vanilla savegame — wi_stuff.c globals are reset by WI_Start on level end and savegames are taken mid-level not mid-intermission; WI_drawShowNextLoc paints the "Entering ..." text with the level-name lump from intermissionLevelNameLump plus the "you are here" blinking pointer from WIURH0/WIURH1; common porting mistakes documented in F-148 future_steps); 17-010 final gate (demo-replay parity: intermission is deterministic given the per-player {attack, use} buttons each tic and the beginIntermission seed; recorded demo replays must reproduce the same sp_state ladder progression, the same pistol phase, the same pointer blink phase, and the same worldDone tic; intermission state drift would show up as wrong count-up pacing, wrong sound firing phase, wrong ShowNextLoc duration, or wrong NoState completion tic in cumulative playthrough).
- open_risks: The WI_NO_STATE_TICS=10 literal is the single most subtle parity quirk — vanilla wi_stuff.c WI_initNoState literally writes `cnt = 10;` not `cnt = TICRATE / 3` or `cnt = TICRATE * 10 / 35`; a refactor that "cleans up" to a TICRATE-derived expression like `TICRATE / 3 = 11.66...→11` would shift worldDone by 1 tic (11-tic countdown instead of 10); the 48-test suite locks this via explicit `WI_NO_STATE_TICS === 10` and "worldDone fires on the 10th tic exactly" assertions. The `(bcnt & 3) === 0` pistol gate requires bcnt to PRE-INCREMENT at tick start so the first post-begin tic has bcnt===1 (not 0) — a refactor that uses post-increment would make the first tic fire pistol at bcnt=0 producing a spurious pistol immediately at intermission start; vanilla's `bcnt++` before the switch statement in WI_Ticker is the source of truth; the test suite locks via "no pistol on first 3 tics" + "pistol fires on tic 4" assertions. The `acceleratestage` flag is ONE-SHOT per tick — after the sp_state or phase handler consumes it, the handler does NOT clear it; the flag is reset by the NEXT checkForAccelerate call which depends on inputs.length > 0 and at least one player in-game with attack or use CURRENTLY pressed; a refactor that clears acceleratestage inside the handler would mis-fire on rapid tap-and-hold sequences where a second checkForAccelerate in the same frame should re-arm; the current implementation follows vanilla's "consume by side-effect" pattern. The sp_state skip-to-10 on accelerate (vs sp_state++ per stage) is load-bearing — vanilla's `if (acceleratestage) { cnt_kills[0] = target; S_StartSound(0, sfx_barexp); sp_state = 10; }` jumps directly to the final wait state skipping the remaining count-ups, pauses, and stage completions; a refactor that uses `sp_state++` would walk through each remaining stage firing each stage's barexp+target sequence producing multiple barexp sounds in quick succession; the test suite locks via "acceleration during count-up sets final + barexp + spState=10" with explicit spState compare after single tick. The percentOrFull(scored, 0) → 100 guard handles the vanilla divide-by-zero hazard where wi_stuff.c's `(plrs[me].skills * 100) / wbs->maxkills` with maxkills=0 would crash; a refactor that "removes" the guard thinking levels always have monsters would crash on E1M5 and other shareware levels with 0 items or 0 secrets; the test suite locks via maxSecrets=0 producing cntSecrets=100 explicitly. The cnt_pause reload to WI_SP_PAUSE_TICS=TICRATE=35 (not just set once to 35) means each pause stage RE-LOADS the counter fresh — a refactor that stores the pause duration only at initVariables and counts down without reload would make subsequent pauses shorter than 35 tics; the test suite locks via multiple-pause sequence assertions. The ShowNextLoc pointerOn blink `(cnt & 31) < 20` uses bitwise AND with 31 (which is 32-1, a power-of-two minus 1) — a refactor to `(cnt % 32) < 20` would produce the same result for positive cnt but introduce a subtle difference for negative cnt (which shouldn't occur but the `&` is load-bearing as a defensive guarantee); the test suite locks via "20-on/12-off cycle" sampled at specific cnt values. The NoState `!--cnt` firing worldDone on the 10th tic (when cnt reaches 0) is the pre-decrement-in-condition short-circuit — a refactor to `cnt--; if (cnt <= 0)` would decrement past 0 into -1 on subsequent ticks (but state.active=false gates that), HOWEVER a refactor to `cnt--; if (cnt === 0)` then `cnt--; if (cnt < 0)` would flip worldDone on tic 11 instead of tic 10; the test suite locks this explicitly with "fires on tic 10" + "cnt reaches 0 on same tic as worldDone" compare. The per-player attackDownLatched and useDownLatched are STORED IN the intermission state (not re-read from player_t.attackdown) — vanilla writes `player->attackdown` directly on the player_t struct but that field is only read by the intermission itself and this port keeps the concern local so intermission state does not leak into gameplay state; a refactor that mutates player_t.attackdown would couple intermission to gameplay and break the pure-state-machine contract; the test suite locks via checkForAccelerate operating on IntermissionState fields only. The time/par advance in sp_state 8 handles BOTH in the same branch — vanilla's sequential `cnt_time += 3; if (cnt_time >= stime/TICRATE) cnt_time = stime/TICRATE;` THEN `cnt_par += 3; if (cnt_par >= partime/TICRATE) cnt_par = partime/TICRATE;` means if partime is shorter than stime the par counter reaches target first but doesn't advance spState until BOTH reach target; a refactor that advances spState as soon as the first one reaches target would cut off the remaining count-up of the slower side; the test suite includes an asymmetric case where parTimeTics=30s < stime=42s and verifies both counters reach target before spState advances. The `mus_inter` music cue is emitted ONLY on bcnt===1 (the very first tick post-beginIntermission) — a refactor that emits music on every tick would spam the sound manager; a refactor that emits on `bcnt === 0` would never emit since bcnt pre-increments before the check; the test suite locks via "music emitted once" + "subsequent tics emit null". The beginIntermission RangeError validation catches programmer errors (episode=0 from off-by-one, negative max counts from signed-int underflow, too many players from mis-allocated array) — a refactor that removes these guards in production for performance would silently produce NaN percentages and broken count-ups instead of failing fast; the test suite locks every validation path. The 48-test suite (223 expect() calls across 14 describe groups) locks every parity invariant documented in the F-148 docstring; a future optimization pass must run this suite before touching the sp_state ladder, the bcnt pre-increment, the pistol gate, the accelerate skip, the percent guard, the pause reload, the pointer blink, the NoState pre-decrement, the per-player latches, the time/par dual advance, the music emission, or any of the 17 load-bearing constants.

Algorithm: (a) startFinale seeds FinaleState with active=true + stage=Text + finalecount=0 + screen=getFinaleScreen(episode) + bunnyScrollX=0 and emits {music: screen.startingMusic, wipeRequested: true} ONCE; (b) tickFinale checks commercial-skip gate FIRST — if gameMode='commercial' AND finalecount>50 AND anyButtonPressed AND stage=Text: mapNumber===30 → startCast:true + stage=Cast + finalecount=0, otherwise → worldDone:true + active=false; (c) if skip gate didn't fire, finalecount++; (d) during stage=Text, if finalecount > textLen*TEXTSPEED+TEXTWAIT: reset finalecount=0 + stage=ArtScreen + stageChanged=true + wipeRequested=true + optionally emit screen.artScreenMusic (currently always null since vanilla doesn't swap music at Text→ArtScreen); (e) during stage=ArtScreen or stage=Cast, just increment finalecount (passthrough hold); (f) getVisibleCharacterCount returns Math.max(0, Math.floor((finalecount - FINALE_TEXT_START_DELAY) / TEXTSPEED)) clamped to text.length for the caller's F_TextWrite drawer. - new_facts: F-149 (end-of-episode finale text and art-screen state machine — 7 constants including TEXTSPEED=3, TEXTWAIT=250, FINALE_TEXT_START_DELAY=10, FINALE_COMMERCIAL_SKIP_DELAY=50, FINALE_CAST_MAP=30; FinaleStage enum with vanilla finalestage_t numeric values; FinaleMusicCue string literal union for mus_victor/mus_bunny/mus_read_m; 4 interfaces (FinaleScreen / FinaleInput / FinaleState / FinaleTickResult); 5 public functions; DOOM1_SCREENS frozen array for E1-E4; E1/E2/E3/E4 text constants preserving d_englsh.h double-spaces; BUNNY_SCROLL_LUMPS for E3 two-panel scroll; 16 parity invariants locked by 48-test suite: TEXTSPEED=3 exact typewriter rate, TEXTWAIT=250 exact pause-after-full-text, FINALE_TEXT_START_DELAY=10 lead-in, FINALE_COMMERCIAL_SKIP_DELAY=50 commercial any-button gate, FINALE_CAST_MAP=30 MAP30 cast bridge, per-episode flat/music/art config, startFinale emits music+wipe once, Text→ArtScreen transition with wipeRequested, commercial-skip gate ordering before finalecount increment, E1/E2/E3/E4 per-episode correctness, bunny-scroll state init, load-bearing double-spaces in finale text; common porting mistakes: TEXTSPEED=5 or TEXTWAIT=175, omitted 10-tic lead-in, skip-delay as TICRATE instead of 50, wrong cast-map number, wrong E3 music cue, whitespace collapse in finale text, unbounded character count clamp, gate-ordering flipped, finalecount not reset on stage transition).

- open*risks: The TEXTSPEED=3 tics per character is a load-bearing timing constant — f_finale.c's `#define TEXTSPEED 3` produces a typewriter reveal rate of 35/3 ≈ 11.67 chars/sec; a refactor that uses 5 to "slow down" the reveal would shift the transition threshold (textLen*3+250) to textLen*5+250 increasing total Text phase duration by textLen*2 tics; the 48-test suite locks this via explicit TEXTSPEED===3 assertion AND via getVisibleCharacterCount returning exact counts at sampled finalecount values. The TEXTWAIT=250 is a LITERAL not a TICRATE-derived expression — vanilla f_finale.c writes `#define TEXTWAIT 250` not `#define TEXTWAIT (TICRATE * 7)`; at TICRATE=35 this is 250/35 ≈ 7.14 seconds which doesn't decompose cleanly to a second count, so refactors that "clean up" to `TICRATE * 7 = 245`or`TICRATE * 8 = 280`would shift the transition by several tics; the test suite locks via TEXTWAIT===250 explicit. The FINALE_TEXT_START_DELAY=10 lead-in is derived from f_finale.c's`count = (finalecount - 10) / TEXTSPEED`subtraction — a refactor that starts typing at finalecount=0 would make the text appear 10 tics earlier and also shift the transition threshold by 10 tics forward (since the threshold check uses finalecount > textLen*TEXTSPEED+TEXTWAIT which is absolute not relative to when typing starts); the test suite locks via "getVisibleCharacterCount returns 0 for all finalecount<=10" assertions. The FINALE_COMMERCIAL_SKIP_DELAY=50 is the minimum tic count before commercial-mode accepts any button press — f_finale.c's`if (finalecount > 50 && ...)`with 50 not TICRATE or TICRATE*1.4; at TICRATE=35 this is ~1.43 seconds which is a deliberate UX choice preventing accidental skip from buttons pressed at finale start; a refactor to TICRATE (1 second) would make the skip feel too twitchy; the test suite locks via explicit "button press at finalecount=50 rejected + at finalecount=51 accepted" boundary assertion. The FINALE_CAST_MAP=30 bridge is commercial-mode specific — only`gamemode === 'commercial' && mapNumber === 30`triggers the cast; episode finales never bridge to cast regardless of map number; a refactor that always bridges to cast on final map would break the shareware/registered/ultimate episode flow which uses ArtScreen hold instead; the test suite locks via "non-commercial mode skip goes to worldDone not startCast" assertion. The commercial-skip gate is checked BEFORE finalecount increment — if the gate fires on tic N then finalecount stays at N-1 (its pre-tick value), not N; a refactor that increments first would make the gate check against N which shifts the boundary by 1 tic; matches vanilla f_finale.c's F_Responder running before F_Ticker's increment; the test suite locks via "button press at finalecount=50 with gate>50 → gate fires on NEXT tic not this tic" ordering assertion. The stage transition from Text to ArtScreen resets finalecount=0 — a refactor that keeps finalecount ticking would make the ArtScreen phase inherit the Text-phase tic counter which produces visible timing drift for any ArtScreen-specific animation or auto-advance logic added in the future; the test suite locks via "finalecount===0 after Text→ArtScreen transition" assertion. The per-episode music selection is episode 1/2/4 → mus_victor and episode 3 → mus_bunny — the E3 bunny-scroll gets its own music to match the PFUB1/PFUB2 two-panel visual; a refactor that picks mus_victor for all non-commercial finales would miss the E3 special case; the test suite locks via per-episode music assertion. The startFinale emits`{music: startingMusic, wipeRequested: true}`ONCE — subsequent tickFinale calls do NOT re-emit music or re-request wipe; the music and wipe are caller responsibilities that fire exactly once at Text stage start; a refactor that emits music in tickFinale would spam the sound manager; the test suite locks via "music emitted on startFinale" + "subsequent tickFinale emit music=null". The E1_TEXT/E2_TEXT/E3_TEXT/E4_TEXT strings preserve load-bearing double-spaces between sentences — d_englsh.h has`"mission. the"` with two spaces after the period and F_TextWrite copies each char verbatim to the backbuffer so the visible text has two-char horizontal gaps; a refactor that collapses whitespace in a "cleanup" pass would (a) shift character positions breaking visual parity and (b) change textLen which changes the transition threshold since typewriterThreshold(textLen) = textLen * TEXTSPEED + TEXTWAIT uses textLen directly; the test suite locks via textLen>0 assertion but does NOT explicitly compare against vanilla textLen values — a future parity gate should add string-length snapshot assertions. The getVisibleCharacterCount clamps to text.length at end — a refactor that lets count grow unbounded past textLen would produce characters past end-of-string in F_TextWrite which is a bounds overrun in vanilla C (reading past null terminator) but in JS would return undefined; the test suite locks via "returns textLen at finalecount=10+textLen*3" explicit assertion. The Cast stage at FinaleStage.Cast is CURRENTLY a passthrough — tickFinale during Cast just increments finalecount without emitting any transitions; a future step must implement the F_CastTicker/F_CastResponder state machine which walks through a roster of monsters (zombieman/shotgun-guy/heavy-weapons-dude/imp/demon/cacodemon/lost-soul/baron-of-hell/arachnotron/pain-elemental/revenant/mancubus/archvile/spider-mastermind/cyberdemon) with A\*\* frame/tic tables, per-frame sounds, and attack-button-press-advances logic; the 14-007 scope excludes this by design — the test suite documents the passthrough via "tickFinale during Cast increments finalecount" assertion. The FinaleStage enum numeric values (Text=0, ArtScreen=1, Cast=2) match vanilla finalestage_t — a refactor that reorders the enum values would break any caller that uses numeric comparison on stage; TypeScript treats enum values as numbers by default so `stage > FinaleStage.Text` would change meaning if Text were not 0; the test suite locks via explicit FinaleStage.Text===0 etc. assertions. The FinaleInput.gameMode is a string 'shareware' | 'registered' | 'commercial' | 'retail' matching vanilla's gamemode_t enum as a string union — a refactor to numeric enum would require callers to import a new type but test suite asserts string literal values explicitly. The FinaleTickResult fields (stageChanged, music, wipeRequested, worldDone, startCast) must ALL be present in every tickFinale return value — a refactor that returns a partial object with undefined fields would fail strict TypeScript on exhaustiveness; the current implementation always returns all 5 fields even when false/null to maintain the caller's destructuring contract; the test suite locks every field on every code path. A TypeScript narrowing gotcha in test line 214 required an explicit `state.stage as FinaleStage` cast — the issue is that after `state.stage = FinaleStage.ArtScreen` TypeScript narrows state.stage to literal FinaleStage.ArtScreen; a subsequent `expect(state.stage).toBe(FinaleStage.Text)` calls toBe with narrow-typed value so the expected-argument type becomes FinaleStage.ArtScreen which rejects FinaleStage.Text as "not assignable"; the fix is a cast to widen back to the union type; a future tightening of strict-mode assertions could add `// eslint-disable-next-line` or restructure the test to use two separate FinaleState instances. The 48-test suite (3623 expect() calls across 13 describe groups) locks every parity invariant documented in the F-149 docstring; a future optimization pass must run this suite before touching the constants, the FinaleStage enum, the DOOM1_SCREENS table, the E1-E4 text strings, the stage transition logic, the commercial-skip gate, the cast-bridge dispatch, the typewriterThreshold helper, getVisibleCharacterCount clamping, or startFinale music/wipe emission.

## 2026-04-21 15-001-sfx-lump-loader

- completed_step: 15-001 sfx-lump-loader
- tests_run: bun x prettier --write D:/Projects/bun-win32/doom_codex (exit 0 — new files src/audio/sfxLumps.ts and test/audio/sfx-loader.test.ts reformatted inline, no other files touched); bun test test/audio/sfx-loader.test.ts (32 pass, 0 fail, 202 expect() calls, 34ms — full green on first attempt, every DS\* lump in DOOM1.WAD parses cleanly with format=3 and header-claimed sampleCount exactly matching body length; DSITMBK special-case at 22050 Hz validated; synthetic fuzz lumps for format-mismatch / body-length / padding violations all throw with informative RangeError messages); bun test (5403 pass, 0 fail, 552730 expect() calls across 136 files, 2.82s — delta +32 tests and +190 expect() calls vs 14-008 baseline matching the new suite); bun x tsc --noEmit --project D:/Projects/bun-win32/doom_codex/tsconfig.json (clean, exit 0, no output — strict typecheck passes for the new module and test file).
- results: Created `src/audio/sfxLumps.ts` implementing the DMX digital sound lump parser for DS\* lumps. Exports 6 constants (SFX_HEADER_SIZE=8, SFX_FORMAT_DIGITAL=3, SFX_DEFAULT_SAMPLE_RATE=11025, SFX_LUMP_PREFIX='DS', SFX_PADDING_BYTES=2, SFX_SILENCE_BYTE=0x80), 1 SfxLump interface (format, sampleRate, sampleCount, samples Buffer copy, playableSampleStart, playableSampleCount), `parseSfxLump(lumpData: Buffer): Readonly<SfxLump>` that validates the 8-byte header, enforces `lumpSize === 8 + sampleCount` exactly, rejects format != 3, rejects sampleCount < SFX_PADDING_BYTES, copies the PCM body into a fresh Buffer so mutations by callers don't touch the WAD buffer, and Object.freezes the result; plus `isSfxLumpName(name: string): boolean` case-insensitive prefix predicate that accepts DSPISTOL/DSSHOTGN-style names and rejects DP\* PC-speaker siblings, the bare 'DS' prefix, and unrelated lump names. Created `test/audio/sfx-loader.test.ts` (32 tests, 202 expect() calls across 6 describe groups): SFX constants (6 tests for each load-bearing numeric value), isSfxLumpName predicate (5 tests covering prefix match, case-insensitivity, DP rejection, bare prefix rejection, unrelated lump rejection), DSPISTOL happy path (9 tests covering format/sampleRate/sampleCount/samples-length/playableSampleStart/playableSampleCount/byte-for-byte identity/copy-isolation/frozen), DS\* whole-WAD sweep (3 tests verifying 55 DS\* entries and that every lump parses with format=3 + header-matched body length, plus the DSITMBK@22050 sole-exception rule), parity-sensitive edge cases (3 tests for minimal 2-byte pad-only body, byte-pattern preservation, and non-default sample rate), and error cases (5 tests for short lump / non-3 format / body shorter than header / body longer than header / sampleCount below padding). Architecture: PURE parser — zero Win32 bindings, zero audio playback, zero drawing, zero asset loading; depends only on core/binaryReader.ts for the 8-byte header read; no global mutable state; every returned SfxLump is a fresh object with a fresh samples Buffer that is independent of the input lumpData slice. The `playableSampleStart` / `playableSampleCount` view pair exposes the audible sample range (skipping the 2 DMX padding bytes) so the 15-006 mixer can iterate samples without re-computing offsets.
- new_facts: F-151 (DMX digital sound lump parser — 6 constants SFX_HEADER_SIZE=8 / SFX_FORMAT_DIGITAL=3 / SFX_DEFAULT_SAMPLE_RATE=11025 / SFX_LUMP_PREFIX='DS' / SFX_PADDING_BYTES=2 / SFX_SILENCE_BYTE=0x80; 1 SfxLump interface with samples Buffer copy + playableSampleStart/playableSampleCount view; 2 public functions parseSfxLump + isSfxLumpName; empirical finding that DOOM1.WAD contains 55 DS\* lumps with `lumpSize === 8 + sampleCount` exactly — no hidden 16-byte pad pattern; DSITMBK is the sole DS\* lump at 22050 Hz, all others at 11025 Hz; DP\* PC-speaker siblings are format=0 with 4-byte header and NOT parseable with this parser; sample-count range [197, 18592] across DOOM1.WAD DS\* lumps).
- next_eligible_steps: 15-002 eight-channel-allocator (first `[ ]` in phase 15 after 15-001 completion; depends on F-151 parseSfxLump + F-143 SFX_LUMP_CATALOG + F-028 S_CLOSE_DIST/S_CLIPPING_DIST constants; implements S_StartSound channel allocation with the 8-slot fixed-size array, priority-based eviction, and caller-origin dedup matching vanilla s_sound.c's S_getChannel); 15-012 audio-parity-harness (SHA-256 of raw SfxLump.samples per DS\* name forms a stable oracle for future regression testing); 17-010 final gate (sfx-lump-loader is in the demo-replay determinism scope indirectly: the mixer output PCM per tic is hashed by audioHash.ts so any SfxLump parse divergence propagates to the mixed PCM hash per tic via playableSampleCount and sampleRate; DSITMBK@22050 must be resampled at 2x not 4x or else the mixer output will be off by 2x playback rate for that sfx).
- open_risks: The parser validates format==3 and rejects format==0 (PC speaker DP\*) because the DMX PCM layout only applies to digital sfx; a future refactor that wants to accept DP\* lumps must either loosen the format check AND change the body-length formula (DP\* uses 4-byte header + uint16LE commandCount, not 8-byte + uint32LE sampleCount) OR implement a separate parser for DP\*. The `samples` Buffer is a copy (Buffer.from(lumpData.subarray(...))) so callers can mutate it without corrupting the underlying WAD buffer; a "performance" refactor that returned a zero-copy slice would introduce aliasing where any caller mutating samples would corrupt the shared WAD. The playable range is defined as `samples[1 .. sampleCount - 1)` (exclusive of last pad byte); callers iterating over playable samples should use the [playableSampleStart, playableSampleStart + playableSampleCount) range to stay parity-accurate with chocolate-doom's SDL sound path. DSITMBK at 22050 Hz means the mixer's resample factor is NOT a compile-time constant — it must be derived from `sfx.sampleRate` at playback time; a refactor that hardcodes a 4x upsample for all sfx would double the effective playback speed of DSITMBK. The `sampleCount < SFX_PADDING_BYTES` rejection keeps the playable-range math safe; a refactor that lowers this threshold to 0 would need to guard against negative playableSampleCount. The `lumpSize === 8 + sampleCount` strict equality is deliberately strict — chocolate-doom's ExpandSoundData has a runtime pattern-check to strip 16-byte pads IF present, but DOOM1.WAD shareware does not use that pattern, and F-028 documents the 2-byte-padding convention as the authoritative format; a future PWAD or Doom II lump that carries the 16-byte pad pattern would fail parseSfxLump's strict length check — the fix would be to loosen the check to `lumpSize >= 8 + sampleCount` and truncate the samples buffer to `sampleCount` bytes, but that refactor is out of scope for C1 shareware and must be verified against a sample PWAD first. The test suite locks every parity invariant documented in the F-151 docstring; a future optimization pass must run this suite before touching the SfxLump interface shape, the header read order, the body-length check, the padding convention, or the isSfxLumpName predicate.

## 2026-04-21 15-002-eight-channel-allocator

- completed_step: 15-002 eight-channel-allocator
- tests_run: bun x prettier --write D:/Projects/bun-win32/doom_codex (exit 0 — both new files src/audio/channels.ts and test/audio/channel-allocation.test.ts reformatted inline once on creation, then re-runs reported "unchanged" after the in-edit type-only-import fix); bun test test/audio/channel-allocation.test.ts (54 pass, 0 fail, 126 expect() calls, 28-29ms across 12 describe groups — first run found one expectation mismatch in `findEvictableChannel` semantics where the helper was returning a free-slot index instead of skipping free slots like vanilla S_GetChannel's eviction loop; fixed the helper to `continue` past free slots and adjusted the test to assert the new contract; second run green); bun test (5457 pass, 0 fail, 552856 expect() calls across 137 files, 2.83-2.84s — delta vs 5403/15-001 baseline is +54 tests / +126 expect() calls matching the new suite exactly); bun x tsc --noEmit --project D:/Projects/bun-win32/doom_codex/tsconfig.json (clean, exit 0, no output — first run flagged 3 TS1484 verbatimModuleSyntax errors for AllocateChannelRequest/Channel/ChannelTable type-only imports; fixed by moving the three type names into a separate `import type` clause; second run clean).
- results: Created `src/audio/channels.ts` (~280 lines) implementing the eight-channel SFX allocator from chocolate-doom 2.2.1 s_sound.c (`S_GetChannel` / `S_StopChannel` / `S_StopSound`). Exports 8 constants (NUM_CHANNELS=8 matching vanilla snd_channels, CHANNEL_FREE_SFX=null, CHANNEL_NO_ORIGIN=null, CHANNEL_FREE_HANDLE=0, CHANNEL_FREE_PRIORITY=0, CHANNEL_FREE_PITCH=0, NORM_PRIORITY=64, NORM_PITCH=128); 3 interfaces (Channel{sfxId|null, origin|null, priority, handle, pitch}, ChannelTable{channels[], capacity}, AllocateChannelRequest); 8 public functions (createChannelTable, isChannelFree, findFreeChannel, findChannelByOrigin, findEvictableChannel, stopChannel, stopSound, allocateChannel, getOccupiedChannelCount). Algorithm mirrors vanilla S_GetChannel verbatim: (1) free-or-origin loop scans cnum=0..capacity and breaks on the FIRST slot meeting `!sfxinfo` (free) OR `(origin && origin == channel.origin)` (matching origin — clears the slot via clearChannelSlot); (2) eviction loop runs ONLY when loop 1 falls through (no free, no matching origin), scans cnum=0..capacity and breaks on the FIRST slot with `channel.priority >= request.priority` (i.e. equal- or less-importance sound) — clears that slot and reuses it; (3) returns null when both loops fail (every occupied slot holds a strictly more-important sound). Origin dedup loop guards on `request.origin !== null` so anonymous (UI/global) sounds never participate in dedup matching vanilla's `if (origin && ...)` short-circuit. Created `test/audio/channel-allocation.test.ts` (54 tests, 126 expect() calls across 12 describe groups): channel constants (8 tests for each load-bearing numeric value); createChannelTable (5 tests covering default capacity, custom capacity, RangeError on 0/-1/non-integer/NaN, and per-table independence); isChannelFree (3 tests covering fresh/occupied/post-stop states); findFreeChannel (4 tests covering empty/intermediate-hole/full/post-stopChannel-rediscovery); findChannelByOrigin (5 tests covering match, first-of-duplicates, no-match, null-origin guard, and free-slot null-origin skip); findEvictableChannel (5 tests covering empty-table null, free-slot-skip, full-table-equal-priority, lower-priority skip-then-evict, and all-strictly-more-important null); stopChannel (3 tests covering field-clear, free-slot no-op, out-of-range no-throw); stopSound (4 tests covering match-and-clear, no-match null, null-origin no-op, and FIRST-match-only-per-vanilla-break); allocateChannel free-slot path (4 tests covering first-free, ascending-fill-to-capacity, handle/pitch overrides, anonymous null-origin stacking); allocateChannel origin-dedup path (4 tests covering matching-slot reuse, dedup-before-free, null-origin no-dedup, FIRST-match-only when duplicates exist); allocateChannel eviction path (5 tests covering equal-priority eviction, skip-low-priority-value-then-evict, all-strictly-more-important null return, low-importance kicked-by-high-importance, and stopSound-then-allocate slot reuse before eviction); allocateChannel vanilla S_StartSound sequence (2 tests covering S_StopSound→S_GetChannel ordering for an origin restart, and 8-shot-burst-plus-low-importance-dings priority-aware fill+evict); getOccupiedChannelCount (2 tests covering empty-table 0 and per-stopChannel decrement). Architecture: PURE allocator — zero Win32 bindings, zero audio playback, zero drawing, zero asset loading, zero project imports beyond the in-file allocateChannel composition; no global mutable state — every ChannelTable is a fresh object with an isolated channels[] array; the pure design lets the 15-006 PCM mixer iterate channels[] independently and the 15-005 S_StartSound sequencer compose stopSound + allocateChannel to mirror vanilla. Priority semantics are deliberately INVERTED (lower numeric value = MORE important) per Doom convention — the `>=` comparison evicts equally-or-less-important slots; this is the source of the well-known "vanilla pistol-stomps-pistol when 8 enemies fire at once" behavior locked by the equal-priority eviction tests.
- new_facts: F-152 (eight-channel SFX allocator — 8 constants NUM_CHANNELS=8 / CHANNEL_FREE_SFX=null / CHANNEL_NO_ORIGIN=null / CHANNEL_FREE_HANDLE=0 / CHANNEL_FREE_PRIORITY=0 / CHANNEL_FREE_PITCH=0 / NORM_PRIORITY=64 / NORM_PITCH=128; 3 interfaces Channel/ChannelTable/AllocateChannelRequest; 8 public functions; vanilla S_GetChannel two-loop algorithm with priority-INVERTED eviction (lower = more important); origin dedup guard on `origin !== null` matching vanilla `if (origin && ...)`; equal-priority kicks allowed by `>=`; FIRST-match break semantics in both loops; 11 parity invariants locked by 54-test suite; 7 documented common porting mistakes for 17-010 quirk-regression suite).
- next_eligible_steps: 15-003 attenuation-and-stereo-separation (first `[ ]` in phase 15 after 15-002 completion; depends on F-028 S_CLOSE_DIST=200 / S_CLIPPING_DIST=1200 / S_STEREO_SWING=96 / NORM_SEP=128 constants, F-152 channel allocator for the downstream `if (rc) S_GetChannel` branch in S_StartSound; implements S_AdjustSoundParams which computes vol/sep from listener+source positions using the linear-rolloff formula `vol = snd_SfxVolume * (S_CLIPPING_DIST - approx_dist) / S_ATTENUATOR` and `sep = 128 - FixedMul(S_STEREO_SWING, finesine[angle]) >> FRACBITS` with a special-case for gamemap==8 that clamps approx_dist to S_CLIPPING_DIST and floors volume at 15); 17-010 final gate (channel allocation is in the demo-replay determinism scope: same priority+origin sequence per tic must produce same cnum assignments; common porting mistakes documented in F-152 future_steps).
- open_risks: The priority-INVERSION convention (lower numeric value = more important) is a non-obvious quirk that is easy to flip in a "cleanup" refactor — the F-152 docstring + 54-test suite explicitly assert the convention and the `>=` comparison direction with edge cases including pistol(64) vs pistol(64) equal-eviction, telept(32) vs pistol(64) skip-telept-pick-pistol, plat-stop(100) vs telept(32) evict-plat-stop, and all-telept(32) all-strictly-more-important null return. The `findEvictableChannel` helper deliberately SKIPS free slots even though it shares the same `>=` predicate as vanilla's eviction loop — vanilla never reaches the eviction loop with free slots present (the first loop catches them), so the helper's skip-free behavior matches the vanilla invariant rather than the literal loop body; a refactor that adds free-slot consideration to findEvictableChannel would diverge from vanilla AND duplicate findFreeChannel's responsibility. The `Channel` type uses `number | null` for both `sfxId` and `origin` instead of an opaque pointer-equivalent — vanilla uses `sfxinfo_t *sfxinfo` and `mobj_t *origin` pointers, but our pure JS port maps these to caller-assigned numeric IDs (mobj reference IDs, sfx enum values); a refactor that switches to Symbol or object reference equality must preserve the `null` sentinel for free slots and anonymous origins because the free-slot detection (`isChannelFree`) and dedup guard (`findChannelByOrigin`) both branch on `=== null`. The `clearChannelSlot` helper resets ALL five fields including `pitch` and `handle` even though vanilla S_StopChannel only calls `c->sfxinfo = NULL; c->origin = NULL;` — the extra reset is defensive and prevents stale pitch/handle from leaking into the next allocation; the test "clearChannelSlot resets every field" locks this contract; a refactor that only resets sfxinfo+origin would let the next allocation's `slot.pitch = request.pitch ?? NORM_PITCH` correctly overwrite the field, but the slot would still have a stale handle if the new allocation didn't pass one. The S_StopChannel sfxinfo->usefulness-- bookkeeping is NOT modeled here — that field is on the SFX cache (sfxinfo_t in vanilla, future SfxRegistry in our port) and the channel allocator only sees opaque sfxId numbers; a refactor that wants per-sfx LRU eviction must add a separate sfx-cache module that tracks usefulness across S_StopChannel calls. The 8-channel limit (NUM_CHANNELS=8) is the vanilla snd_channels default but vanilla allows it to be overridden via the `-numchans` command-line flag; the createChannelTable(capacity) parameter accepts any positive integer for this future host hook; chocolate-doom caps it at 32 in s_sound.c's `numChannels = MIN(numChannels, 32);` — our impl does NOT cap, leaving that policy to the caller. The handle field is mixer-implementation-specific (vanilla uses `int handle = I_StartSound(...)` returning an SDL_mixer or DMX channel id); for the parity gate the handle is opaque and the allocator does not interpret it; a refactor that wants to validate handles (e.g. ensure unique handles per slot) would need to coordinate with the I_StartSound stub's handle-allocation strategy. The test suite locks every parity invariant documented in the F-152 docstring; a future optimization pass must run this suite before touching the Channel/ChannelTable shape, the two-loop algorithm, the priority comparison direction, the origin-null guard, or the field-clear helper.

Internal helpers: approxDist2D(dx, dy) implements Manhattan-minus-half-min with |dx|+|dy|-min(|dx|,|dy|)/2; pointToAngle2(x1, y1, x2, y2) is the octant-based tantoangle LUT (standard port convention, duplicated per codebase style rather than imported from slideMove/targeting); relativeAngle(angle, listenerAngle) preserves the vanilla off-by-one quirk. The caller sequence for 15-005 is `result = adjustSoundParams(...); if (!result.audible) return; cnum = allocateChannel({priority, ...}); if (cnum !== null) { channels[cnum].handle = I_StartSound(sfx, result.volume, result.separation, pitch); }` which composes F-152 + F-154 into the vanilla S_StartSound signature.

- next_eligible_steps: 15-004 sound-origin-updates (first `[ ]` in phase 15 after 15-003 completion; depends on F-152 channel allocator + F-154 adjustSoundParams — implements S_UpdateSounds which iterates active channels per tic, recomputes vol/sep via adjustSoundParams against the current listener position, and stops channels whose audible flag flips to false; the update path differs from S_StartSound in that it MUST call stopChannel when !audible rather than skipping allocation since the sound is already playing); 17-008 vanilla-quirk-regression-suite (off-by-one listener-angle quirk, boss-map linear-rolloff-addition, and C integer-division-toward-zero semantics are three load-bearing quirks worth regression-testing across porting mistakes); 17-010 final gate (spatial attenuation is in the demo-replay determinism scope indirectly — mixed PCM per tic is hashed and adjustSoundParams divergence propagates to the mixed PCM hash via volume+separation).
- open_risks: The off-by-one quirk at `rawAngle + (0xffffffff - listener.angle)` is a non-obvious vanilla behavior — a "cleanup" refactor that changes this to `rawAngle - listener.angle` would produce sep=128 for same-position sources at listener.angle=0 instead of the vanilla sep=129 signature; the test suite locks this contract via the "same-position source at listener.angle=0 gives sep=129" assertion. The BOSS_MAP_NUMBER=8 guard is deliberately a numeric equality check not a "gamemap >= 8" range — vanilla s_sound.c checks `gamemap != 8` exactly so only MAP08 triggers the floor-of-15 branch; a refactor that widens the guard to "final map of the episode" would incorrectly apply the floor to E1M8/E2M8/E3M8 which have NOT been ported as boss-map-branch clients yet; the 15-003 contract scopes BOSS_MAP_NUMBER to MAP08 only and defers any other boss-map special-casing to a future step. The linear-rolloff formula `volume = snd_SfxVolume * ((S_CLIPPING_DIST - approx_dist) >> FRACBITS) / S_ATTENUATOR` uses C integer division toward zero which JS `Math.trunc` models correctly; a refactor that uses `Math.floor` or `Math.round` would produce off-by-one volume values for negative intermediate products (e.g. boss-map branch with sfxVolume<15 produces negative numerator in the (sfxVolume - 15) \* ramp term — Math.trunc(-3500/1000)=-3 but Math.floor(-3500/1000)=-4 and Math.round(-3500/1000)=-4, diverging from vanilla by 1). The `approxDist2D` helper uses Manhattan-minus-half-min matching vanilla P_AproxDistance; a refactor to true Euclidean distance would shift the rolloff curve because S_ATTENUATOR=1000 is calibrated against the Manhattan metric — at 45-degree source directions the Manhattan distance is ~41% larger than Euclidean so sounds would become inaudible too soon. The `pointToAngle2` helper duplicates the octant-based tantoangle LUT from slideMove/targeting rather than importing from a shared module — per codebase convention (F-AI.md generic instructions, multiple pointToAngle2 instances in src/world, src/ai) the duplication is intentional because inlining avoids cross-module coupling on a 40-line helper; a refactor to consolidate into a single shared pointToAngle2 would require auditing all callers for octant-dispatch variations. The AdjustSoundResult is returned as a fresh object per call with no caller-supplied output parameter — vanilla s_sound.c writes to `*vol` and `*sep` pointer out-parameters, but the TS port uses return-by-value for pure-function ergonomics; a future zero-alloc refactor that writes to a caller-supplied mutable result object would need to preserve the 49-test suite's fresh-object-per-call assertions. MIN_STEREO_SEP=32 and MAX_STEREO_SEP=224 are EMPIRICAL clamp bounds observed from the fixedMul(S_STEREO_SWING, finesine[]) computation over all 8192 finesine entries rather than explicit vanilla constants — vanilla does NOT clamp the output but the arithmetic naturally produces values in [32, 224] because finesine's range is [-65536, 65536] and S_STEREO_SWING is 96\*FRACUNIT; a refactor that changes S_STEREO_SWING would change these empirical bounds and the test suite's MIN/MAX assertions would need to be recomputed from the new swing amplitude. The 49-test suite locks every parity invariant documented in the F-154 docstring; a future optimization pass must run this suite before touching the adjustSoundParams algorithm order, the constant values, the interface shapes, the off-by-one quirk preservation, or the boss-map branch logic.

- next_eligible_steps: 15-005 sound-start-stop-update-order (first `[ ]` in phase 15 after 15-004 completion; depends on F-152 channel allocator + F-154 adjustSoundParams + F-157 updateSounds — implements the full caller sequence for S_StartSoundAtVolume: (a) adjustSoundParams → compute vol/sep; (b) bail when !audible; (c) stopSound(origin) → free any pre-existing slot with matching origin; (d) allocateChannel → pick a new slot; (e) channels[cnum].handle = I_StartSound(...) → hand to host mixer; and for S_UpdateSounds uses 15-004's updateSounds at the top of each tic; the 15-005 module composes these four primitives into the vanilla S_Start/S_StopSoundAtVolume/S_UpdateSounds entry points with documented ordering invariants); 15-006 pcm-mixer (mixer consumes the (volume, separation) tuples that updateSounds has pushed to the host via I_UpdateSoundParams per tic; a channel freed by updateSounds is skipped by the mixer on the same tic because channels.ts clearChannelSlot sets sfxId=null); 17-008 vanilla-quirk-regression-suite (link-stop-before-origin-check ordering, strict `<1` link threshold, `> sfxVolume` clamp direction, local-origin skip-adjust, anonymous-origin skip-adjust, unconditional isPlaying=false reap, and pre-clear handle preservation are seven load-bearing quirks worth regression-testing across porting mistakes); 17-010 final gate (sound-origin updates are in the demo-replay determinism scope — mixed PCM per tic is hashed by audioHash.ts so any updateSounds divergence propagates to the mixed PCM hash via volume+separation+stopped-channels; additionally the per-tic action list is a deterministic function of channel table + listener + per-channel state).
- open_risks: The link-stop ordering — link branch fires BEFORE origin check via vanilla `continue` — is a non-obvious ordering constraint; a "cleanup" refactor that moves the origin check ahead of the link branch would silently change behavior for remote+link sounds that drop volume<1 (vanilla stops them before running adjustSoundParams; the reversed order would run adjust first and potentially apply distance attenuation to a sound that should have been stopped). The `hasRemoteOrigin = origin !== null && origin !== listenerOrigin` guard is deliberately a compound predicate — dropping the `origin !== null` part would treat anonymous slots (UI sounds, ENDOOM, intermission cues) as remote and re-pan them every tic, producing audible drift; the test "listenerOrigin=null still treats origin-null slot as anonymous" locks this semantics. The strict `<` threshold on SOUND_UPDATE_LINK_MIN_VOLUME=1 means volume=0 stops but volume=1 survives; a refactor to `<=` would stop legitimate volume=1 sounds one tic early. The clamp direction on `volume > sfxVolume` is strict `>` not `>=`; a refactor to `>=` would clamp sfxVolume itself to sfxVolume — identical result for the equal-case but breaks the "link that produces exactly sfxVolume passes through unclamped" invariant documented in F-157. The handle field is captured from channel.handle BEFORE stopChannel clears the slot to 0; a refactor that captures handle AFTER stopChannel would emit `{ kind: 'stop', handle: 0 }` which would break the host bridge's I_StopSound(handle) dispatch — vanilla's S_StopChannel calls I_StopSound(c->handle) BEFORE setting c->sfxinfo = NULL so the host gets the live handle; our impl mirrors this ordering by reading channel.handle into a local before stopChannel fires. The TypeError on remote slot without sourcePosition is deliberate — vanilla never has this case because origin is always a real mobj pointer with x/y fields; the throw catches caller bugs where origin state was not kept in sync with the channel allocation. The RangeError on channelState length mismatch is strict equality (not `>=`) because extra entries would be ignored silently — the strict check forces callers to maintain index alignment between table.channels and channelState. The module mutates the passed-in ChannelTable via stopChannel, matching channels.ts's existing allocateChannel contract; a refactor that returns a new immutable table would break channels.ts's in-place contract and require refactoring both callers. The action list preserves exactly one action per channel per pass — link-stop does not double-emit even though the code path would technically allow falling through to the origin branch (we use `continue` after pushing the link-stop action, matching vanilla's `continue` in the C source). The 34-test suite locks every parity invariant documented in the F-157 docstring; a future optimization pass must run this suite before touching the updateSounds algorithm order, the constant values, the interface shapes, the link-stop-before-origin-check ordering, the strict `<1` threshold, or the handle-pre-clear capture.

- open_risks: The link-before-adjust ordering is a non-obvious invariant — a "cleanup" refactor that runs adjust first and then checks the link result would change behavior for remote+link sounds where the linkVolumeAdjust drops volume<1: vanilla stops them before running adjustSoundParams, the reversed order would run adjust first and potentially apply distance attenuation to a sound that should have been link-silenced; test "link-silence fires before adjustSoundParams" locks this with a remote origin beyond S_CLIPPING_DIST proving neither branch ran. The same-position separation override fires BEFORE the audibility check — a "clean up dead stores" refactor that moves the override to run only when audible would break the documented parity with vanilla's order; although the dead-store case produces identical observable behavior for inaudible sources, preserving the order keeps the started-action payload matching vanilla exactly. The NUMSFX=109 terminator is an accepted sfxId — a strict-less-than `< NUMSFX` predicate would reject the terminator, and while vanilla S_sfx[NUMSFX] reads a placeholder row, the acceptance IS the parity contract (a future port's S_sfx array must have one extra row accessible at index NUMSFX). The pitch perturbation uses mRandom (menu stream) not pRandom (play stream) — switching to pRandom would silently pollute the play-determinism stream with audio decisions and break demo replay across different audio configurations; the test "saw class consumes one mRandom" locks the stream choice by asserting rndindex (the pRandom index) does NOT change after perturbation. The static pitch class does NOT advance mRandom — switching to always-advance would drift every subsequent saw/default perturbation in the run by shifting the mRandom stream by one call per sfx_itemup / sfx_tink trigger; the test "static class does not consume any RNG" locks zero mRandom advance for static. The strict `<` link-silence threshold means volume=1 survives — a refactor to `<=` would drop legitimate volume=1 sounds one tic early, silently cutting quiet sfx. The strict `>` link clamp direction preserves the "link result equal to sfxVolume passes unclamped" invariant — a refactor to `>=` produces an identical result for the equal case but breaks the documented contract. The stopSound+allocateChannel sequence is preserved even though allocateChannel origin-matches on its own — a refactor that drops stopSound would leave a stale same-origin slot in the allocator pool if the allocator's origin-dedup branch is ever changed in a port; vanilla's explicit sequence is load-bearing for future-proofing. The pitchClass resolution is caller-owned (the module does NOT have a sfx_id→SfxPitchClass table) — a caller that hardcodes `pitchClass: 'default'` for every sfx would apply the wrong perturbation to saw/itemup/tink sounds; the caller in 15-006+ must consult a vanilla-equivalent sfx_id classifier (the F-158 docstring lists the exact sfx_id ranges: saw=10..13, static={32, 87}, default=all else). The stopSound is called on the allocateChannel pre-step even when the allocator would origin-match on its own — this dual-call contract preserves vanilla ordering semantics for any future port that mutates the allocator's behavior. The 45-test suite locks every parity invariant documented in the F-158 docstring; a future optimization pass touching the startSound algorithm order, the constants, the interface shapes, the link-before-adjust ordering, the same-position override, the mRandom stream choice, or the static-class no-advance must re-run this suite.

## 2026-04-22 15-007-mus-parser

- completed_step: 15-007 mus-parser
- tests_run: bun x prettier --write D:/Projects/bun-win32/doom_codex (exit 0 — formatted the new src/audio/musParser.ts and test/audio/mus-parser.test.ts inline; rest of the workspace unchanged); bun test test/audio/mus-parser.test.ts (47 pass, 0 fail, 98486 expect() calls, 145ms — green on first attempt across descriptor-mask constants, MusEventKind discriminants, synthetic per-event-type decode, variable-length VLQ delays, error cases for reserved event types / out-of-range controllers / truncated body / truncated delay, full DOOM1.WAD D_E1M1 parse with header agreement and frozen-array invariants, and parity sweep across all 13 shareware MUS lumps); bun test (5716 pass, 0 fail, 655094 expect() calls across 142 files, 2.98s — full green vs the 5669 baseline + 47 new tests in the new file matches exactly); bun x tsc --noEmit --project D:/Projects/bun-win32/doom_codex/tsconfig.json (clean, exit 0, no output — strict typecheck passes including the discriminated-union MusEvent type with channel/delay base shape, the readonly MusScore wrapper, and verbatimModuleSyntax type-only `MusHeader` import).
- results: Created `src/audio/musParser.ts` (~280 lines) implementing `parseMusScore` — a full MUS lump decoder that builds on the existing `parseMus` header parser in src/assets/mus.ts (F-053) and walks the score buffer producing a discriminated-union `MusEvent[]` stream with per-event delays in MUS quickticks. Exports: 12 numeric constants (MUS_SYSTEM_EVENT_CONTROLLER_MIN=10, MUS_SYSTEM_EVENT_CONTROLLER_MAX=14, MUS_CONTROLLER_CHANGE_MIN=0, MUS_CONTROLLER_CHANGE_MAX=9, MUS_NOTE_MAX=127, MUS_VELOCITY_MAX=127, MUS_LAST_EVENT_FLAG=0x80, MUS_EVENT_TYPE_MASK=0x70, MUS_EVENT_TYPE_SHIFT=4, MUS_CHANNEL_MASK=0x0F, MUS_NOTE_VELOCITY_FLAG=0x80, MUS_NOTE_VALUE_MASK=0x7F); 1 frozen const-object enum `MusEventKind` (ReleaseNote=0, PlayNote=1, PitchBend=2, SystemEvent=3, ControllerChange=4, ScoreEnd=6) plus a derived numeric union type alias of the same name; 6 event interfaces (MusReleaseNoteEvent, MusPlayNoteEvent with `velocity: number | null` to preserve the "reuse previous channel velocity" semantics from mus2mid.c, MusPitchBendEvent, MusSystemEvent with controller in [10, 14], MusControllerChangeEvent with controller in [0, 9], MusScoreEndEvent); 1 union type MusEvent; 1 result interface MusScore{header, events, totalDelay, bytesConsumed}; 1 public function `parseMusScore(lumpData): Readonly<MusScore>`. Algorithm: (1) delegate header parsing to `parseMus` from ../assets/mus.ts (returns header.scoreData); (2) walk the score buffer cursor-style decoding one event at a time — descriptor byte unpacks into hasDelay flag (bit 7), eventType (bits 4-6 right-shifted by MUS_EVENT_TYPE_SHIFT), and channel (bits 0-3); (3) each event type reads its body bytes via `readBodyByte` which throws RangeError on truncation; (4) play-note checks the bit-7 velocity flag on the note byte and only consumes the second byte when set, returning `velocity: null` when reusing the previous channel velocity; (5) system-event and controller-change validate their controller-number ranges and throw RangeError on values outside [10, 14] / [0, 9]; (6) reserved event types 5 and 7 throw RangeError immediately; (7) when hasDelay is set, `readVariableLengthDelay` consumes bytes accumulating `delay = delay * 128 + (byte & 0x7F)` until a byte with bit 7 clear is found (matching the MIDI VLQ encoding and the mus2mid.c reference); (8) the per-event delay is attached to the event via a frozen spread before pushing to the events array; (9) totalDelay accumulates as the running sum; (10) the loop terminates when a ScoreEnd event is decoded, and throws RangeError if the buffer is exhausted before encountering one; (11) returns a frozen MusScore wrapper with the parsed header, frozen events array, totalDelay, and bytesConsumed (cursor position at termination). Created `test/audio/mus-parser.test.ts` (~340 lines, 47 tests, 98486 expect() calls across 8 describe groups): MUS event mask constants (11 tests — every numeric constant value plus a cross-check that the three descriptor masks decompose to 0xFF without overlap); MusEventKind discriminants (2 tests — exact event-type values and frozen-enum invariant); parseMusScore on synthetic single-event scores (7 tests — release-note, play-note without velocity, play-note with velocity (note bit 7), pitch-bend, system event with controller=11, controller-change with controller=7 / value=96, percussion channel=15); variable-length delays (4 tests — 0-delay events without flag, 1-byte delay=5, multi-byte VLQ delay 0x83 0x40 = 448, totalDelay sum); error cases (8 tests — reserved type 5, reserved type 7, system-event controller<10, system-event controller>14, controller-change controller>9, missing ScoreEnd, truncated body byte, truncated delay byte); DOOM1.WAD D_E1M1 parity (8 tests — header agreement with parseMus, ScoreEnd terminator, exactly one ScoreEnd, contains play-note events, all channels in [0,15], all delays non-negative, totalDelay equals sum of event.delay, bytesConsumed <= scoreLength, frozen invariants); every shareware MUS lump (3 tests — all 13 lumps parse cleanly, all report positive totalDelay, every event channel in [0, 15]); parity-sensitive edge cases (3 tests — channel field preserved exactly as encoded, PlayNote velocity=null preserves "reuse previous channel velocity" semantics across two consecutive PlayNote events, MIDI VLQ semantics for 0x40=64, 0x81 0x00=128, and 0x81 0x80 0x00=16384). Architecture: PURE module — zero Win32 bindings, zero global mutable state, zero dependencies on the host audio device; the only state is the local cursor and accumulator within parseMusScore, and the function is referentially transparent given the same input bytes. The next steps in the music chain (15-008 scheduler, 15-009/15-010 OPL synthesis, 15-011 device integration) consume the MusEvent[] stream produced here as a deterministic, frozen artifact that the music-event-log oracle (F-038) can hash for parity.
- new_facts: F-160 (MUS score event grammar — 12 numeric constants for descriptor mask layout and validation ranges, 1 MusEventKind frozen enum with 6 valid event types and 2 reserved (5, 7) that throw, 6 event interfaces with the play-note `velocity: number | null` semantics for "reuse previous channel velocity", 1 MusEvent union, 1 MusScore wrapper, 1 parseMusScore function; variable-length delay encoding identical to MIDI VLQ; system-event controller in [10, 14] and controller-change controller in [0, 9] validated and throw on out-of-range; per-event delay attaches to the CURRENT event (the gap before the next), not the next event; score MUST terminate with an explicit ScoreEnd event or RangeError; 8 documented common porting mistakes for 17-008; consumed by 15-008 scheduler which must mirror the per-channel velocity cache the parser deliberately surfaces via velocity=null).
- next_eligible_steps: 15-008 mus-event-scheduler (first `[ ]` in phase 15 after 15-007 completion; depends on F-160 — schedules the MusEvent[] stream onto a wall-clock timeline, accumulating event.delay (MUS quickticks at 140 Hz) into MUS-tick offsets and dispatching events to the music device; the scheduler MUST track a per-channel velocity cache so that PlayNote events with `velocity: null` reuse the most recent velocity for the channel, and is responsible for any looping behavior since parseMusScore stops at the first ScoreEnd); 15-009 opl-register-model + 15-010 opl-synthesis-core + 15-011 music-device-integration (downstream consumers of the parsed event stream, mapping channel 15 → MIDI channel 9 (percussion) and applying controller events to the OPL register model — the parser's strict controller-range validation removes any need for defensive clamping at the device layer); 17-008 vanilla-quirk-regression-suite (the 8 documented common porting mistakes in F-160 should be regression-tested: variable-length delay truncation, velocity-flag mis-mask, default-velocity substitution, reserved-event-type silent-skip, out-of-range controller-clamp instead of throw, missing score-end termination, delay-attached-to-next-event off-by-one, int32 overflow on multi-byte delays); 17-010 final gate (parsed MUS event stream is in the music-event-log oracle scope (F-038) — same lump bytes across runs MUST produce identical MusEvent[] arrays for music parity).
- open_risks: The play-note `velocity: number | null` discriminant is load-bearing for parity — vanilla's mus2mid.c keeps a per-channel `channelvelocities[16]` cache that the scheduler equivalent must mirror, and the parser deliberately surfaces this via `null` rather than substituting a default velocity (e.g., 64 or 127); a port that substitutes a default at parse time would override the per-channel cache and produce flat dynamics across the score, audible as missing crescendo/decrescendo on every musical lump. The score MUST terminate with an explicit ScoreEnd event — a port that silently terminates at the buffer boundary would miss the trailing event-delay attachment and produce one-event-too-short scores; the test "throws when score data ends without a ScoreEnd event" locks this. The variable-length delay accumulation uses `value * 128 + (byte & 0x7F)` rather than `(value << 7) | (byte & 0x7F)` to extend safely past the int32 boundary in JavaScript — for delays >= ~16M the bit-shift form would overflow to negative, while the multiplication form extends naturally through Number space; the test "MIDI VLQ semantics for the documented delay encoding" locks the encoding through 16384 and the parser is correct beyond that. The system-event controller range [10, 14] and the controller-change controller range [0, 9] are STRICT — a port that clamps out-of-range values silently would corrupt the device-state for malformed MUS data; vanilla's mus2mid.c returns `false` (parse failure) on out-of-range, and parseMusScore mirrors this by throwing RangeError. The reserved event types 5 and 7 throw RangeError — a port that silently skips an unknown event type would have no way to know how many body bytes to skip and would desync the rest of the score; mus2mid.c also returns `false` on these. Per-event delay attaches to the CURRENT event (the gap BEFORE the next event), not to the next event — a port that attaches to the next event would shift every delay by one position and accumulate to the wrong total; the test "sums every event delay into totalDelay" with a 3-event score (delays 3, 7, 0) locks this ordering. The descriptor-byte unpacking uses bit-7 (`MUS_LAST_EVENT_FLAG=0x80`) for the last-event flag and bits 4-6 (`MUS_EVENT_TYPE_MASK=0x70`) for the event type — a port that reads the event type from a different bit range (e.g., bits 5-7) would silently shift every event type and produce a different mix of event kinds. The 47-test suite locks every parity invariant in the F-160 docstring; a future optimization pass touching the parseMusScore algorithm, the mask constants, the velocity-null semantics, the strict controller-range validation, the score-end termination requirement, or the per-event delay attachment must re-run this suite.

- results: Created `src/audio/pcmMixer.ts` (402 lines) composing the vanilla PCM mixer clipping-and-stepping from chocolate-doom 2.2.1 `i_sdlsound.c` `ExpandSoundData_SDL` + `I_SDL_UpdateSoundParams` + the real-time SDL*mixer callback. Exports 8 constants (PCM_BYTE_MIDPOINT=0x80 — DMX silence byte; INT16_MIN=-32768 and INT16_MAX=32767 — clipToInt16 saturation endpoints; MIX_MAX_VOLUME=127 — divisor in the (254-sep)*vol/127 / sep*vol/127 gain formulas that lets one side exceed 127 or go negative at the endpoints; SEP_LEFT_MAX=254 — the constant in the (254-sep) left-gain term; DMX_NATIVE_SAMPLE_RATE=11025 — default DMX rate; DEFAULT_OUTPUT_SAMPLE_RATE=44100 — reference SDL mixer rate; EXPAND_RATIO_SHIFT=8 and EXPAND_RATIO_SCALE=256 — 8.8 fixed-point step bits/scale); 2 interfaces (StereoGains{left, right} readonly pair — unclamped so the host mixer bridge sees vanilla endpoint asymmetry; MixerVoice{samples: Int16Array, position: number, leftGain: number, rightGain: number, finished: boolean} — one active voice); 7 public functions: `dmxByteToInt16(byte): number` via `(b | (b << 8)) - 0x8000` with RangeError on non-integer / out-of-range input preserving the 0x80 → +128 silence quirk; `clipToInt16(accumulator): number` saturates to [INT16_MIN, INT16_MAX] via Math.trunc branches, with the non-saturated branch returning `truncated | 0` to normalize -0 to +0 for Object.is semantics; `computeExpandedLength(sourceLength, sourceRate, outputRate): number` via Math.trunc((length * outputRate) / sourceRate) matching chocolate-doom's uint64 math under C-style toward-zero division; `computeExpandRatio(sourceLength, expandedLength): number` returns Math.trunc((length << 8) / expandedLength) with zero-length short-circuit; `expandDmxSamples(samples, sourceRate, outputRate): Int16Array` runs the full nearest-neighbour sample-and-hold loop with `src = (i _ ratio) >> 8`indexing and a`samples[src] ?? 0x80`fallback for defensive index safety, TypeError on non-Uint8Array input;`computeStereoGains(volume, separation): StereoGains`returns Math.trunc((254-sep)*vol/127) / Math.trunc(sep*vol/127) unclamped;`createMixerVoice(samples, volume, separation): MixerVoice`convenience constructor setting position=0 and finished=(samples.length===0);`mixVoices(voices, frameCount, output?): Int16Array`runs the real-time mixer producing`frameCount`interleaved stereo frames with signed-32-bit accumulator saturated per-frame via clipToInt16, zero-filling the output buffer on entry, advancing each voice's position by 1 per frame, and setting finished=true when position>=samples.length; throws RangeError on non-integer frameCount or output length mismatch. clipToInt16 (4 tests — pass-through in range, positive saturation above INT16_MAX, negative saturation below INT16_MIN, fractional truncation with -0 normalization to +0); computeExpandedLength (6 tests — the uint64 math, zero-length, empty, RangeError on negative/non-integer inputs); computeExpandRatio (5 tests — ratio=64 for 11025→44100 4x upsampling, ratio=128 for 22050→44100 2x DSITMBK case, zero-length short-circuit, ratio=256 for same-rate no-op, RangeError on invalid inputs); expandDmxSamples (7 tests — 4x sample-and-hold produces 4 identical outputs per source byte, DSITMBK 2x case produces 2 identical outputs, empty source produces empty output, uniform 0x80 silence produces uniform +128 output confirming the DC-offset quirk, the src=i\*ratio>>8 formula matches exact positions, the algorithm holds source byte for ratio/256 frames, TypeError on non-Uint8Array input);
